PlaceSiteIntent.cs:41-42 rejects any tile that already holds a structure. There is no path that removes a never-completed ConstructionSite or returns its Delivered materials, and combat capture changes OwnerId rather than removing structures. So a misplaced site (or one that can never reach materials/builders) blocks its tile permanently and sinks any already-hauled materials with no reclaim. Medium confirmed.

  [MEDIUM] (balance | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) Born citizens are stuck at CargoCapacity 1 and the Hauler role gives no cargo bonus â€” haul throughput dead-ends
    EVIDENCE: BirthEvent spawns children as `new Unit(childId, HouseTile){ Role=None,... }` with no CargoCapacity, so they take the default of 1 (src/Sim.Core/Population/BirthEvent.cs:45-50; Unit.CargoCapacity default 1, Unit.cs:28). CargoCapacity is init-only with no runtime setter; TrainUnitIntent only flips Role (Unit.SetRoleForTraining, Unit.cs:171), and pickup uses CargoCapacity alone with zero role multiplier (HaulPickupEvent.cs:88). UnitRole.Hauler therefore confers no mechanical advantage over any other role for hauling. Grassland move cost is 10 ticks/tile (Biome.cs:24), so a cap-1 citizen hauling wood from a camp 5 tiles away does ~100 ticks of travel per 1 wood.
    IMPACT:   Genesis can hand-spawn high-capacity haulers, but as those die of old age every replacement born in a House carries 1 unit per trip, and there is no in-game way to raise capacity (no carts/horses yet, no role bonus). Combined with the tiny buffers above, a mature economy's haul throughput collapses, and the 'Hauler' role is purely cosmetic.
    FIX:      Give UnitRole.Hauler (or training to it) a CargoCapacity multiplier the way extractor PreferredRole gives a rate bonus, and/or let births inherit a configurable starting cargo capacity. Long term this is where the deferred carts/horses (design 7.2) plug in.
    VERIFY:   Verified. Unit.CargoCapacity defaults to 1 and is init-only (Unit.cs:28); BirthEvent spawns children with no CargoCapacity (BirthEvent.cs:45-50) so they inherit the default 1. No runtime setter exists â€” TrainUnitIntent only flips Role via SetRoleForTraining (Unit.cs:171), which leaves capacity untouched. HaulPickupEvent.cs:88 computes `Math.Min(hauler.CargoCapacity, available)` with zero role multiplier, so UnitRole.Hauler confers no hauling advantage (BoatConstants.cs:11 even notes 'ground haulers (CargoCapacity defaults at 1)'). Only Genesis/WorldFactory/boats hand-set capacity >1 (grep confirms every CargoCapacity assignment is a spawn-time initializer). Carts/horses are a design-intended future capacity mechanic (design Â§7 'capacity matters', Â§272 'needed their own carts along') that is unimplemented. So as genesis haulers die of old age, replacements are stuck at cap-1 with no in-game remedy, and the Hauler role is mechanically inert for its namesake function. Medium confirmed.

  [MEDIUM] (missing-feature | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=high) Tiny output buffers + no autonomous hauling freeze the economy while the player is offline
    EVIDENCE: Buffer caps are small: LumberCamp 30, Quarry 20, Mine 20, Farm 40 (src/Sim.Core/World/StructureCatalog.cs:33,55,69,91). A 3-Lumberjack camp produces 6 wood/10 ticks (BaseRatePerWorker 1 x Lumberjack bonus 2 x 3 workers, StructureCatalog.cs:31-44) and fills its 30 buffer in 50 ticks, after which ProductionTickEvent stops rescheduling (ProductionTickEvent.cs:75-83, 101-117). Hauling is exclusively player-driven: HaulIntent is 'one submission = one trip' (HaulIntent.cs:3) and nothing in the event system auto-generates hauls â€” there is no standing-order/supply-route intent in the Intents set.
    IMPACT:   The design is explicitly async on 'geological time' with players usually offline, yet every extractor halts production roughly 50 ticks into an offline window (one full buffer) and wastes the rest of the time the player is away, because no citizen hauls on its own to relieve back-pressure. The economy effectively only runs while the player is actively micromanaging hauls â€” the opposite of fair-while-asleep.
    FIX:      Add standing haul orders / supply routes (assign a hauler or House to repeatedly drain a buffer to a stockpile) and/or substantially larger buffer banks so offline production accrues. This is the single biggest economy/async-design gap.
    VERIFY:   Mechanical facts verified: buffer caps are LumberCamp 30 / Quarry 20 / Mine 20 / Farm 40 (StructureCatalog.cs:33,54,72,92); a 3-Lumberjack camp makes 6 wood/period (BaseRate 1 x bonus 2/1 x 3) every 10 ticks and fills 30 in 50 ticks, after which ProductionTickEvent.cs:75-83 goes dormant; hauling is one-trip player-driven (HaulIntent.cs:3) with no auto-haul event. BUT severity is overstated and the framing is wrong: (1) back-pressure halting at a full buffer is intentional design (prevents unbounded accumulation), not a bug; (2) the design doc does NOT promise autonomous hauling â€” it explicitly defers it as an OPEN QUESTION: Â§12 'Action queuing is essential for fairness... players plan ahead and log off' and Â§13.4 'Anti-whale / fair while offline meta... Needs an explicit action-queuing design and possibly catch-up mechanics.' So this is an acknowledged, not-yet-built design area, not a code-breaks-design contradiction. Legitimate missing-feature observation, but high is too strong; medium.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=low) HaulIntent doesn't reject Source==Dest or an Extractor destination â€” cargo gets stranded
    EVIDENCE: HaulIntent.Resolve validates source has stock and dest has a structure but never checks SourceTile != DestTile, and never checks the dest can actually accept a deposit (src/Sim.Core/Logistics/HaulIntent.cs:47-60). HaulDepositEvent only deposits into StorageStructure or ConstructionSite (`dest switch { StorageStructure..., ConstructionSite..., _ => 0 }`, HaulDepositEvent.cs:83-88), so hauling to an Extractor returns 0 deposited. With Source==Dest on an Extractor, the pickup drains the buffer (HaulPickupEvent.cs:104-108) and the deposit returns 0.
    IMPACT:   In both cases the picked-up resource ends up stranded as cargo on an Idle hauler, which â€” per the cargo-overwrite finding â€” is then destroyed on the unit's next haul. Pure waste, but easy to trigger by mistargeting.
    FIX:      Reject SourceTile == DestTile at submission, and reject DestTile structures that can't accept the resource (non-storage / non-matching construction site) so the trip never runs.
    VERIFY:   Verified. HaulIntent.Resolve (HaulIntent.cs:47-60) validates source has stock and dest has a structure but never checks SourceTile!=DestTile and never checks the dest can accept a deposit. HaulDepositEvent.cs:83-88 deposits only into StorageStructure or ConstructionSite (`_ => 0`), so an Extractor destination returns 0 deposited. With Source==Dest on an Extractor, HaulPickupEvent.cs:104-108 drains the buffer and the same-tile deposit returns 0, stranding the resource as cargo on an Idle hauler â€” which is then destroyed on the next haul per the cargo-overwrite finding. Easy to trigger by mistargeting; low confirmed. (Note: Source==Dest on a StorageStructure is harmless â€” it withdraws then re-deposits the same amount; only the Extractor-dest cases leak.)

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=low) BuildCompleteEvent never re-checks biome â€” a degraded tile can finish a dead-on-arrival extractor
    EVIDENCE: PlaceSiteIntent validates the derived biome at placement (src/Sim.Core/Logistics/PlaceSiteIntent.cs:44-55), but BuildCompleteEvent only re-checks ConditionsMet = materials + builders (src/Sim.Core/Logistics/BuildCompleteEvent.cs:39; ConstructionSite.ConditionsMet, Structure.cs:279-280) â€” no biome re-validation before constructing the Extractor (BuildCompleteEvent.cs:60). DegradeRadius is 2 (Chebyshev 5x5; src/Sim.Core/Biomes/BiomeDegradationConfig.cs:76), so a neighboring producing LumberCamp/Farm can degrade the site's tile out of its required biome (e.g. Forest->Grassland) before the build finishes.
    IMPACT:   The completed Extractor then immediately fails ProductionTickEvent's biome guard and goes dormant forever (ProductionTickEvent.cs:46-61), wasting the build cost and a tile. Niche (requires two extractors close together) but reachable and silent.
    FIX:      Re-validate the target's RequiredBiome against BiomeAt(now) inside BuildCompleteEvent (and/or ConditionsMet); on mismatch, fail-clean the completion so the site stays paused rather than producing a dead structure.
    VERIFY:   Verified. PlaceSiteIntent.cs:44-55 validates the derived biome at placement, but BuildCompleteEvent.cs:39 only re-checks site.ConditionsMet (materials + builders) before constructing the Extractor at :60 â€” no biome re-validation. DegradeRadius is 2 (BiomeDegradationConfig.cs:76, Chebyshev), DegradeAmount 1 per DegradePeriod 100 ticks, and build durations are short (LumberCamp 40, Farm 30), so a neighboring producing LumberCamp/Farm can degrade the site's tile across a biome band mid-build only when the tile is already ~1 fertility from the boundary and a degrade tick lands in the window â€” genuinely niche but reachable. The finished extractor then trips ProductionTickEvent.cs:46-61's biome guard on its first tick and goes dormant, wasting the build cost and tile silently. Low is appropriate.

---------------------------------------------------------------------

##### Population, Breeding, Training, Aging  [key=population-breeding]
SUMMARY: The M8/M13 population layer is architecturally excellent: age is a pure derivation from BornTick (no per-unit tick), lifespan is rolled once inside the sim's owned construction/event stream at exactly two grep-checkable sites, variable lifespans smear cohort cliffs, and a single OnUnitRemoved rule decouples combat/aging from breeding via one signal â€” all backed by strong snapshot/regen tests. The weaknesses are at the balance/design seam, not the engine: the per-birth food cost is decorative (the real throttles are the adult-lock and the finite-Grassland food wall), there is no offline auto-breeding despite an async "fair-while-asleep" premise that the demographic loop structurally requires, roles confer no combat value so the doc's "future army" framing is hollow, and BeginBreedingIntent omits the group/embark guards every sibling intent enforces.
STRENGTHS:
  + Age as a pure derivation from BornTick (no per-unit clock) :: Population.AgeYears/CanTrain/CanBreed (Population.cs:17-31) read state and never mutate; Unit has no Age field (reflection-pinned by PopulationAgeTests.Unit_HasNoMutableAgeField). This matches the fog/road precedent, eliminates a per-tick global sweep in an idle-heavy async sim, and is structurally impossible to desync because there is no per-unit age state to diverge.
  + Lifespan rolled once, inside the sim's owned construction and event stream, at exactly two grep-checkable sites :: ScheduleLifespan (Population.cs:43-59) is idempotent and called only from the spec-aware Simulation ctor (canonical id order, Simulation.cs:41-44) and BirthEvent.Apply (BirthEvent.cs:51). No post-hoc sweep that could consume RNG out of order or be forgotten on a new code path â€” a genuinely strong determinism discipline, validated by Twin_LifespanScenario_HashesMatch.
  + Variable lifespan smears cohort cliffs for free :: Uniform roll over [LifespanMin,Max] (Population.cs:48-49) means a panic-bred generation does not become fertile, post-fertile, and die in synchronized waves. LifespansVary_NoSyncedCliff pins it. Emergent boom/bust demography with one extra RNG draw and zero extra code.
  + One stop-on-removal rule decouples combat/aging from breeding :: Population.OnUnitRemoved (Population.cs:110-148) is the single place breeding cleanup lives; combat (CombatRules.OnUnitDeath) and aging (DeathByAgeEvent) both route through it and never name Breeding. Every future death pathway (starvation, drowning) gets correct breeding cleanup for free, and the BirthEvent fences via anchor mismatch (BirthEvent.cs:26-38). Clean, extensible cross-feature seam.
  + Fencing-token persistence for in-flight births and deaths :: (BirthTick,BirthSeq) on the House and (DeathTick,DeathSeq) on the Unit let RegenerateQueue rebuild queued BirthEvents/DeathByAgeEvents at their original Seq on snapshot restore (RegenerateQueue.cs:71-92), so a gestation or a scheduled death survives a crash deterministically. The CRUX tests (MidGestation_SnapshotRoundTrip_BirthFiresAtSameTick, MidLife_SnapshotRoundTrip_DeathFiresAtSameTick) prove it bit-for-bit.
FINDINGS (kept=8, refuted/dropped=0):

  [MEDIUM] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=medium) BeginBreedingIntent omits the GroupId/IsEmbarked guards every sibling intent enforces â€” group movement can bypass the breeding move-lock
    EVIDENCE: BeginBreedingIntent.cs:49-62 validates owner/presence/Idle/fertility but never checks unit.GroupId or unit.IsEmbarked. Every sibling intent does: MoveIntent.cs:19,26 (GroupId, IsEmbarked), FormGroupIntent.cs:48,50, EmbarkIntent.cs:70-72, TrainUnitIntent.cs:41,43. A unit at a group's rendezvous tile stays Activity.Idle (FormGroupIntent.cs sets GroupId but does not change activity for already-present members), so a grouped, idle, fertile unit standing on a House tile passes all BeginBreeding checks and becomes a Working, move-locked parent. GroupArrivalEvent.cs:57-60 then overwrites unit.Position for every member with no activity/lock check, while the House.Occupation still names the relocated parent and the BirthEvent stays queued.
    IMPACT:   BreedingMoveLockTests proves the SOLO MoveIntent path refuses to move a breeding parent â€” that invariant ('a parent is locked to the house until BirthEvent', House.cs:13-15) is the documented contract. But the GROUP move path has no such guard, so a group move drags a move-locked parent away from its house; BirthEvent later fires at the now-empty house tile, spawning the child where neither parent is and Idling parents that are elsewhere. Same class of inconsistency for an embarked parent (boat sails off with a 'breeding' passenger). It is a reachable invariant violation purely from legal intent sequences.
    FIX:      Add `if (a.GroupId is not null || b.GroupId is not null) reject;` and `if (a.IsEmbarked || b.IsEmbarked) reject;` to BeginBreedingIntent.Resolve, mirroring the sibling intents. core-touching (Sim.Core/Population).
    VERIFY:   Group-move bypass confirmed as a reachable invariant violation. BeginBreedingIntent.cs:49-71 omits the GroupId guard that MoveIntent.cs:19, FormGroupIntent.cs:48, EmbarkIntent.cs:70, TrainUnitIntent.cs:41 all enforce. Reachable sequence: FormGroup with the two parents at a House tile (already present -> pending 0 -> group State=Idle, members stay Activity.Idle), BeginBreeding (passes - on tile, Idle, fertile, food), parents go Working with Occupation+BirthEvent queued, then MoveGroupIntent (only blocks Forming groups). GroupArrivalEvent.cs:56-64 overwrites every member's Position with NO activity/lock check, dragging the move-locked Working parents away; BirthEvent.cs:45-61 later fires at the now-parent-less House, spawning the child where neither parent is. This bypasses the documented 'parent locked to house until BirthEvent' invariant (House.cs:7-15) that BreedingMoveLockTests pins only for the SOLO MoveIntent path (MoveIntent.cs:33). The EMBARK half of the finding, however, is already mitigated/moot: EmbarkIntent.cs:72 rejects breeding parents, and an embarked unit cannot start breeding because its Position stays the Dock tile (EmbarkIntent.cs:74) and one tile holds one structure, so BeginBreedingIntent.cs:55's House-tile check fails - no IsEmbarked guard is needed there. Net: real group-path logic hole at medium; the embark concern is non-reachable.

  [MEDIUM] (balance | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) BirthFoodCost is decorative; breeding's only real per-child cost is the adult-lock, enabling explosive growth where food is cheap
    EVIDENCE: BirthFoodCost=20, drawn once from the House (BeginBreedingIntent.cs:64,74; PopulationConfig.cs:39). Consumption is 1 food/citizen per 60-tick period (FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:21-22) = 250/60 â‰ˆ 4.17 food/citizen/year. One maxed Farm = 3 workers Ã— BaseRatePerWorker 2 Ã— Farmer role bonus 2/1 = 12 food per 10 ticks = 1.2 food/tick = 300 food/year (StructureCatalog.cs:83-96; ProductionTickEvent.cs:92). So BirthFoodCost 20 â‰ˆ 6.7% of one farm-year and â‰ˆ 4.8 citizen-years of food â€” trivial. With fertility window 18-45 (27 years) and gestation 1.2 years, a single locked pair can birth ~22 children over its life, and ~15 before its first child is even fertile (4500-tick maturation / 300-tick gestation).
    IMPACT:   The design intends 'no steady state' with gestation as the throttle, which is fine. But the intended food brake (M13 consumption) is set so low that the per-birth cost provides no meaningful resistance â€” the only genuine costs are (a) two adults locked off the economy for 300 ticks and (b) the aggregate finite-Grassland food wall (Farm permanently deserts Grassland after ~260 ticks). Population therefore grows explosively whenever a player has spare houses and any food surplus, until it slams into the food wall and famine-collapses. The throttle the player feels is binary (plenty vs starvation), not graduated.
    FIX:      Either raise/scale BirthFoodCost so it is a visible fraction of a citizen's lifetime upkeep (e.g. tens of percent), or explicitly accept that the finite-Grassland aggregate is the brake and document that the birth cost is just a down-payment. Changing the PopulationConfig default is config, not logic, but it is a Sim.Core default (core-touching).
    VERIFY:   Numbers verified exactly. BirthFoodCost=20 drawn once (BeginBreedingIntent.cs:64,74; PopulationConfig.cs:39/30). Consumption 1 food/citizen/60t (FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:21-22) = 250/60 = 4.17/citizen/yr. Maxed Farm = 3 workers x BaseRatePerWorker 2 x Farmer bonus 2/1 = 12 food/10t = 300 food/yr (StructureCatalog.cs:89-95; ProductionTickEvent.cs:92-93), so 20 food = 6.7% of a farm-year and ~4.8 citizen-years - one farm feeds ~72 citizens. Grassland goes permanently Desert after ~260t (StructureCatalog.cs:99-108, confirmed). Fertility window 18-45 (27y) / gestation 300t (1.2y) ~= 22 children/pair, ~15 before the first child reaches 18 (4500t/300t). The narrow claim - BirthFoodCost is decorative and the M13 food brake is too weak to graduate the throttle - is accurate. Note (as the finding does) that two real throttles remain: the 300-tick adult-lock (two adults off-economy per child) and Farm BufferCap=40 + haul-out requirement; 'explosive growth' is contingent on spare houses + food surplus. Confirmed at medium.

  [MEDIUM] (missing-feature | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=high) No offline auto-breeding: an asleep player's civilization monotonically ages out and dies, contradicting the async premise
    EVIDENCE: Breeding is the ONLY post-genesis unit source (Population.cs: units are created only by BirthEvent.Apply and the genesis ctor; boats are vehicles excluded from population, GameWorld.cs:148). Each birth requires an explicit BeginBreedingIntent and there is no rebreed/maintenance automation â€” population-model.md:163-165 lists 'Automation (auto-rebreed, keep my population stable)' as unbuilt 'Future expansion.' Meanwhile every unit has a hard DeathByAgeEvent: default lifespan 50-80 years at TicksPerYear=250 (PopulationConfig.cs:35-42), so a genesis adult (StartingAgeYears 30, Genesis.cs:54) dies within (80-30)=50y..(50-30)=20y = 5000-12500 ticks. Gestation is 300 ticks and parents do NOT auto-rebreed (BirthEvent.cs:56-61 just sets them Idle). A player who issues one breeding cycle and logs off gets at most one child per pre-loaded house, while all adults keep aging toward death.
    IMPACT:   The whole game is built on 'geological time / players usually offline / fair-while-asleep.' But the population loop is the one system that requires the player to be awake every ~1.2 years to keep issuing breeding intents. An offline player returns to a shrunken, aged population; a population with no fertile members left (all 45+, or only sub-18 children with no surviving adults to re-breed once they mature) trends to unavoidable extinction with no input. This lets an attacker grind a sleeping civilization down with no possible defense â€” the exact failure mode the design's async rules exist to prevent.
    FIX:      Build the server-side 'keep my population stable' / auto-rebreed policy the doc already scopes (host-side convenience layered on BeginBreedingIntent â€” NOT core-touching). At minimum, a standing policy that re-pairs idle fertile adults at owned vacant houses when food is available. Consider this a prerequisite for the async premise to hold, not optional polish.
    VERIFY:   Mechanics fully confirmed: breeding (BirthEvent.Apply -> Population.OnUnitAdded -> AddUnit) and the genesis ctor are the ONLY citizen-spawn paths (BoatProductionTickEvent spawns boats, excluded at GameWorld.cs:148; Sim.Host.Program.cs:244-245 is dev scaffold). DeathByAgeEvent is automatic and unconditional; PopulationConfig.cs:35-42 gives lifespan 50-80y at TicksPerYear 250, so a StartingAge-30 genesis adult (Genesis.cs:54) dies in 5000-12500 ticks. BirthEvent.cs:56-59 idles parents with no rebreed; population-model.md:162-163 lists auto-rebreed as unbuilt 'Future expansion.' The structural asymmetry (death automatic/continuous, breeding manual/presence-gated) is real and worth flagging. BUT severity is overstated to high: (1) 'no possible defense' is wrong - war is telegraphed with a declare-delay + target notification (design ss11-12), giving the asleep player a reaction window to log in and rebreed; (2) population-model.md:5-8 states 'no steady state by design ... breeding adds ... the gap is the strategic metabolism' - active population management is intentional, not a contradiction; (3) the absolute decay rate depends on an undetermined tick->wall-clock mapping (FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:9 only assumes 1 tick~1min); (4) the fix is explicitly roadmapped (population-model.md:162-163, design ss13.4 open question 'fair while offline'). Real gap, medium.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=low) Doc states fertility window 18-40 but the shipping default MaxFertileAge is 45
    EVIDENCE: population-model.md:22 and the PopulationConfig comment region describe 'Fertility window (18 â‰¤ age â‰¤ 40)', and most tests use MaxFertileAge:40, but the shipped default is MaxFertileAge:45 (PopulationConfig.cs:38). MinTrainAge (15) and MinFertileAge (18) match between doc and code.
    IMPACT:   Harmless today, but the spec doc and the live default disagree on a tuning constant that directly sizes the fertile window (27 vs 22 years), so anyone reasoning about demographics from the doc gets the wrong number. Minor, but it is the kind of drift that misleads balance work.
    FIX:      Pick one value and align population-model.md with PopulationConfig's default (or vice-versa). Doc/config only â€” not logic.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed. population-model.md:21 states 'Fertility window (18 <= age <= 40)'; the shipped default is MaxFertileAge:45 (PopulationConfig.cs:38). MinTrainAge 15 and MinFertileAge 18 agree between doc and code (PopulationConfig.cs:36-37). The drift is corroborated by the test fixtures using 40 (e.g. BreedingMoveLockTests.cs:23 MaxFertileAge:40), so the live default (45) disagrees with both the doc and the tests, sizing the fertile window at 27y instead of the documented 22y. Harmless at runtime but misleads anyone reasoning about demographics from the doc. Low, as stated.

  [LOW] (unnecessary | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=low) TrainUnitIntent's GetActiveBreedingFor check is dead code â€” the Idle precondition already excludes breeding parents
    EVIDENCE: TrainUnitIntent.cs:45 rejects any unit whose Activity != Idle. A breeding parent is always Activity.Working (BeginBreedingIntent.cs:75-76 sets Working; only BirthEvent/stop-on-removal returns them to Idle). The subsequent GetActiveBreedingFor scan at TrainUnitIntent.cs:47-48 can therefore never fire â€” it runs a full sweep over world.Structures for a condition the prior line already guarantees false.
    IMPACT:   Not a correctness bug, but it is a per-call structure sweep that is provably unreachable, plus a maintenance trap (it implies the two checks are independent when they are not). Quality-over-quantity: minor.
    FIX:      Drop the GetActiveBreedingFor call from TrainUnitIntent (the Idle check covers it), or add a comment that it is intentionally defensive. core-touching if removed.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed unreachable. TrainUnitIntent.cs:45 rejects any unit with Activity != Idle, and a breeding parent is always Activity.Working: BeginBreedingIntent.cs:75-76 sets Working, and the only paths back to Idle (BirthEvent.cs:56-61 and Population.OnUnitRemoved at Population.cs:142) both clear house.Occupation in the same step, so no reachable state has a unit that is simultaneously Idle and named by a live Occupation. I traced every Idle-setting path (MoveIntent rejects breeders before idling at MoveIntent.cs:33; EmbarkIntent rejects at :72; GroupArrivalEvent only sets Position, not Activity). Therefore the GetActiveBreedingFor scan at TrainUnitIntent.cs:47-48 can never be the rejection cause - it runs a structures sweep for a condition line 45 already guarantees false. Caveat: it's cheap (Houses are few, per Population.cs:133 comment) and mirrors the defensive pattern in MoveIntent, so it's arguably intentional layering rather than a defect; removing it is optional. The finding's factual claim (provably unreachable) holds. Low.

  [LOW] (unnecessary | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=low) The Hauler role confers no mechanical benefit â€” a dead role-flip
    EVIDENCE: CargoCapacity is a per-unit init field defaulting to 1 (Unit.cs:28), set from UnitSpawn (Genesis.cs:110-115), never derived from Role. HaulIntent only requires CargoCapacity > 0 (HaulIntent.cs:43) â€” any unit, including a role-less child, hauls identically (confirmed by PopulationTrainingTests.Child_CanMoveAndHaul). No extractor lists PreferredRole=Hauler (StructureCatalog.cs), and combat is role-uniform. Design Â§7/Â§5 implies haulers have meaningful capacity.
    IMPACT:   Training a unit to Hauler changes nothing observable: same carry capacity, same combat, no extraction bonus. It is a selectable role that is a no-op, which both wastes the player's attention and contradicts the Â§7 'capacity matters' framing for porters.
    FIX:      Either derive CargoCapacity from Role (Hauler gets a capacity multiplier) so the role pulls its weight, or remove Hauler from the trainable set until it does. core-touching.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed via a full grep of Sim.Core: UnitRole.Hauler appears ONLY in the enum (Unit.cs:12) and as a uniform 10/1 row in UnitCombatCatalog.cs:30; 'HaulerId' elsewhere is just a parameter name, not role-gated. CargoCapacity is a per-unit init field defaulting to 1 (Unit.cs:28), set from UnitSpawn (Genesis.cs:108-115), never derived from Role. HaulIntent.cs:43 only requires CargoCapacity > 0, so any unit - including a role-less child - hauls identically. No extractor sets PreferredRole=Hauler (StructureCatalog.cs:34,55,72,93 are Lumberjack/Quarryman/Miner/Farmer only), and combat is role-uniform. Training to Hauler therefore changes nothing observable, while design ss5:179 ('capacity matters; see ss7') implies haulers should differ. A genuine no-op role. Low.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=medium) All roles share identical combat stats and no military role exists, so the doc's 'future army' / 'incoming specialists' framing has no mechanical backing
    EVIDENCE: UnitCombatCatalog.cs:24-31 gives every citizen role BaseHealth=10/BasePower=1 (only Boat differs). The UnitRole enum (Unit.cs:4-15) has no Soldier/military role, yet design Â§5 (persistent-rts-design.md:180) explicitly lists 'Soldier â€” fights; escorts caravans.' population-model.md:116-121 sells the training gate as making a population center 'a future army the raider can destroy' that 'denies the player... 15 years of incoming specialists.'
    IMPACT:   Because a trained specialist fights exactly as well as a role-less child, killing a household's children denies economic value but no military value â€” the 'future army' strategic texture the population doc leans on does not exist in code. Combat outcomes depend only on headcount and Health, so the demographic investment loop the doc frames around 'specialists' is, today, just a labor/economy loop. This is a design-promise-vs-code gap (acknowledged as future work in the catalog comment, but oversold in the shipped population doc and the design's role list).
    FIX:      Add combat-differentiated/military rows to UnitCombatCatalog (and a trainable Soldier role) so training feeds a real army, or temper the population-model.md 'future army' language until it does. core-touching (catalog + enum).
    VERIFY:   Factual core confirmed: UnitCombatCatalog.cs:24-31 gives every citizen role BaseHealth 10/BasePower 1 (only Boat differs at 40/0); the UnitRole enum (Unit.cs:4-15) has no Soldier/military role; design ss5:180 lists 'Soldier - fights; escorts caravans.' So a trained specialist fights identically to a role-less child. BUT the conclusion is overstated: (1) UnitCombatCatalog.cs:10-12 explicitly flags 'Trainable combat units (Soldier, Archer, Knight) land later as new rows' - this is openly-acknowledged future work, not a hidden contradiction (category 'logic-hole' is too strong; it's a known missing feature); (2) the 'future army the raider can destroy' framing is NOT mechanically hollow - combat is headcount+Health driven (the finding itself says so), so each future child becomes a future combat body (10 HP/1 power), meaning killing a household's kids DOES deny future military mass, contradicting the finding's 'denies economic value but no military value.' What's genuinely missing is role-based combat DIFFERENTIATION, not army value per se. Also note roles are not uniformly inert: Scout gives vision 6 vs 3 (Sight.cs:17-20), Builder gates construction (AssignBuildersIntent.cs:42), PreferredRole doubles extraction (ProductionTickEvent.cs:92-93). Real doc/promise gap, but low and self-acknowledged.

  [LOW] (balance | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=low) Training is instant, free, and infinitely reversible â€” the one transformation in a 'time + distance' game with no time or material cost
    EVIDENCE: TrainUnitIntent.cs:69-73 flips Role and returns Applied in the same tick â€” no duration, no resource cost, no cooldown. TrainUnit_FreeRetrain_AllowsBuilderToFarmer (TrainUnitTests.cs:48-55) pins that retraining is unlimited. The only friction is being Idle on an owned School tile (one-time 80-wood build, StructureCatalog.cs:144-151). Every other state change in the sim is time-gated: movement, construction (BuildDurationTicks), gestation (300), production periods, even old age.
    IMPACT:   The design calls roles 'the main character-progression lever' (Â§5), but with zero per-train cost or time and free reversibility, role choice has near-zero stakes â€” a player perfectly reallocates labor at will (walk to school, flip). That undercuts roles as progression and is thematically off-key for a game whose whole identity is that nothing is instant and everything is hauled/earned over hours.
    FIX:      Give TrainUnitIntent a training DURATION (schedule a TrainCompleteEvent, mirroring gestation/construction) and/or a small per-train resource cost, so role specialization is an investment rather than a toggle. core-touching.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed. TrainUnitIntent.cs:70-73 calls SetRoleForTraining and returns Applied in the same tick - no duration, no resource cost, no cooldown, and reversible (the design comment at line 19 even calls Role 'the entire payload'). The only friction is being Idle on an owned School tile (TrainUnitIntent.cs:45,61-66), a one-time 80-wood build (StructureCatalog.cs:144-151). Every other state transition in the sim is time-gated: movement (per-hop ExecutionCost), construction (BuildDurationTicks 30-200), gestation (300), production periods (10-15), old age. The finding's own cited test TrainUnit_FreeRetrain_AllowsBuilderToFarmer pins unlimited retrain. Thematically off-key for a 'nothing is instant' game and undercuts roles-as-progression (design ss5:182). The finding rates it low and that's right - it's a design-feel/altitude note, not a correctness bug.

---------------------------------------------------------------------

##### Food, Consumption, Famine, Starvation  [key=food-famine]
SUMMARY: The food subsystem is engineering-clean â€” the M9 lazy-catch-up math is observation-independent and integer-exact, both scheduled events fence on (tick,seq) anchors and are regenerated on restore, and the castle-only sink correctly keeps food physical. The weaknesses are in BALANCE and one real LOGIC HOLE. The starvation death-clock fully resets on any positive deposit and re-arms the full 1440-tick delay, so trickle-feeding (literally 1 food per ~1500 ticks for any empire size) prevents all deaths â€” the food consequence is binary, not proportional. Separately the numbers make food a trivial standing constraint: one farm feeds 72 mouths, a full castle buffers ~1200 citizen-years, and the fixed 60-tick death interval makes large empires nearly immune to famine. At the opposite extreme the server seeds only 40 food for 14 units, so a fresh game enters famine at tick 180.
STRENGTHS:
  + Observation-independent lazy catch-up is genuinely correct :: FoodConsumption.CatchUp advances LastFoodConsumedTick by completed periods with remainder carry, computes the famine failure-boundary deterministically, and is anchored at every rate-changing event (Population.OnUnitAdded/OnUnitRemoved catch up at the OLD rate before mutating pop â€” Population.cs:77-129; HaulDeposit catches up before depositing â€” HaulDepositEvent.cs:79-81). CatchUp_IsObservationIndependent and CurrentLevel_IsPureRead_NoMutation (100x no-mutation hash pin) lock the M9 contract. The math is integer-exact with no float/remainder leakage.
  + Both scheduled events fence cleanly and survive snapshot/restore :: FamineCheckEvent and StarvationDeathEvent both fence on (At,Seq) against per-castle anchors (FamineCheckEvent.cs:29-42, StarvationDeathEvent.cs:38-57) plus a FamineStartTick!=null guard, so stale events from population shifts/deposits no-op. RegenerateQueue.cs:109-129 regenerates BOTH events at their original (tick,seq) on restore, and Recovery_MidFamine_*_Identical proves mid-famine snapshot/restore hashes match an uninterrupted run.
  + Staggered, oldest-first, long-delayed deaths satisfy async-fairness :: First death only at FamineStartTick + 1440t, then one per 60t in deterministic ascending (BornTick, Id) order (StarvationDeathEvent.cs:90-107, FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:28-29). No population cliff, no RNG, fully telegraphed â€” a player who logs in during a famine always has time and a visible decline to react to, exactly matching the design's 'no catastrophic dice the player can't react to' principle.
  + Castle-only sink keeps food physical :: Consumption drains only Castle.Holdings[Food] and food only arrives via real HaulIntent/HaulDepositEvent (no stockpile virtualization, no auto-haul). This preserves the logistics spine â€” raids on supply lines bite, roads matter for food, and you genuinely can starve with full stockpiles 100 tiles away. Single-mutation discipline on PopulationCount (Player.cs:19-27, audited by PopulationCount_HasOneMutationPoint) keeps the rate input auditable.
FINDINGS (kept=7, refuted/dropped=1):

  [HIGH] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) Any positive food deposit fully clears famine and re-arms the entire StarvationStartDelay, so sub-subsistence trickle-feeding prevents all deaths
    EVIDENCE: HaulDepositEvent.cs:97-108 clears FamineStartTick and calls ClearStarvationDeathAnchor whenever a Food deposit leaves Holdings[Food] > 0 â€” the threshold is `> 0`, i.e. a single unit. When the larder next dries out, FoodConsumption.CatchUp re-enters famine and schedules the FIRST death at `failureBoundary + StarvationStartDelay` (FoodConsumption.cs:94-106), a fresh 1440 ticks (FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:28). There is no accumulated-deficit memory: each famine cycle starts the death countdown from scratch. Net effect: after any deposit, food drains in ~1 period (60t) then a death is scheduled +1440t later, so depositing 1 food roughly every 1500 ticks keeps a population of ANY size alive forever, while supplying 1 food/period to a pop that needs `pop` food/period.
    IMPACT:   The system measures 'was the larder momentarily at exactly zero for 1440 continuous ticks', not 'is the population's caloric need being met'. A player who feeds far below subsistence never loses a citizen as long as hauls keep landing periodically. The design's core promise ('if your supply line breaks, your civ shrinks', food-consumption.md:59-76) only bites under a total, sustained 1440-tick cutoff â€” partial starvation has zero consequence. This guts the food sink as an economic pressure and hands players a degenerate 'feed a trickle' strategy.
    FIX:      Core-touching (Sim.Core/Food + HaulDepositEvent). Make starvation cumulative/proportional rather than binary-reset: e.g. carry an accumulated-deficit counter that deposits reduce but do not zero, OR on famine re-trigger do not reset the full StarvationStartDelay (resume from remaining delay), OR drive deaths from a running food-debt rather than a clean larder==0 latch. Minimum stop-gap: don't clear FamineStartTick unless the deposit covers at least one period's full rate, and preserve elapsed famine time across re-feeds.
    VERIFY:   Code reads exactly as claimed. HaulDepositEvent.Apply (HaulDepositEvent.cs:97-108) clears FamineStartTick and calls ClearStarvationDeathAnchor whenever a Food deposit leaves Holdings[Food] > 0 (literal `> 0` threshold, line 100), then OnRateOrFoodChanged reschedules a fresh FamineCheckEvent. When food re-dries, FoodConsumption.CatchUp re-enters famine and schedules the first death at failureBoundary + StarvationStartDelay (FoodConsumption.cs:105-106), a full 60*24=1440 ticks (FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:28). There is NO accumulated-deficit memory: during famine, ConsumptionUpTo/CatchUp consume 0 (food is already 0, FoodConsumption.cs:65-69,168), so the unmet demand of the famine window is simply forgotten, and citizens keep working at full productivity (the design chose death-only, no productivity/breeding penalty). I searched the test suite â€” no test exercises sustained underfeeding; HaulDeposit_DuringFamine_ClearsFamineAndReschedules and StarvationDeath_FencesWhenFamineEnds only cover a single deposit, so nothing guards this. The cost asymmetry is real and large: 1 food per ~1500t versus the ~pop*25 food/1500t actual need. The only caveat is that the binary-larder trigger is itself a deliberate design choice (food-consumption.md:101-122), but the design's STATED promise 'if your supply line breaks, your civ shrinks' (food-consumption.md:71-72) is genuinely defeated by trickle-feeding. Confirmed at high.

  [MEDIUM] (balance | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) Server seeds 40 food for 14 starting units (famine at tick 180); second faction gets 0 food and its lone scout starves at tick 1500
    EVIDENCE: WorldFactory.cs:51-66 spawns 2 of each of 7 roles = 14 units; CastleHoldings Food = 40 (WorldFactory.cs:82). rate = 14/period, fullMeals = 40/14 = 2, so FoodConsumption.OnRateOrFoodChanged schedules famine onset at (2+1)Ã—60 = tick 180 (~0.72 years) and the first death at 180+1440 = 1620. The in-code comment (WorldFactory.cs:75-77) claims the 40 food 'covers the M13 consumption drain until a farm is up', but it covers only ~2 consumption periods. The optional second faction (WorldFactory.cs:91-97) is seeded Wood only (no Food) with a single Scout, so it famines at tick 60 and its only unit starves at tick 1500 with no intervention, deleting the 'other' that fog/combat depend on.
    IMPACT:   Onset of famine 180 ticks into a fresh, async game contradicts the geological-time/fair-while-asleep principle: a new player who places pieces and logs off can return to a famine-flagged castle. It is not catastrophic (deposit any food resets it, and first death is 1620t out), but the buffer is far thinner than the comment implies. The neutral faction self-destructing at tick 1500 quietly removes the intended sparring partner.
    FIX:      Not core (server WorldFactory). Seed starting food proportional to starting pop (e.g. ~20 food/unit â‰ˆ 280, giving ~20 periods before onset) and give any non-trivial second faction enough food to survive bootstrapping, or exclude zero-pop-after-starvation factions from the fog/combat-partner role.
    VERIFY:   All cited numbers verified. WorldFactory.cs:51-66 spawns 2 of each of 7 roles = 14 units; CastleHoldings Food=40 (WorldFactory.cs:82). fullMeals = 40/14 = 2, so OnRateOrFoodChanged schedules famine at (2+1)*60 = tick 180 and first death at 180+1440 = 1620. Second faction (WorldFactory.cs:91-97): Wood=20, NO Food, one Scout (pop=1); genesis schedules a FamineCheck at (0+1)*60 = 60 (cf. test EmptyFoodAtStart_FamineSetByFirstCheckEvent), famine sets, scout starves at 60+1440 = 1500 with no intervention â€” its castle then has pop=0, quietly removing the sparring partner's only mobile unit. The comment (WorldFactory.cs:75-77) does overclaim ('covers the M13 consumption drain until a farm is up') given only ~2 full meal-periods of cover. The one overstated part is the 'contradicts fair-while-asleep' framing: famine only sets a recoverable flag (any deposit clears it) and the first death is 1620t out (~27 hours at the ~1-tick=1-min comment cadence), a fairly generous reaction window. So the facts are exact; the concrete real issues are the thin/over-claimed buffer and the neutral faction's guaranteed self-destruct. Confirmed at medium.

  [MEDIUM] (balance | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) Starvation kills a flat 1 citizen per 60 ticks regardless of population or deficit â€” big empires are nearly immune
    EVIDENCE: StarvationDeathEvent reschedules unconditionally at `now + StarvationDeathInterval` = +60 ticks (StarvationDeathEvent.cs:82-83, FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:29), independent of PopulationCount or how badly underfed the civ is. Full-wipe time = 1440 + (pop-1)Ã—60 ticks. A 100-pop empire under TOTAL famine loses only ~1 citizen per 60t (~4/year at 250 t/yr) and takes 6000t (~24 years) to wipe; a 3-pop empire wipes in ~180t after the delay.
    IMPACT:   Per-capita starvation pressure shrinks as the empire grows, so a large civilization barely feels a famine while a tiny one is gutted. Combined with breeding drawing food from Houses (not the castle, BeginBreedingIntent.cs:64-74), a big empire can out-breed starvation deaths during a castle famine, producing an endless churn rather than the intended decline. The design's 'shrinking pop lowers the rate' self-correction (food-consumption.md:74-76) does nothing during famine because food is already 0 â€” only hauling ends it.
    FIX:      Scale the death cadence with the deficit or population (e.g. interval = base / max(1, deficitMouths), or kill a fraction of the hungry pop per interval) so famine severity tracks how badly the civ is underfed, while keeping the staggered-not-cliff async-fairness property.
    VERIFY:   StarvationDeathEvent.Apply reschedules unconditionally at sim.Now + StarvationDeathInterval = +60 (StarvationDeathEvent.cs:82-83; constant FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:29), with no dependence on PopulationCount or deficit â€” confirmed. Full-wipe = StarvationStartDelay 1440 + (pop-1)*60; for pop=100 that's 7380t (~29.5 yrs), slightly more than the finding's '6000t' approximation but same order, and per-capita pressure (~4 deaths/yr) is indeed flat. The breeding-outpaces-starvation embellishment is situationally true: BeginBreedingIntent.cs:64-74 draws BirthFoodCost=20 from the House (not the famine-struck castle), GestationTicks=300 (PopulationConfig.cs:39), so a civ with several stocked Houses births faster than 1 death/60t * (you'd need 5+ continuously-breeding houses to net-grow). The central balance point holds: large empires barely feel famine while tiny ones are gutted. Confirmed at medium.

  [MEDIUM] (balance | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) Consumption is tiny vs farm output and castle storage â€” food is a one-time setup chore, not a standing constraint
    EVIDENCE: Consumption = 1 food/citizen per 60 ticks (FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:21-22); at TicksPerYear=250 (PopulationConfig.cs:35) that is 4.17 food/citizen/year. A Farm with 3 farmers produces 3Ã—(BaseRatePerWorker 2 Ã— RoleBonus 2/1) = 12 food per 10-tick period = 1.2 food/tick (StructureCatalog.cs:89-95, ProductionTickEvent.cs:92-94) = 72 food/60t, i.e. one farm sustains 72 concurrent citizens. Castle StorageCapacity = 5000 (StructureCatalog.cs:13) = 1200 citizen-years of buffer; a single full castle feeds a 30-unit empire for ~40 years. Even one lone farmer (0.4 food/tick) feeds 24 citizens.
    IMPACT:   For realistic empire sizes (server seeds 14 units, WorldFactory.cs:51-66; breeding is gated to ~1 child/300t/house), a single farm plus an occasional top-up haul trivially covers consumption, after which the 5000-cap castle granary makes food a non-issue for decades. The intended friction (hauling/raids) exists, but the production-and-storage side is so generous that food rarely does any ongoing work â€” borderline 'doesn't pull its weight' in steady state. The interesting long-game pressure (farms permanently sterilize a 5x5 grassland block over ~2600t â€” BiomeDegradationConfig.cs:51,62,72,76) is real but slow and invisible at typical play horizons.
    FIX:      Raise FoodPerCitizenPerPeriod (or shorten the period) so a citizen-year of food is a meaningful fraction of a farm's output, and/or lower the Castle food cap so the granary buffers months not decades. Tune so a static empire must keep ~1 farm per N citizens actively hauling, making supply lines continuously load-bearing.
    VERIFY:   Every cited number checks out. Consumption = 1 food/citizen/60t (FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:21-22); TicksPerYear=250 (PopulationConfig.cs:35) gives 4.17 food/citizen/year. Farm: BaseRatePerWorker=2, RoleBonusNumerator/Denominator=2/1, PreferredRole=Farmer, WorkerCap=3 (StructureCatalog.cs:89-95); ProductionTickEvent.cs:92-93 computes per preferred worker = 2*2/1 = 4 per 10t period, so 3 farmers = 12/period = 72 food/60t = sustains 72 citizens; a lone farmer = 0.4/tick = 24 citizens. Confirmed. Castle StorageCapacity=5000 (StructureCatalog.cs:13) = 1200 citizen-years, ~40 years for a 30-pop empire. Two honest mitigations the finding itself acknowledges: Farm BufferCap=40 (StructureCatalog.cs:92) throttles uncollected output (production isn't free-flowing without hauling), and Farm degradation sterilizes its grassland tile (latching to permanent Desert) over ~2600t (~10.4 years), forcing periodic farm relocation. So food is more than a pure one-time chore, but the core claim â€” consumption is tiny versus production and storage â€” is accurate. Confirmed at medium.

  [LOW] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=low) Flat per-citizen consumption: a 50-soldier army eats the same as 50 farmers, removing any demobilization/standing-army food pressure
    EVIDENCE: Rate is `pop * FoodPerCitizenPerPeriod` with FoodPerCitizenPerPeriod = 1 for every unit regardless of role or activity (FoodConsumption.cs:60-61, FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:22). Boats are excluded (GameWorld.cs:146-151) but all citizen roles are identical. Variable rates are explicitly deferred (food-consumption.md:319-321).
    IMPACT:   In a logistics-war game, 'armies eat' is the classic lever that makes mobilization a real economic decision and makes raiding/sieging supply lines pay off. With flat rates there is no cost to keeping a large standing army parked, and no reason to demobilize â€” food never differentiates a productive citizen from an idle soldier. This is the most impactful single knob the design already anticipates but the code lacks.
    FIX:      Add a per-role (or per-activity) consumption multiplier in the rate computation â€” soldiers eat more, children/embarked eat less. The lazy-catch-up structure already treats rate as a single derived scalar, so this is a localized change to the rate formula, though it becomes core-touching and must remain a pure function of snapshot state for determinism.
    VERIFY:   Accurate. Rate = pop * FoodPerCitizenPerPeriod with FoodPerCitizenPerPeriod = 1 for every role (FoodConsumption.cs:60-61, FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:22); only Boats are excluded from the pop count (GameWorld.cs:146-151 BumpPopulationCount and StarvationDeathEvent.cs:96-98 FindOldestCitizen). All citizen roles eat identically, so a standing army costs the same food as idle farmers and there is no demobilization pressure. This is a genuine missing lever in a logistics-war game. The one correction to the framing: it is an EXPLICITLY deferred design choice, not an oversight â€” food-consumption.md:319-321 ('Variable consumption rates. Soldiers eat more...') and the Out-of-scope list line 330 defer it by name, and the finding itself acknowledges this. So it is a fair missing-feature call at low severity, not a bug. Confirmed at low.

  [LOW] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=low) Design and acceptance-test list promise a capture-on-death food path that is not implemented; multi-castle behavior is mis-described and would double-drain
    EVIDENCE: food-consumption.md:188-195,360 describes capture via 'the existing M7 path' and lists FoodConsumptionTests.Capture_TransfersCitizen_DrainsBothCastles, but no owner-reassignment exists in combat (grep for `.OwnerId =` across Sim.Core finds only reads â€” View.cs:149,160, MovementCost.cs:62; CombatRules.cs has no capture), and that test is absent from FoodConsumptionTests.cs. Worse, population events only catch up FindCastleFor's canonical (lowest y,x) castle (Population.cs:79,117), while the non-canonical castle drains only via its own FamineCheck/StarvationDeath â€” it can enter famine and kill citizens while the canonical castle is full (and both castles can schedule independent starvation deaths, doubling the kill rate).
    IMPACT:   Latent today because capture isn't built, so no live bug. But the design's stated behavior is backwards (penalty, not bonus), and the FindCastleFor-canonical asymmetry means whenever capture does land, a player can 'starve with a full granary' on their second castle and suffer double starvation deaths. The acceptance-test list overstates coverage.
    FIX:      When capture lands, designate a single HomeCastle as the sink (already noted as deferred, food-consumption.md:310-314) so consumption isn't duplicated; until then, fix the doc to stop calling it a 'free larder' and remove the non-existent acceptance test from the list.
    VERIFY:   Verified. My grep for `OwnerId =` across Sim.Core returns only construction/genesis/birth/snapshot writes (BuildCompleteEvent, Genesis.cs:91,113, BirthEvent.cs:48, Snapshot.cs, PlaceSiteIntent.cs:87) and the boat-production path â€” NO combat owner reassignment; CombatRules has none. The similarly-named CombatCaptureTests.cs is about CARGO drop-to-ground ('M7 Phase E: capture economy. Cargo from a dying laden unit drops to the tile'), not castle/owner capture. The promised test is genuinely absent from FoodConsumptionTests.cs (I read the full file). On the double-drain/asymmetry: FoodConsumption.CatchUp uses PopulationOf(owner) = full pop per castle (FoodConsumption.cs:60-61), and FindCastleFor returns only the canonical lowest-(y,x) castle (FoodConsumption.cs:188-206), so OnUnitAdded/OnUnitRemoved catch up only the canonical castle while each castle runs its own FamineCheck/StarvationDeath keyed on full pop â€” so if capture ever lands, a second castle could famine/kill while the canonical one is full, and both could schedule independent deaths. The doc is genuinely self-contradictory ('the population eats from both castles simultaneously' = penalty vs 'for free second larder' = bonus, food-consumption.md:189-192).   [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=low) Two comments state DegradePeriod = 10 ticks but the value is 100 â€” farm-tile lifetime (and thus the food/grassland economy) is 10x what the docs imply
    EVIDENCE: BiomeDegradationConfig.cs:72 sets `DegradePeriod: 100` but its own adjacent comment says '10 ticks aligns with ProductionPeriodTicks'. With the real value 100, the math is 26 Ã— 100 = ~2600 ticks (Grassland baseline 50, DesertThreshold 25 â€” BiomeDegradationConfig.cs:51,62; step-snap to Desert baseline 10 in BiomeDegradation.ApplyMath:335-348). A 3-farmer farm therefore yields ~3120 food over ~2600t before its tile latches to permanent desert, not the ~312 over ~260t the comment implies.
    IMPACT:   This is the single biggest lever on whether food is a tight or trivial long-game constraint (farm lifetime output = how much grassland one citizen-life costs). The 10x doc/code discrepancy means anyone tuning the food economy from the comments will be off by an order of magnitude. The code is internally consistent at 100; only the comments are wrong, but the food balance is currently set by an unintended value relative to the documented design intent.
    FIX:      Reconcile intent: either change DegradePeriod to 10 (matching both comments and making farms a much sharper, finite food source, which would meaningfully tighten food balance) or fix both comments to 100. Decide deliberately because it directly sets farm-tile food yield.
    VERIFY:   Verified directly. BiomeDegradationConfig.cs:71-72 sets DegradePeriod: 100 while its adjacent comment says '10 ticks aligns with ProductionPeriodTicks (LumberCamp=10, Farm=10)'. StructureCatalog.cs:99-108 (Farm) likewise says '1 fertility per DegradePeriod (10 ticks)... -> ~260 ticks'; with the real 100 it is 26*100 = ~2600 ticks. Note the LumberCamp comment (StructureCatalog.cs:40-43) is ALSO wrong by the same factor ('~1000 ticks' to exhaust a Forest tile; real headroom 100->74 = 26 points * 100 = ~2600). Code is internally consistent at 100; only the comments are stale, and the food/grassland long-game lever is therefore set by a value 10x the documented intent. Low (comment-only correctness wart, but it is the single biggest food-economy tuning lever, so anyone tuning from comments is off by an order of magnitude). Confirmed at low.
  REFUTED/DROPPED:
    - [logic-hole] CurrentLevel pure-read casts periods*rate to int, can wrap for very long-idle high-pop castles and over-report food  (sev0=low -> verdict=refuted)  :: The cast at FoodConsumption.cs:177 `return (int)(periods * rate)` is real (periods is long, rate is int, product is long then truncated), but the overflow is structurally unreachable, so it is not a problem. Two compounding bounds: (1) Castle food is hard-capped â€” StorageStructure.Deposit returns Math.Min(amount, FreeSpace()) with FreeSpace = Capacity - TotalHeld and Castle Capacity = 5000 (Structure.cs:33,40; StructureCatalog.cs:13), so `available` <= 5000. (2) While not in famine and food>0, OnRateOrFoodChanged always schedules a FamineCheckEvent at the dry-out boundary lastTick + (fullMeals+1)*period (FoodConsumption.cs:147-159), and the sim cannot advance sim.Now past that scheduled event without firing it (which re-anchors LastFoodConsumedTick). Hence whenever CurrentLevel is called, now <= NextFamineCheckTick, so periods <= fullMeals+1 and periods*rate <= available + rate <= 5000 + pop. To overflow int you'd need pop ~ 2.1e9, which would overflow PopulationCount (also int) first and is physically absurd. Additionally, once famine is active ConsumptionUpTo short-circuits to 0 (FoodConsumption.cs:168), so a long-starved castle reports 0, not a full larder. World age in 'millions of ticks' does not increase periods because the anchor is refreshed at each dry-out, not at world start. Pure-read only, never hashed â€” and not reachable. Refuted.

##### Combat  [key=combat]
SUMMARY: The combat core is architecturally clean and its headline async-fairness goal â€” zero-variance, deterministic, snapshot-recoverable resolution â€” is genuinely met and well-tested (twin-run + mid-fight-restore hashes match). However, the model has serious gameplay-level holes. The first round is delayed a full RoundInterval and damage only accrues to units that linger across round boundaries, so moving units â€” especially on roads (cost as low as 2 vs the 10-tick round) â€” pass through hostile forces taking ~zero damage, which quietly defeats blockades and the raiding-of-caravans economy that the design treats as a pillar. Combat is also a deterministic fight-to-annihilation (the loser is always reduced to zero), so a marginal force edge produces total wipes rather than the "losses proportional to power ratio" the design promises, cementing the predictable-winner stalemate Â§9.3 warns about. Several promised mechanics are entirely absent (combat unit types / RPS, ranged-from-adjacent, castle capture = the win condition, unit healing), and a zero-net-power fight (two enemy boats, BasePower 0) never terminates.
STRENGTHS:
  + Zero-variance deterministic resolution, proven by twin-run and mid-fight snapshot hashes :: Resolution uses start-of-round power snapshots, sums (order-independent) for budgets, and a (Health ASC, Id ASC) casualty sort (CombatRoundEvent.cs:59-126), so outcomes are fully deterministic and order-independent even across snapshot restore. CombatResolutionTests.SameTickContention_Deterministic / Twin_FullBattle_Deterministic / MidFight_SnapshotRoundTrip_Identical and RecoveryTests lock it in. This is the single hardest async-fairness requirement (no coin-flip army wipes) and it is genuinely satisfied.
  + Deterministic, anti-griefing casualty rule :: Lowest-Health-first / lowest-Id tiebreak (CombatRoundEvent.cs:104-126) means a player never loses their best unit to a roll resolved while asleep â€” wounded units die first, predictably and observably. The design explicitly rejected seeded-random casualty selection for exactly this reason and the code honors it.
  + Re-gather-each-round makes reinforcement and retreat fall out for free :: Each round re-gathers current tile forces (CombatRoundEvent.cs:40,81) with no special-case wiring; units that arrived join, units that left drop out. Reinforcement_MidFight and Retreat_MidFight tests confirm. It's an elegant single mechanism that also correctly handles 3+-faction tiles (each owner is damaged only by its hostile counterparts, CombatRoundEvent.cs:65-73).
  + Force-pool-by-owner avoids the group-vs-solo branch :: ForcePower / GatherForcesOnTile pool by OwnerId and ignore group membership (CombatRules.cs:27-62), so a lone unit and a 3-unit group fight under identical code â€” no 'promote-solo-to-singleton-group' shim, exactly as the model intended.
  + Capture-not-destruction economy is implemented end-to-end and clean :: A dying laden unit drops cargo to world.GroundResources (CombatRules.cs:112-120) and HaulPickupEvent falls back to ground piles when no structure sources the resource (HaulPickupEvent.cs:79-118). CombatCaptureTests prove drop, accumulation across multiple deaths, and haul-from-ground. Against stationary targets the Â§7.3 raiding loop works.
  + Death cleanup and persistence discipline are thorough :: OnUnitDeath clears movement/haul/group anchors, attrition-disbands empty groups, handles embarked passengers and boat-drowning, and notifies the population layer (CombatRules.cs:70-149); pending stale events fence via Units.TryGetValue (CombatDeathTests). Combat state is pure (per-tile anchor) and regenerated by RegenerateQueue.From (RegenerateQueue.cs:62-69), so a mid-fight crash recovers to an identical outcome.
FINDINGS (kept=10, refuted/dropped=0):

  [HIGH] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) A fight where all belligerents have zero EffectivePower (two hostile boats, BasePower 0) reschedules rounds forever and never resolves
    EVIDENCE: Boats have BaseHealth 40 / BasePower 0 (UnitCombatCatalog.cs:36) and EffectivePower floors at 0 (CombatRules.cs:18-19). In CombatRoundEvent, each owner's damage budget is the sum of hostile counterparts' start power; if damage <= 0 the owner is skipped (CombatRoundEvent.cs:65-75), so two power-0 boats deal 0 to each other. The post-round end-check only ends combat when no hostile PAIR remains (CombatRoundEvent.cs:81-92) â€” both boats are still present and still hostile, so it reschedules another round at Now+10 (CombatRoundEvent.cs:94-97), forever. Boats move via MoveArrivalEvent and trigger combat like any unit (MoveArrivalEvent.cs:75); two enemy boats co-located on a water tile is reachable (cap is 50/tile, MovementConstants.cs:13). RoundNumber is a byte (CombatState.cs:19) and wraps every 256 rounds.
    IMPACT:   Two enemy boats that come to rest on the same water tile lock into an eternal no-damage combat: an unbounded scheduling loop (one CombatRoundEvent every 10 ticks forever) that never drains, must be regenerated on every snapshot restore, and would spam any future 'battle started' notification. Because passenger combat is deferred and boats can't damage each other, transports are effectively unsinkable â€” naval interdiction and at-sea raiding are impossible, and the boat-drowning death pipeline (CombatRules.cs:92-106) is unreachable in normal play. Same root cause would hit any fully-debuffed (0-power) land force.
    FIX:      Add a 'no progress' guard: if a round applies zero total damage across all owners, end the combat (or never start one where no belligerent has positive power). For real naval raiding, give boats positive BasePower or let escort passengers contribute. Core-touching (CombatRoundEvent / CombatTrigger).
    VERIFY:   Verified. Boat BaseHealth 40 / BasePower 0 (UnitCombatCatalog.cs:36); EffectivePower floors at 0 (CombatRules.cs:18-19). In CombatRoundEvent each owner's damage = sum of hostile counterparts' startPower; both boats contribute 0, so damage<=0 -> 'continue' skips both (CombatRoundEvent.cs:65-75). The end-check re-gathers and only terminates when no hostile PAIR remains (lines 81-92); both boats are still present and hostile, so it reschedules at Now+10 forever (lines 94-97). I confirmed there is NO round cap anywhere -- RoundNumber is a byte that just wraps (CombatState.cs:19) and is never compared to a limit. Reachable: boats are units that move via MoveIntent/Traversal.Water and trigger combat on arrival (MoveArrivalEvent.cs:75); two enemy boats can co-occupy a water tile (cap 50, MovementConstants.cs:13). One precision the finding omits: like finding #1, a MOVING boat leaves before round 1 (water cost 6 < 10), so the eternal loop specifically needs two enemy boats AT REST on the same tile -- still clearly reachable. Consequences are real: a permanent zombie combat re-scheduled every snapshot, transports literally unsinkable, and the boat-drowning pipeline (CombatRules.cs:92-106) is dead code in normal play. No existing test covers boat-vs-boat. High stands.

  [HIGH] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) Structures are non-combatants: no siege, no castle capture, no surrender â€” the game's only win condition is unreachable through combat
    EVIDENCE: combat-model.md:51-52 'Structures are NOT combatants. Sieges and capturing castles are a later combat extension.' GatherForcesOnTile only pools Units (CombatRules.cs:47-62); nothing reads structure health or transfers ownership. combat-model.md:164 'A faction at zero units just continues unit-less today.'     IMPACT:   You can kill every enemy unit and still not win â€” the castle is invulnerable and there is no surrender path, so matches cannot terminate via combat. The entire victory loop the design is built around is absent. (Acknowledged as deferred, but it is the single largest gameplay gap in the combat domain.)
    FIX:      Implement structures-as-combatants for the castle/war path: castle gains Health and joins the tile's force; reducing it transfers ownership (or triggers a surrender offer).     VERIFY:   Verified. combat-model.md:51-52 states 'Structures are NOT combatants. There is no surrender intent. So the stated win condition (conquer every castle or force surrender) is unreachable via combat. It is explicitly scoped as future work rather than a hidden bug, but it is genuinely the single largest gameplay gap in the combat domain, so high is fair.

  [HIGH] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) First combat round is delayed a full interval; moving units (especially on roads) take ~zero damage, defeating blockades and caravan-raiding
    EVIDENCE: CombatTrigger.MaybeBeginCombatOnTile schedules round 1 at sim.Now + RoundIntervalTicks (CombatTrigger.cs:45-48), never at Now; CombatRoundEvent reschedules at sim.Now + RoundIntervalTicks (CombatRoundEvent.cs:94-97). Default RoundIntervalTicks = 10 (CombatConfig.cs:13). Damage only lands when the round event fires and re-gathers the tile (CombatRoundEvent.cs:40,81). A unit arriving at an enemy tile at T schedules its next hop at T+ExecutionCost (MoveArrivalEvent.cs:99) â€” on a maxed grassland road that cost is 10-8=2 (RoadConstants.cs:14-20, MIN_COST=1), and water is 6 (BoatMovementCost.cs:20). All are < 10, so the mover leaves before round 1 fires; round 1 then re-gathers, finds the mover gone, and ends with zero damage. On plain grassland (cost 10) the combat round's Seq is lower than the next-hop's (trigger runs at MoveArrivalEvent.cs:75 before ScheduleNextHop at :99), so a mover takes exactly one round of chip then walks on. This directly contradicts design Â§9.2 'Melee on contact resolves in the engagement event â€” needs nothing extra.'
    IMPACT:   A stationary force cannot interdict a moving one: a healthy caravan/army passing through an ambush tile takes at most one round of chip (= blockers' power) and continues, and on any road takes nothing at all. Since roads are the logistics arteries (Â§8) and water cost (6) is also sub-interval, raiding MOVING caravans â€” the core of the Â§7.3 capture economy and the Â§8 'supply lines can be threatened' pillar â€” is essentially impossible; only units that voluntarily stop on a tile for â‰¥1 full interval, or are already near-death (the tests use Health=1 walkers, CombatDeathTests.cs:117-132), actually die. Perverse incentive: routing a caravan on your best road makes it both faster AND immune to ambush, the opposite of the design's 'a road you built can be used against you by a raider' (Â§8.6).
    FIX:      Add an engagement/zone-of-control model: when MaybeBeginCombatOnTile starts a fight, pin units on the tile (clear PathRemaining/NextArrival so they must issue a fresh disengage move, which itself re-triggers on arrival), and/or resolve round 1 immediately at sim.Now so contact always lands a blow. Core-touching (CombatTrigger/CombatRoundEvent/MoveArrivalEvent).
    VERIFY:   Verified end-to-end. CombatTrigger.cs:45 schedules round 1 at sim.Now + RoundIntervalTicks (no immediate round); CombatConfig default = 10 (CombatConfig.cs:13), and that default is what Genesis/WorldFactory use (no override in WorldFactory.cs). Grassland MoveCost = 10 (Biome.cs:23), road MAX_REDUCTION = 8 -> maxed grassland road cost 2 (RoadConstants.cs:20, EffectiveCost Road.cs:43-45), boat water cost 6 (BoatMovementCost.cs:20). MoveArrivalEvent.Apply triggers combat at line 75 BEFORE ScheduleNextHop at line 99, so on grassland (cost 10) the round (lower Seq) and next-hop fire same tick T+10 with the round dequeued first (EventQueue keyed (At,Seq), EventQueue.cs:11) -> mover takes exactly one round of chip then leaves; on any road or water (cost <10) the mover's next hop fires before T+10 -> ZERO damage. Decisively corroborated by the tests: the only mover-death tests (CombatDeathTests.cs:117,149) force Health=1, and the capture/trigger tests use stationary co-location (CombatTriggerTests.cs:63-65 both units stop on the SAME tile) or hand-placed Health=1 victims (CombatCaptureTests.cs:44,71). No test shows a full-HP caravan surviving/being-stopped while moving. This breaks road-based caravan raiding and blockades, which combat-model.md:31-34 and design 8.6 treat as real. One fair nuance: on plain (non-road) grassland a stationary ambush of >=10 power CAN one-round-kill a single passing 10-HP unit, so interdiction isn't literally zero everywhere -- but on roads (the logistics arteries) it is exactly zero regardless of ambush size. High stands.

  [MEDIUM] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) Unit Health is never restored anywhere â€” combat damage is permanent, so even decisive victories permanently degrade your army
    EVIDENCE: Across Sim.Core, Health is only ever auto-initialized at spawn (GameWorld.cs:159-160) or decremented in combat (CombatRoundEvent.cs:114-122).     IMPACT:   There is no rest, repair, or hospital mechanic, so an army's HP only ratchets downward over a campaign; the 'wounded soldier crawls home' texture the design wanted (combat-model.md:124-127) never recovers.     VERIFY:   Verified by exhaustive search: Unit.Health is only ever set at spawn-from-catalog (GameWorld.cs:159-160), decremented in combat (CombatRoundEvent.cs:114-122, u.Health -= damage / =0), or restored from snapshot (Snapshot.cs:372). One caveat: no design doc explicitly PROMISES healing -- combat-model.md only references the 'wounded soldier crawls home' texture (124-127) as a reason for per-unit HP, not a recovery mechanic -- so this is a forward-looking missing-feature, not a broken promise. The gameplay impact (armies only ratchet down, discouraging engagement) is real; medium is reasonable.

  [MEDIUM] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) Combat is only triggered by arrival, never by a diplomacy change: forces already sharing a tile when war becomes effective do not fight
    EVIDENCE: Combat is triggered solely from MoveArrivalEvent.cs:75 and GroupArrivalEvent.cs:73 (arrival).     IMPACT:   Two armies standing on the same tile when their war timer elapses simply coexist peacefully until one of them next moves â€” the mover can even walk away without a fight (arrival triggers only on the destination tile, not the one left).     VERIFY:   Verified. Combat is triggered only on arrival (MoveArrivalEvent.cs:75, GroupArrivalEvent.cs:73). WarBecomesEffectiveEvent.Apply just sets rel.State = Enemy and clears the pending anchor (WarBecomesEffectiveEvent.cs:39-41); Diplomacy.SetState likewise only mutates state (Diplomacy.cs:55-59); neither calls CombatTrigger. So forces already co-located when war flips coexist until one next ARRIVES somewhere. And because the trigger fires only on the destination tile, a co-located unit can move away to an empty tile with no combat on the tile it left -- a free disengage, confirmed by the trigger logic. This does soften design 10 'Enemy -- auto-combat when paths cross' and the 10.1 point-blank-flip picture. Medium is fair.

  [MEDIUM] (balance | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=high) Combat is a deterministic fight-to-annihilation: the loser is always wiped to zero and a marginal edge causes total losses, contradicting 'losses proportional to power ratio'
    EVIDENCE: Combat only ends when no hostile pair remains on the tile (CombatRoundEvent.cs:51-55, 81-92), i.e. when one side is fully gone or has left. There is no partial-loss/morale/break-off outcome. With lowest-Health-first concentration (CombatRoundEvent.cs:104-126) the winner loses the fewest possible whole units. Tests encode the shape: 2 vs 1 leaves the loser with 0 units and the WINNER with 2 units (one merely at 5 HP) â€” 100% vs 0% unit losses from a 2:1 edge (CombatResolutionTests.cs:76-91); equal 1v1 forces mutually annihilate to zero (CombatResolutionTests.cs:55-67). Because the weaker side deals less damage as it shrinks, the advantage compounds (Lanchester square law): an 11-vs-10 fight wipes the 10-stack entirely while the attacker keeps ~half. CombatRoundEvent reads only EffectivePower (catalog BasePower + buffs, CombatRules.cs:15-20) â€” no terrain, fortification, high-ground, or defender modifier anywhere. Design Â§9.3 demands 'losses proportional to the power ratio, no wild swings' and flags the 'bigger force always wins predictably â†’ players avoid all uncertain fights and stalemate' residual.
    IMPACT:   Outcomes are 100% computable before committing, and the loser is ALWAYS annihilated (no proportional partial loss). A 10% force edge yields a total enemy wipe, not a 10% trade, so a rational player never engages without a decisive local advantage and never accepts an even fight (mutual annihilation) â€” exactly the maneuver-only stalemate the design fears. It is also the worst case for fair-while-asleep: an offline defender who is even slightly outnumbered loses their entire army deterministically, with no defender's advantage on home tiles to blunt it (structures grant no combat bonus).
    FIX:      Introduce a defender/terrain advantage (e.g. damage-reduction for units on owned/structured tiles or favorable biome) and/or a small symmetric low-variance band (Â§13.5), and a disengage/break-off path so the loser isn't guaranteed total annihilation. At minimum, give fortified/home tiles a multiplier so defending while asleep is meaningfully safer than fighting in the open. Core-touching (CombatRoundEvent).
    VERIFY:   The mechanics are exactly as described: combat is fully deterministic (no Rng touched in CombatRoundEvent.cs), EffectivePower reads only catalog BasePower + buff PowerModifier with no terrain/fortification/high-ground/defender term (CombatRules.cs:15-20), combat ends only when no hostile pair remains (CombatRoundEvent.cs:51-55,81-92), and lowest-Health-first concentration plus shrinking-side damage gives Lanchester-square compounding (the loser is fully wiped while the winner keeps a disproportionate remainder; verified against BiggerForceWinsPredictably CombatResolutionTests.cs:76-91 and EqualForces mutual annihilation :55-67). However 'high' is overstated and the 'contradicts the design' framing is too strong: design 9.3 EXPLICITLY names the 'bigger force always wins predictably -> stalemate' as a 'Residual concern (tuning, not architecture)... not a reason to add tactical rules now,' and 13.5 lists 'combat variance band' as an open question. Per-round damage IS proportional to power; it's the cumulative all-or-nothing loser outcome that isn't. Also 'ALWAYS annihilated' is overstated for present players: retreat via re-gather is a real escape (Retreat_MidFight_StopsParticipation CombatResolutionTests.cs:204-222). Real and worth flagging for the fair-while-asleep/offline-defender angle, but an acknowledged, deferred tuning concern -> medium.

  [MEDIUM] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) Every fighter is statistically identical (HP 10 / Power 1); no soldier/archer/cavalry, no counters â€” combat is pure headcount with zero unit-design depth
    EVIDENCE: All civilian roles are uniform BaseHealth 10 / BasePower 1 (UnitCombatCatalog.cs:24-31); the only non-uniform row is Boat 40/0 (:36).     FIX:      Add the promised combat roles to UnitRole + UnitCombatCatalog (Soldier higher HP/Power, plus a ranged class) and let TrainUnitIntent produce them; give classes asymmetric stats so composition matters. Core-touching only for the enum/catalog rows (rollup already buff-aware).
    VERIFY:   Verified. Every civilian role is BaseHealth 10 / BasePower 1 (UnitCombatCatalog.cs:24-31); the only differentiated row is Boat 40/0 (:36) which has 0 power and so never fights. UnitRole has no Soldier/Archer/Knight class. combat-model.md:106-112,142-143 promises these 'later.' Force strength == headcount, no counters. Explicitly deferred but a real depth gap -> medium is appropriate.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=low) Edge-swap (two groups trading adjacent tiles) never triggers combat â€” armies can slip past each other
    EVIDENCE: The trigger only checks co-location on the arrived-at tile (CombatTrigger.cs:26-41); two units that swap tiles X<->Y in the same step never co-locate. Design Â§9.1 (lines 358-360) and the open question Â§13.8 (lines 522-523) call this out as 'ignore or special-case'.

    VERIFY:   Verified. Two units swapping tiles X<->Y in adjacent events never co-locate, so no combat triggers -- a raider can slip past a single blocker by swapping. Combined with finding #1 it does weaken stationary frontier blocking, but low is the right severity given the explicit acknowledgement.

  [LOW] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=low) Ranged-from-adjacent (Â§9.4) is unimplemented: GatherForcesOnTile only ever reads the single contact tile
    EVIDENCE: GatherForcesOnTile reads exactly one tile with no radius parameter (CombatRules.cs:47-62); the comment and combat-model.md:148-151 note the radius-0 'today / radius-1 later' plan.   [LOW] (unnecessary | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=low) Buff.HealthModifier is serialized and documented but read by no code path â€” a future +HP armor/training buff would silently do nothing
    EVIDENCE: EffectivePower sums only PowerModifier (CombatRules.cs:16-19).
