---------------------------------------------------------------------

##### Diplomacy (three states, telegraphed war)  [key=diplomacy]
SUMMARY: The diplomacy core is small, clean, and well-tested: canonical symmetric pair keys, the M4 anchor/fence pattern for pending wars, deterministic snapshots, and a coherent unilateral-war / bilateral-peace asymmetry that matches the async-fairness vision. The telegraphed-war delay does close the literal "flip at point-blank for an instant strike" version of the neutral exploit for ONLINE defenders. However, there are real gaps: war-becomes-effective never initiates combat on already-co-located forces (so the ambush army doesn't actually fight, and an at-cap contested tile deadlocks), no intent carries an authenticated actor (any client can declare war or accept peace on another faction's behalf), proposals have no dedup/cap (griefable + unbounded state), the Ally state is a near-dead mechanic with essentially no payoff over Neutral, and the "costly" half of the Â§10.1 escalation promise is unimplemented.
STRENGTHS:
  + Canonical symmetric pair key with self-pair guard :: FactionPair.Of always stores (min,max) and throws on a==b (FactionPair.cs:9-15), so AreHostile(a,b)==AreHostile(b,a) by construction and directional drift is impossible. RelationshipBetween adds a defensive a==bâ†’Neutral short-circuit (Diplomacy.cs:30). Clean, well-tested (FactionPair_Canonicalizes / RejectsSelfPair / RelationshipBetween_IsSymmetric).
  + Pending war uses the engine-wide anchor+fence pattern correctly :: A pending war is pure state (PendingEffectiveTick + PendingSeq on Relationship.cs:19-20); WarBecomesEffectiveEvent fences on (At,Seq) and no-ops if peace cleared it (WarBecomesEffectiveEvent.cs:28-37); RegenerateQueue rebuilds the event from the anchor on restore (RegenerateQueue.cs:52-56). This makes pending wars survive snapshot+crash deterministically, verified by DeclareWar_PendingWar_SnapshotRoundTrip and RecoveryTests.
  + Principled unilateral-war / bilateral-peace asymmetry :: Aggression is one-sided and telegraphed; peace and alliance require mutual consent and apply instantly because both sides agreed (RespondToProposalIntent.cs:62-69). The aggressor-keeps-initiative texture (a winning attacker can decline a loser's peace, since peace needs the attacker's accept) is a thoughtful, internally consistent fit for conquest-as-win-condition, and the doc reasons it out explicitly.
  + Public diplomatic state with proposals as the only private exception :: Relationships and pending wars are public to all viewers; only IncomingProposals are scoped to the target (View.cs:172-186), pinned by tests (PendingWar_VisibleToEveryPlayer, IncomingProposals_ScopedToTargetOnly). This avoids a 'political fog' complexity sink while keeping negotiation posture private â€” a clean, well-justified scoping decision.
  + Determinism discipline :: Relationships and Proposals are SortedDictionaries keyed by canonical pair / monotonic id (Diplomacy.cs:17-22) for order-stable serialization, and the full declareâ†’effectiveâ†’proposeâ†’accept scenario is asserted bit-identical across twin runs (DiplomacyDeterminismTests.FullScenario_TwinRunMatches). Consistent with the rest of the sim's determinism contract.
FINDINGS (kept=8, refuted/dropped=0):

  [HIGH] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) Declarer/Proposer/Responder ids are self-asserted and never bound to the submitting player
    EVIDENCE: DeclareWarIntent (DeclareWarIntent.cs:39-62) validates DeclarerId only against world.Players, never against Intent.PlayerId. ProposeRelationshipIntent (ProposeRelationshipIntent.cs:35-71) likewise. RespondToProposalIntent checks proposal.TargetId != ResponderId (RespondToProposalIntent.cs:42-46) but never checks that the submitter IS ResponderId. Intent.PlayerId (Intent.cs:12) is documented as only '(eventually) used by validation when intents become player-scoped.' The host does no auth: GameHost.SubmitEnvelopeJson (GameHost.cs:76-92) deserializes the client envelope and submits it verbatim; the /intent endpoint (HttpApi.cs:58-64) takes no player identity.
    IMPACT:   In a 'dumb client sends intents' model the server must bind submitterâ†’actor. Today nothing does. A client can submit DeclareWarIntent(declarer=3, target=4) to start a war between two OTHER factions, or RespondToProposalIntent(responder=1, accept=true) to accept/decline a peace or alliance on faction 1's behalf, or accept its own proposal by impersonating the target. For a subsystem whose entire fairness model rests on 'aggression is your choice; peace needs the other side's consent,' unauthenticated actor ids void the guarantee.
    FIX:      Cross-check the actor id against the authenticated submitter. Cleanest: drop DeclarerId/ProposerId/ResponderId in favor of the base Intent.PlayerId, set PlayerId from the authenticated session at the host (not from client JSON), and validate in Resolve. This is a cross-cutting/known-deferred concern (the Intent.PlayerId comment flags it), but diplomacy is the subsystem where the spoof is most damaging.
    VERIFY:   Code claim fully verified. DeclareWarIntent.Resolve (DeclareWarIntent.cs:39-62) and ProposeRelationshipIntent.Resolve (ProposeRelationshipIntent.cs:35-71) validate the actor id only against world.Players, never against Intent.PlayerId. RespondToProposalIntent.cs:42-46 checks proposal.TargetId==ResponderId but never that the submitter IS ResponderId. GameHost.SubmitEnvelopeJson (GameHost.cs:76-93) deserializes the envelope and submits verbatim; the /intent endpoint (HttpApi.cs:58-64) carries no identity. So a client can declare war between two other factions, or accept/decline a proposal on another faction's behalf. Mitigations the finding understates: Intent.cs:9-12 explicitly documents PlayerId as deferred ('eventually used by validation when intents become player-scoped'), the listener binds http://localhost only (HttpApi.cs:19), and this is a SYSTEM-WIDE pre-multiplayer gap (every intent is unauthenticated), not a diplomacy-specific bug. So it is not a live exploit in the current single-host dev build. But the game's whole premise is async multiplayer, and the diplomacy consent model ('peace needs the other side's consent') is genuinely unenforced in code, so it is a real must-fix-before-multiplayer hole. High retained with that context.

  [HIGH] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) War becoming effective never starts combat on already-co-located forces (at-cap tiles deadlock)
    EVIDENCE: WarBecomesEffectiveEvent.Apply (WarBecomesEffectiveEvent.cs:18-42) only sets rel.State=Enemy and clears the pending anchor; it never calls Combat. Combat is initiated ONLY by an arrival: CombatTrigger.MaybeBeginCombatOnTile is invoked solely from MoveArrivalEvent.cs:75 and GroupArrivalEvent.cs:73. Both arrival handlers also reject an at-cap arrival and return BEFORE reaching that trigger (MoveArrivalEvent.cs:48-59 returns at line 57; GroupArrivalEvent.cs:46-54 returns at line 53; MaxUnitsPerTile=50, MovementConstants.cs:13). Neutral/Ally co-location is permitted because AreHostile is true only for Enemy (Diplomacy.cs:39), so a neutral army can legally stack onto an enemy tile.
    IMPACT:   Design Â§10 promises 'Enemy â€” auto-combat when paths cross.' If paths are ALREADY crossed (a neutral army marched onto the defender's tile and stopped) and the relationship then flips to Enemy, no combat starts â€” there is no arrival event to fire the trigger. The 'ambush' just sits there inert until someone routes a fresh unit onto the tile. Worse: if the tile is saturated to the 50-unit cap, every reinforcing arrival is rejected before the combat trigger runs, so two enemy armies stacked to cap can never fight there â€” a permanent no-combat zone. This directly undercuts the exact neutral-exploit scenario the telegraph is meant to resolve.
    FIX:      Core-touching: in WarBecomesEffectiveEvent.Apply, after flipping to Enemy, scan tiles occupied by the now-hostile pair and call CombatTrigger.MaybeBeginCombatOnTile on each (or maintain a per-owner tile index to avoid a full unit scan). This makes the auto-combat contract hold for relationship transitions, not just movement. Also reconsider ordering so an at-cap tile can still resolve into combat.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed. WarBecomesEffectiveEvent.Apply (WarBecomesEffectiveEvent.cs:18-42) only sets rel.State=Enemy and clears the pending anchor â€” it never calls CombatTrigger. A repo-wide grep confirms MaybeBeginCombatOnTile is invoked from exactly two PRODUCTION sites: MoveArrivalEvent.cs:75 and GroupArrivalEvent.cs:73 (the many other hits are test scaffolding). Both handlers reject an over-cap arrival and return BEFORE the trigger (MoveArrivalEvent.cs:48-59; GroupArrivalEvent.cs:46-54; cap 50, MovementConstants.cs:13). AreHostile is true only for Enemy (Diplomacy.cs:39), so a Neutral army can legally stack onto an occupied tile (no ownership gate on tile entry â€” CountUnitsOnTile is owner-agnostic). The CombatTriggerTests.EnemyArrival_StartsCombat test makes war effective FIRST then marches units in, so the co-located-then-flip path is untested. This is exactly the Â§10.1 'march in neutral, flip to enemy at point-blank' scenario the design says combat must resolve ('the sneak-army must survive the target reacting before the switch flips'), and Â§10's 'Enemy â€” auto-combat when paths cross' is broken for already-crossed paths. Two caveats that keep this from being unconditional: (a) below cap the attacker has an easy workaround â€” nudge any fresh unit onto the tile to re-fire the trigger; (b) reaching the 50-unit cap is the documented 'panic switch never hit in normal play.' But at cap it is a genuine permanent no-combat deadlock, and the auto-combat promise genuinely fails on contact. High stands.

  [MEDIUM] (balance | verdict=partial | conf=medium | sev0=medium) War delay is a flat tick constant blind to target-online-status and proximity
    EVIDENCE: Delay default = 100 ticks (DiplomacyConfig.cs:21). Movement costs (Biome.cs:22-41): grassland 10 ticks/tile, forest 30, hills 25, mountain 45, desert 40 â€” so 100 ticks is only ~10 grassland tiles (â‰ˆ2 on mountain) of reaction. At the default host rate TicksPerSecond=20 (ServerOptions.cs:8) that is 5 wall-clock seconds. The telegraph is uniform regardless of whether the declarer's army is across a 30-tile map (test map 30x30, castles at (2,2) and (25,25), ~23 tiles apart) or already at point-blank.
    IMPACT:   The game's stated principle is 'fair while asleep' (async, players usually offline). The telegraph is the sole diplomacy lever for that, but it is measured in TICKS that elapse on wall-clock time, with no coupling to whether the target has been online. If the delay elapses while the defender sleeps, they get the notification but cannot react â€” the exploit is only closed for ONLINE defenders. Separately, a single flat delay is crude: at point-blank every tick matters and 10 grassland-tiles of reaction may be too little to muster a defense (pursuit speed == flee speed, so the defender can't outrun a stacked attacker), while a cross-map declaration's telegraph is strategically irrelevant.
    FIX:      Tie async-fairness to a real signal rather than a flat tick count: e.g. ensure the effective tick can't fall inside a window where the target hasn't been seen online, or pair the delay with offline/just-attacked protection (a Â§12 concern, currently deferred). At minimum document the intended ticksâ†’hours mapping and pick a default that exceeds a typical offline window at the production tps. Per-proximity or per-pair 'diplomatic insulation' is already sketched as future work in the doc.
    VERIFY:   Numbers all verified: Delay default 100 (DiplomacyConfig.cs:21); biome costs grassland 10 / forest 30 / hills 25 / mountain 45 / desert 40 (Biome.cs:22-41) â†’ 100 ticks â‰ˆ 10 grassland tiles; TicksPerSecond default 20 (ServerOptions.cs:8); test map 30x30 castles (2,2)/(25,25). Importantly, WorldFactory.BuildSpec (WorldFactory.cs:100-106) does NOT override Diplomacy, so the live host ships the default Delay=100. Two overstatements: (a) the '5 wall-clock seconds' is a dev artifact of --tps 20 â€” the tickâ†’wallclock mapping is a deployment knob (a production tps of, say, ~1 tick/min turns 100 ticks into ~1.7h, matching the design's 'some hours'); the sim constant is in TICKS, not seconds. (b) The flat/proximity-uniform delay is a DELIBERATE, documented decision: diplomacy-model.md:95-102 and 134-137 explicitly choose a single world constant and list per-pair delays as planned future work ('we don't need that flexibility yet'). The one genuinely strong, tps-independent point survives: the telegraph elapses on wall-clock and is blind to whether the target is awake, so it only protects online/soon-online defenders â€” a real tension with the 'fair while asleep' principle (push-notification infra is itself deferred, diplomacy-model.md:138-141). Pursuit==flee speed is accurate (no role-based speed modifier). Real concern, overstated framing â†’ partial, medium for the online-status point.

  [MEDIUM] (balance | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) Proposals have no dedup or cap â€” griefable and unbounded state growth
    EVIDENCE: ProposeRelationshipIntent.Resolve only rejects a proposal when currentState==DesiredState && !hasPendingWar (ProposeRelationshipIntent.cs:56-58). There is no check for an existing open proposal of the same (proposer,target,desired). So while Neutral, ProposeRelationshipIntent(A,B,Ally) can be submitted thousands of times, each minting a fresh id (NextProposalId++, ProposeRelationshipIntent.cs:62-69) and a persistent row in Diplomacy.Proposals (Diplomacy.cs:21). Proposals are only removed on touch (response) or lazy expiry-on-touch (RespondToProposalIntent.cs:47-54); nothing GCs untouched expired offers. The PlayerView includes EVERY proposal addressed to the player with no expiry filter (View.cs:180-186), so the target's IncomingProposals list balloons and even shows already-expired offers.
    IMPACT:   A hostile (or, given the auth gap above, any) faction can flood a target's inbox with duplicate/expired offers, bloat every snapshot, and grow the view payload without bound. Even absent malice, expired proposals linger forever until individually responded to.
    FIX:      Reject a propose when an open, non-expired proposal already exists for the same (pair, desiredState) â€” or cap open proposals per (proposer,target). Filter expired proposals out of the PlayerView (now > ExpiryTick), and/or add a cheap periodic sweep. Low risk, non-core-shape change.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed. ProposeRelationshipIntent.Resolve only rejects when currentState==DesiredState && !hasPendingWar (ProposeRelationshipIntent.cs:56-58); there is no dedup against an existing open (proposer,target,desired) proposal, and each accepted proposal mints a fresh id (NextProposalId++, lines 62-69) into the persistent SortedDictionary (Diplomacy.cs:21). So while Neutral, Propose(A,B,Ally) can be submitted unboundedly. Removal happens only on response or lazy expiry-on-touch (RespondToProposalIntent.cs:47-54); no GC sweep exists for untouched expired offers (verified â€” no expiry-event scheduling anywhere). View.cs:180-186 adds EVERY proposal addressed to the player with NO expiry filter, so the inbox includes already-expired offers and grows with the spam. The decision doc (diplomacy-model.md:34-40) calls IncomingProposals the per-viewer state but never specifies caps/dedup/GC. Realistic ceiling on severity: each Proposal is a tiny struct, snapshot order is stable, and the target can decline (one removal each), so this is a griefing/state-hygiene/view-bloat issue rather than a correctness bug. Note same-faction spam works even without the auth gap; the auth gap (finding 2) additionally enables third-party spam. Medium is fair.

  [LOW] (missing-feature | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=low) Proposals can't be withdrawn â€” a stale Ally offer can be cashed in later against the proposer
    EVIDENCE: There is no WithdrawProposalIntent; only the target acts via RespondToProposalIntent (accept/decline), and otherwise the offer lives until ExpiryTick (default ProposalExpiryTicks=200, DiplomacyConfig.cs:21). ProposeRelationshipIntent has no counterpart to rescind (ProposeRelationshipIntent.cs).
    IMPACT:   A proposer is committed to honoring an offer for the full expiry window even if the strategic situation changes. Example: A offers Ally to B early; A later goes to war with B's friend; B can still accept the stale Ally offer at tick 199, locking A into an alliance A no longer wants. The proposer has no recourse.
    FIX:      Add a WithdrawProposalIntent (proposer-only, removes the open proposal). Cheap, non-core-shape, closes the stale-offer lock-in.
    VERIFY:   Verified there is no WithdrawProposalIntent (only DeclareWar/Propose/Respond exist in the Diplomacy folder), and a proposal lives until ExpiryTick = now + ProposalExpiryTicks (default 200, DiplomacyConfig.cs:21; ProposeRelationshipIntent.cs:66), acceptable by the target at any point in that window (RespondToProposalIntent.cs:47-60). So the proposer genuinely can't rescind. But the consequence is overstated: 'locked into an alliance A no longer wants, no recourse' ignores that A CAN exit â€” DeclareWarIntent permits Allyâ†’Enemy (it only rejects already-Enemy/already-pending), so A declares war (telegraphed) to leave. And since Ally is near-inert today (finding 4), being briefly unwilling-allied costs A almost nothing mechanically (only shared boat docks). The window length is also tps-dependent (200 ticks is ~10s at dev tps, longer in production). Real minor missing feature, but consequence inflated â†’ partial, low.

  [LOW] (unnecessary | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=low) AreHostile doc comment claims it is 'queryable but unused' â€” combat uses it heavily
    EVIDENCE: Diplomacy.cs:37-39 comments 'Combat (M7) calls this every time two forces might engage; today it's queryable but unused.' It is in fact called from CombatTrigger.cs:40, CombatRoundEvent.cs:50/71/86, and EmbarkIntent.cs:133. The comment predates M7 landing.
    IMPACT:   Misleading comment for the single most important method in the subsystem (the combat gate). Causes a future reader to under-estimate its blast radius when changing it.
    FIX:      Update the comment to reflect that AreHostile is the live combat gate consumed by CombatTrigger/CombatRoundEvent. Trivial.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed with one citation correction. The finding's claim that AreHostile is also called from EmbarkIntent.cs:133 is wrong â€” that line calls RelationshipBetween(...) == Ally, not AreHostile â€” but this does not weaken the core point, since combat use alone refutes 'unused.' Pure documentation nit, no behavioral impact â†’ low.

  [LOW] (missing-feature | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=medium) Ally offers almost no benefit over Neutral, so the whole bilateral-ally flow has near-zero incentive
    EVIDENCE: AreHostile is true only for Enemy (Diplomacy.cs:39), so Neutral and Ally are identical for combat â€” neither fights on contact. The ONLY concrete mechanical benefit wired for Ally in the whole core is boat embarking (EmbarkIntent.IsOwnOrAllied, EmbarkIntent.cs:113,130-135).     IMPACT:   Because Neutral already grants safe co-existence (no auto-combat) and costs nothing, there is essentially no reason to negotiate an alliance: it adds only the ability to share boats while exposing you to the same telegraphed betrayal (Allyâ†’Enemy is allowed via DeclareWarIntent). The entire propose/respond/ally machinery doesn't pull its weight in the current build â€” players are strictly better off staying Neutral. This is a known deferral, but it means a whole state and its negotiation flow are presently dead weight in gameplay terms.
    FIX:      Land at least one real ally payoff before shipping diplomacy as a feature â€” shared vision (overlap VisibleTiles) is the cheapest high-impact one and is already named in the doc. Until then, consider whether the Ally negotiation UI/flow should be gated off so it doesn't present a meaningless choice.
    VERIFY:   Substance is real but the framing overstates it and it is an explicitly-documented deliberate deferral. Verified: AreHostile gates on Enemy only (Diplomacy.cs:39), and a full grep shows the ONLY Ally-specific behavior in src is boat embarking via EmbarkIntent.IsOwnOrAllied (EmbarkIntent.cs:130-135, used at line 113). RelationshipState.cs:4-7 and diplomacy-model.md:13-15,81-93 describe Ally as 'inert-but-present, behaviorally identical to Neutral for M6,' with shared vision/passage/gated corridors listed as future expansion (lines 124-128) and a stated rationale ('three states, two behaviors, deliberate' â€” zero cost now vs meaningful retrofit later). So this is intended, not an oversight. The claim 'players are strictly better off staying Neutral' is overstated: ally grants a genuine (if minor) benefit â€” embarking from an allied dock â€” so it is marginally better, not strictly worse. Valid as a 'design promises Ally benefits the code lacks' observation, but it is a known deferral with a sound forward-compat justification, so low.

  [LOW] (missing-feature | verdict=partial | conf=medium | sev0=low) Declaring war is free and re-declarable â€” the 'â€¦and costly' half of Â§10.1 is unimplemented
    EVIDENCE: Design Â§10.1 is titled 'Escalation must be telegraphed and costly (closes the neutral exploit)' and says 'Betrayal becomes a genuine, risky, telegraphed act.' DeclareWarIntent.Resolve (DeclareWarIntent.cs:39-62) charges no resource, no reputation, and imposes no cooldown; the only gates are self/missing/already-enemy/already-pending. After a bilateral peace returns the pair to Neutral, the aggressor can immediately re-declare with no penalty.
    IMPACT:   Only the 'telegraphed' half of the promise exists; the 'costly/risky' half does not. Combined with the lack of a cooldown, an aggressor can keep a target in a perpetual declareâ†’peaceâ†’re-declare harassment loop, forcing them to keep re-mounting defenses, at zero cost to the aggressor. The telegraph makes each instance fair-while-awake but does nothing to make aggression a considered, costly act.
    FIX:      Either attach a tangible cost to DeclareWarIntent (resource upkeep, a reputation/standing hit, or a per-pair re-declare cooldown) or amend the design doc to drop the 'costly' framing. A short post-peace cooldown is the lowest-risk lever against the harassment loop.
    VERIFY:   Literal code claim is true: DeclareWarIntent.Resolve (DeclareWarIntent.cs:39-62) charges no resource/reputation and imposes no cooldown; gates are only self/missing/already-enemy/already-pending, and after a bilateral peace returns the pair to Neutral nothing blocks immediate re-declaration. But the 'broken promise' and 'harassment loop' framing is undercut by the decision doc. diplomacy-model.md:44-60 frames aggression's fairness/cost entirely as the telegraph-induced strategic RISK ('Betrayal becomes a genuine, risky, telegraphed act'), not a resource fee â€” so design Â§10.1's heading word 'costly' plausibly means that risk, not an unimplemented currency cost. More decisively, the harassment loop requires the AGGRESSOR to voluntarily accept peace before re-declaring, and the doc explicitly makes peace require the aggressor's consent and treats the aggressor refusing/pressing as 'conquest working as intended' (lines 56-60). A griefer would simply keep the war active rather than accept peace to re-declare, so 'perpetual declareâ†’peaceâ†’re-declare at zero cost' is not a realistic vector. A cost/cooldown is a reasonable future lever, but the finding overstates it as a broken promise + griefing exploit â†’ partial, low.
