##### Vision & Fog of War  [key=vision-fog]
SUMMARY: The fog core is genuinely well-built: visibility is fully DERIVED from vision sources (no "close fog behind unit" code), the explored/remembered-biome layer is the single write path through Sight.Reveal, and a hash-equality determinism test enforces "fog never touches the sim." The memory rule (Â§4.2) is implemented precisely for biome, with an explicit anti-leak test. The main gaps are at the edges of the principle: the Â§4.3 ambush bonus â€” the one sanctioned reward for attacking from fog â€” is unimplemented; road condition leaks live traffic through fog at the server projection (the Â§8.6 promise it should NOT); enemy structures aren't remembered the way biome/roads are; the pathfinder is omniscient about terrain so scouting only ever reveals hidden units, not routes; and all diplomacy is globally visible regardless of presence.
STRENGTHS:
  + Visibility is truly derived â€” the Â§4.1 promise kept exactly :: View.VisibleTiles (View.cs:67-93) recomputes the union of vision-source discs from current positions every call and never writes; there is no 'close fog behind a unit' code anywhere. Re-fog falls out automatically (LiveVisibilityTests.VisibilityMovesWithMovingUnit) and towers 'pin' vision purely by being static sources (Tower_HoldsItsArea_AfterBeingBuilt) with no special-case logic â€” exactly the emergent behavior Â§4.1/Â§4.4 describe.
  + Inverted pure-read wall, enforced by a hash-equality determinism test :: Sight.Reveal is the single write path for Explored + RememberedBiome (Sight.cs:52-89), called only from deterministic events (Move/Group arrival, BuildComplete, Genesis, Disembark). FogDeterminismTests.ViewsOff_HashEquals_ViewsOn spams view computation every 5 ticks and asserts the sim hash is identical â€” a crisp, automated guarantee that fog can never leak into sim state.
  + Last-seen biome memory with a real anti-leak contract (Â§4.2) :: RememberedBiome stores the biome at reveal time (Sight.cs:84-85); BuildPlayerView shows last-seen biome for explored-not-visible tiles and live biome only for visible tiles (View.cs:129-138). BiomeDegradationFogTests.View_DoesNotLeak_CurrentBiome_OnNonVisibleTiles proves a tile that degrades behind the fog still shows its stale value â€” 'terrain remembered, activity hidden,' implemented precisely and tested against leakage.
  + Integer-exact Euclidean discs, identical shape for explored and visible :: Both Sight.Reveal and View.AddDisc use squared-distance vs r*r with grid clamping (Sight.cs:67-88, View.cs:213-232), kept deliberately identical so a source's visible disc and the explored disc it writes match exactly. No floating point, so visibility is bit-deterministic and snapshot-stable (ExploredMemoryTests round-trips, TwoUnitsArrivingSameTick_ProduceStableExplored).
  + Sensible, well-tiered vision radii :: base unit 3 (~29 tiles) < castle 5 (~81) < scout 6 (~113) < tower 7 (~149) (Sight.cs:17-31). The scout sees ~3.9x a base citizen â€” a clear role payoff â€” and the largest radius belongs to the static, vision-pinning tower, so the 'invest presence to hold vision' idea is encoded directly in the numbers. Retraining to Scout is free/instant (TrainUnitIntent has no resource cost), keeping exploration cheap and time-gated rather than resource-gated, in line with the time-and-distance principle.
FINDINGS (kept=8, refuted/dropped=0):

  [MEDIUM] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=medium) Enemy structures vanish on re-fog â€” not remembered like biome and roads
    EVIDENCE: View.BuildPlayerView (Vision/View.cs:157-162) adds a non-owned StructureView only when visible.Contains(s.At). There is no per-player remembered-structures layer (GameWorld has Explored + RememberedBiome only, GameWorld.cs:40-53). ViewProjector forwards only view.VisibleStructures (ViewProjector.cs:144). Meanwhile biome (Â§4.2) and road existence (Â§8.6) DO persist through re-fog.
    IMPACT:   Scout an enemy castle or tower, lose vision, and it disappears from your map entirely â€” you 'forget' a permanent structure exists. That contradicts the spirit of the memory rule (terrain/infrastructure remembered, only live activity hidden). For a conquest game whose win condition is 'destroy every enemy castle,' forgetting where you found a castle the moment you re-fog is a real intel regression and a UX hole.
    FIX:      Add a sparse per-player remembered-structures layer written in lock-step with Reveal (last-seen kind/owner/position), surfaced alongside RememberedTerrain; keep live holdings/garrison fogged. Core-touching (write path lives next to Sight.Reveal in Sim.Core).
    VERIFY:   Confirmed. View.BuildPlayerView (View.cs:158-162) adds a non-owned StructureView only when visible.Contains(s.At); GameWorld carries Explored + RememberedBiome but no remembered-structures layer (GameWorld.cs:40-53), and ViewProjector forwards only view.VisibleStructures (ViewProjector.cs:144). Biome (Â§4.2) and road existence (Â§8.6) persist through re-fog, so scouting an enemy castle/tower and losing vision erases it from the map. For a game whose win condition is 'destroy every enemy castle' this is a genuine intel/UX regression and is inconsistent with the design's memory model (infrastructure remembered, only live activity hidden). Medium stands; note one defensible counter-argument â€” structures are mutable (capturable/destroyable) so could be treated as 'live,' but biome/roads already show stale memory by design, so remembering last-seen structures would be the consistent choice.

  [MEDIUM] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) Road condition leaks live activity through fog (contradicts Â§8.6's 'fair tension')
    EVIDENCE: ViewProjector.ProjectFogged (Sim.Server/ViewProjector.cs:124-129) emits Road.ConditionAt(world, tile, now) â€” the LIVE, traffic-inclusive, lazily-decayed condition â€” for every EXPLORED road tile, gated only on view.Explored.Contains(tile), not view.Visible. Road condition is raised by CreditTraffic on each MoveArrival (GameWorld.cs:14-19), so any unseen traversal writes a higher stored value. Design Â§8.6: 'A road is terrain memory... but who is currently walking it is live activity â€” still fogged unless you have eyes on it... A road you built can be used against you by a raider you can't see.'
    IMPACT:   A player watching a remembered (explored-but-fogged) road sees its condition climb above the pure-decay value they could predict from last sighting â€” unambiguous evidence that someone is currently using it, with no presence. This is exactly the inference Â§8.6 says should require a tower. It also undercuts the stated reason towers exist (to watch your roads). Note the inconsistency: biome memory correctly freezes the last-seen value via RememberedBiome with an explicit anti-leak test (BiomeDegradationFogTests.View_DoesNotLeak_CurrentBiome_OnNonVisibleTiles), but roads have no equivalent last-seen snapshot.
    FIX:      Mirror the RememberedBiome pattern for roads: record last-seen condition per player at each Reveal and surface that (or just road existence) for explored-not-visible tiles; show live Road.ConditionAt only for tiles in view.Visible. Fixable entirely in the server projection plus a small per-player remembered-condition layer.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed. ProjectFogged (ViewProjector.cs:124-129) gates road emission on view.Explored.Contains(tile) â€” NOT view.Visible â€” and reports the LIVE Road.ConditionAt(world,tile,now); there is no last-seen road snapshot. CreditTraffic (Road.cs:83, called from MoveArrivalEvent.cs:68 on every arrival) raises stored condition on any unseen traversal. So a player diffing a remembered road's condition against the pure-decay value they could predict sees it climb = presence-free evidence of live traffic, exactly what Â§8.6 says should require a tower. Stronger still: a road that emerged ENTIRELY in fog on a previously-explored tile appears from nothing (the loop iterates live world.Roads.Keys), leaking both existence and rising condition. The asymmetry is real: biome freezes last-seen via RememberedBiome with the anti-leak test View_DoesNotLeak_CurrentBiome_OnNonVisibleTiles (BiomeDegradationFogTests.cs:112-132); roads have no equivalent. Medium is fair â€” it directly contradicts the Â§8.6 'fair tension' and the stated tower rationale, though it is a low-bandwidth leak that requires the player to actively poll/diff.

  [MEDIUM] (missing-feature | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=high) The Â§4.3 ambush bonus (the ONE sanctioned fog-reads-sim exception) is not implemented
    EVIDENCE: Design Â§4.3 names an 'ambush bonus for attacking from outside the enemy's vision: a specific sim rule that reads vision' as the single deliberate coupling of fog into the sim â€” 'that is the point of ambush.' But no combat code reads vision: CombatTrigger.MaybeBeginCombatOnTile (Combat/CombatTrigger.cs:18-50) and the round resolver consult only Diplomacy.AreHostile and ForcePower â€” zero View/Sight calls. A repo-wide search for 'ambush' in src returns no matches. combat-model.md:161-162 lists 'Fog-ambush bonus' under 'Future expansion,' confirming deferral.
    IMPACT:   Attacking from fog confers no mechanical advantage. Because combat is deterministic and 'bigger force wins predictably' (Â§9.3), with no first-strike-from-fog modifier there is no combat payoff for scouting, positioning, or surprise â€” the very behaviors the presence principle is meant to reward. Defenders and attackers are mechanically identical whether or not the victim saw it coming, hollowing out the thematic 'that is the point of ambush.'
    FIX:      Implement the one-shot first-round damage multiplier described in combat-model.md: when CombatTrigger fires, flag the attacking owner(s) whose force arrived from tiles outside the defender's VisibleTiles and apply a bounded (e.g. +25-50%) first-round bonus. Keep it deterministic and low-variance to respect Â§9.3. Core-touching (adds a vision read to Sim.Core combat resolution â€” the explicitly-sanctioned exception).
    VERIFY:   Factual claims are 100% correct. Repo-wide there is no 'ambush' token in src (verified). CombatTrigger.MaybeBeginCombatOnTile (CombatTrigger.cs:18-50) and CombatRoundEvent.Apply (CombatRoundEvent.cs) consult ONLY Diplomacy.AreHostile + CombatRules.EffectivePower/ForcePower â€” no View/Sight call. MoveArrivalEvent.cs:75 fires the trigger, which schedules round 1 at sim.Now+RoundIntervalTicks with NO first-strike damage. combat-model.md:161-162 lists 'Fog-ambush bonus' under 'Future expansion.' So the bonus is genuinely unbuilt. BUT 'high' overstates it: this is an EXPLICITLY DEFERRED feature, not a broken promise. Design Â§9.3 even says of pure-headcount combat 'Watch for this in balancing; it's not a reason to add tactical rules now' â€” directly endorsing deferral. Mechanically a one-shot first-round multiplier (combat-model.md:162) is a modest modifier in a deterministic system, and scouting retains real value (locate forces, plan routes, time attacks, avoid being ambushed). Real gap with thematic weight, but severity is medium, not high.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=low) Â§4.3 'fog never touches the sim (one exception)' is already false â€” pathfinding reads fog
    EVIDENCE: MoveIntent.Resolve calls View.VisibleTiles(world, unit.OwnerId) to compute the committed path (Movement/MoveIntent.cs:114), and MoveGroupIntent does the same (Groups/MoveGroupIntent.cs:55,90). The path determines arrival ticks and thus all downstream combat/economy timing â€” sim state that depends on the player's fog. This is a second fogâ†’sim coupling beyond the (still-unimplemented) ambush exception Â§4.3 calls 'the one deliberate exception.'
    IMPACT:   This does NOT break determinism â€” VisibleTiles is a pure function of world state, computed at resolution time â€” so it is a documentation/principle inconsistency, not a runtime bug. But the design doc's central claim that exactly one rule reads vision is now inaccurate, which matters because Â§4.3 is used as the litmus test for whether new fog couplings are allowed.
    FIX:      Update Â§4.3 to acknowledge fog-aware planning as a deliberate, deterministic 'cost of ignorance' coupling (it is already well-documented in MovementCost.cs), so the 'one exception' framing isn't silently violated. No code change needed.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed and accurately framed. MoveIntent.BeginMove calls View.VisibleTiles(world, unit.OwnerId) (MoveIntent.cs:114) and MoveGroupIntent does the same (MoveGroupIntent.cs:55,90,95); the resulting path sets arrival ticks (ScheduleNextHop) and thus downstream combat/economy timing â€” a genuine second fog->sim read beyond the (still-unimplemented) Â§4.3 ambush exception. As the finding states, it does NOT break determinism: VisibleTiles is a pure function of world state computed at resolution time. movement-cost.md openly documents and defends fog-aware planning as intended ('Why fog-aware planning specifically'), which confirms the point: Â§4.3's claim that exactly one rule reads vision is now imprecise/outdated. Pure documentation/principle inconsistency, low severity â€” correct.

  [LOW] (unnecessary | verdict=partial | conf=medium | sev0=low) PendingWars duplicates Relationships; some view lists have nondeterministic order
    EVIDENCE: PendingWarView is emitted for every relationship whose PendingEffectiveTick is set (Vision/View.cs:176-177), but RelationshipView already carries PendingEffectiveTick (View.cs:174-175) â€” the same data twice. Separately, OngoingCombats is built by iterating world.CombatStates, a plain Dictionary<TileCoord,CombatState> (GameWorld.cs:69), and the diplomacy lists iterate dictionaries too â€” so list ORDER is not stable across runs.
    IMPACT:   The PendingWars duplication is harmless but is extra surface the client must reconcile. The unordered view lists do not affect the sim hash (views are pure reads and aren't hashed), so this is not a determinism bug â€” but it can make view-snapshot diffing or replay-comparison of client state spuriously flaky, which is at odds with the project's replay-everything ethos.
    FIX:      Drop PendingWars (clients derive it from Relationships) or document it as a convenience denormalization. If view determinism is ever desired for tooling, sort OngoingCombats/Relationships/Proposals by a stable key before returning.
    VERIFY:   Mixed. (1) PendingWars duplication: CONFIRMED â€” RelationshipView already carries PendingEffectiveTick (View.cs:21-24,174-175) and a separate PendingWarView is also emitted for the same pairs (View.cs:25,176-177). Harmless redundancy, as claimed. (2) 'diplomacy lists iterate dictionaries so order is not stable': REFUTED â€” world.Diplomacy.Relationships and Proposals are BOTH SortedDictionary (Diplomacy.cs:17,21) and FactionPair implements IComparable<FactionPair> (FactionPair.cs:7,27-31); Factions iterates world.Players, also a SortedDictionary (GameWorld.cs:23). All three iterate in deterministic sorted order. (3) OngoingCombats: world.CombatStates is a plain Dictionary<TileCoord,CombatState> (GameWorld.cs:69) and View.cs:190 iterates it unsorted â€” unlike the snapshot path which canonicalizes it â€” so its order is not the canonical (y,x) order. But 'nondeterministic across runs' is overstated: with a deterministic struct-key GetHashCode and an identical event sequence the enumeration is reproducible; and as the finding concedes, none of this is hashed so there is zero sim-determinism impact. Net: one real (trivial) duplication + one real (cosmetic, combat-only) ordering nit, plus an incorrect broad claim about diplomacy ordering. Partial, low.

  [LOW] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=low) Owner cannot inspect their own embarked citizens (only a passenger count)
    EVIDENCE: View.BuildPlayerView skips IsEmbarked units in ALL views including the owner's (Vision/View.cs:148, 'if (u.IsEmbarked) continue;'), with the comment 'not shown in player views (own or enemy).' The boat's ViewProjector DTO exposes only an aggregate count (ViewProjector.cs:159-160, 174-175: Passengers = u.Passengers.Count) â€” no per-passenger id/role/health/age.
    IMPACT:   The rationale 'the hull blocks their view' correctly hides passengers from ENEMIES, but it also blinds the OWNER to their own in-transit citizens. In an async, plan-ahead game you load citizens on a boat and lose all per-citizen state (who, their health, their age) until disembark â€” you can't tell if a starving or wounded citizen is aboard. The hull should block others' knowledge, not the owner's own.
    FIX:      Surface own embarked passengers (full UnitView detail) to the owning player only; continue hiding them from everyone else. Small change in View.cs / ViewProjector.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed. View.BuildPlayerView skips IsEmbarked units in ALL views including the owner's (View.cs:147-148, comment 'not shown in player views (own or enemy)'). The boat DTO exposes only an aggregate Passengers count (ViewProjector.cs:159-160 reveal path, 174-175 fogged path) â€” no per-passenger id/role/health/age. The concern is substantive because embarked passengers retain MUTABLE state the owner would care about: they still age (AgeYears derives from BornTick regardless of embark) and still drain castle food (BumpPopulationCount, GameWorld.cs:146-151, only excludes Role==Boat, not embarked passengers), so a passenger can age-die or contribute to famine while aboard with the owner blind to it until DisembarkIntent lands them. The hull-blocks-view rationale correctly hides passengers from enemies but over-applies to the owner. Low is appropriate â€” a real inspection/UX gap, not a sim bug.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=partial | conf=medium | sev0=medium) Pathfinder is omniscient about terrain â€” scouting de-risks only hidden units, never routes
    EVIDENCE: MovementCost.PlanCost (Movement/MovementCost.cs:96-110) fogs ONLY crowding (CountVisibleUnitsOnTile), but its terrain term TerrainCostFor â†’ Road.EffectiveCost(world, tile, now) (MovementCost.cs:74-79, 104) reads the true biome + road condition of every tile, including never-explored ones. A* in MoveIntent.BeginMove (MoveIntent.cs:114-120) therefore routes optimally through unexplored terrain. RememberedBiome/Explored are never consulted by the planner.
    IMPACT:   Design Â§4.4 says 'Scouts... de-risk logistics by revealing routes before committing caravans' and Â§6.4 promises 'estimate first, exact after' (first traversal of raw ground should be only an estimate). In practice the planner already knows the cheapest path across terrain it has never seen, so a scout adds nothing to terrain-based route choice â€” its only routing value is exposing hidden enemy crowds. The terrain half of 'knowledge comes from presence' is unmodeled, weakening the headline justification for the scout role.
    FIX:      Make PlanCost read remembered/visible terrain (fall back to a pessimistic or worldgen estimate for unexplored tiles) so routes through fog are genuinely uncertain and scouting pays off in better routing. Core-touching (changes Sim.Core MovementCost.PlanCost). Alternatively, if omniscient terrain is an intentional simplification, soften Â§4.4/Â§6.4.
    VERIFY:   Code claim is correct: PlanCost (MovementCost.cs:96-110) fogs only crowding via CountVisibleUnitsOnTile; its terrain term TerrainCostForâ†’Road.EffectiveCost (MovementCost.cs:74-79,104) reads true biome+road of every tile incl. never-explored, and RememberedBiome/Explored are never consulted by the planner. HOWEVER this is INTENTIONAL, DOCUMENTED design, not a logic hole. movement-cost.md 'Why fog-aware planning specifically' scopes the fog to crowding only and pins it with the load-bearing test Path_DoesNotAvoidFoggedCrowd_RoutesStraightThrough. The Â§6.4 citation is a MISREAD: Â§6.4 explicitly says first traversal 'takes the honest, deterministic terrain time' and the estimate/exact distinction is the player's UI knowledge of arrival time, not the sim using worse routing â€” so true-terrain timing is precisely what Â§6.4 prescribes. The scout is not hollow: it de-risks the dangerous half (hidden enemies/congestion IS fogged in PlanCost). Only the Â§4.4 'reveal routes' framing is mildly in tension. Real but overstated; low, not medium, and design-sanctioned.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=partial | conf=medium | sev0=medium) All factions, relationships, and pending wars are globally visible regardless of presence
    EVIDENCE: BuildPlayerView lists a FactionView for every registered player (Vision/View.cs:166-168), a RelationshipView + PendingWarView for every diplomacy pair (View.cs:170-178) to every viewer. DiplomacyPlayerViewTests.PendingWar_VisibleToEveryPlayer asserts a 'third-party non-belligerent also sees it.' Design Â§10.1 only promises 'the target gets a notification immediately' on a war declaration â€” it never grants the whole world a live diplomatic map.
    IMPACT:   A player learns of factions they have never encountered and of wars on the far side of the map where they have zero presence â€” a direct tension with 'knowledge comes from presence.' This is a deliberate choice (pinned by tests), but it is a meaningful information channel that bypasses fog: you can infer the global political map, and even detect that two distant strangers are fighting, without ever scouting them.
    FIX:      Decide explicitly: either keep global diplomacy (and update Â§10 to say diplomatic posture is public knowledge), or scope FactionView/RelationshipView to factions the viewer has met (has ever had a unit/structure of theirs in vision, or shares a relationship with). Core-touching (View.cs is Sim.Core).
    VERIFY:   Factually correct: BuildPlayerView emits a FactionView for every player (View.cs:166-168) and a RelationshipView+PendingWarView for every diplomacy pair to every viewer (View.cs:170-178); DiplomacyPlayerViewTests.PendingWar_VisibleToEveryPlayer (DiplomacyPlayerViewTests.cs:71-89) pins that a third-party non-belligerent sees it. BUT this is an explicit, documented, test-pinned DESIGN DECISION, not a logic hole: View.cs:16-19 states 'Diplomatic state is PUBLIC KNOWLEDGE,' and Â§10.1 only promises the target a notification â€” it never promises locality, so the code doesn't contradict the doc. The finding itself concedes it is 'a deliberate choice (pinned by tests).' It is a legitimate tension with the presence principle and worth noting, but labeling it a logic-hole at medium overstates an intended, validated behavior. Partial, low.

---------------------------------------------------------------------

##### Boats & Naval  [key=boats-naval]
SUMMARY: The embarked-passenger model is the genuine highlight: passengers are taken off-tile and consistently excluded from vision, combat, crowding, hauling, and player views, with no dupe/loss path and a recursive drown-on-sink that keeps the passenger list consistent. Water-only traversal is enforced cleanly (land is Impassable, so boats can never strand on land), and boats are correctly exempt from food upkeep and aging â€” avoiding the catastrophic "boat dies of old age mid-voyage" failure. However, naval is under-integrated and economically unbounded: the dock auto-produces boats with zero per-boat cost, no upkeep, and no cap (a true free infinite navy); boats have 0 combat power so they can neither sink each other nor be intercepted (and two hostile boats spin combat forever); foot units can still wade across water at 250/tile, contradicting the doc's "un-invadable by sea" claim; and the 100-unit cargo hold is a dead feature nothing can load. There is also a reachable production-deadlock when a unit dies on a dock's slip.
STRENGTHS:
  + Embarked-passenger off-tile invariant is applied consistently :: EmbarkIntent removes passengers from all tile-scoped iterations via IsEmbarked, and every relevant reader honors it: vision (View.cs:75,148 / VisibleTiles), combat force rollups (CombatRules.cs:32,52), crowding cost (MovementCost.cs:41,57), and haul rejection (HaulIntent.cs:39) and move rejection (MoveIntent.cs:26). No dupe/loss path was found; the single invariant cleanly delivers the design's 'passengers contribute zero to movement/combat/vision by construction'.
  + Water-only traversal is enforced without a stuck-on-land class of bugs :: BoatMovementCost.cs maps every land biome to Impassable and Pathfinding.cs:48 skips Impassable (with an explicit A* overflow guard), so a boat can physically never path onto land, and there is no intent that places a boat on land. Boats spawn on a water slip and only ever move over water â€” the 'boat stuck on land / unit-domain confusion' failure mode is structurally impossible.
  + Boats correctly exempt from food upkeep and aging :: GameWorld.cs:146-151 and Population.cs:121-125 exclude UnitRole.Boat from PopulationCount, and BoatProductionTickEvent's bare world.AddUnit means ScheduleLifespan is never called for a boat. This prevents the fair-while-asleep catastrophe of a boat starving or dying of old age mid-voyage and drowning its passengers â€” exactly right for an async game.
  + Sink-drowns and stale-passenger cleanup are robust :: CombatRules.OnUnitDeath handles both directions: a passenger dying by any cause is pulled from its carrier's Passengers list (CombatRules.cs:79-83), and a boat dying recursively death-pipelines every passenger after clearing EmbarkedOn to avoid re-entrancy, then zeroes cargo via the normal drop path (CombatRules.cs:92-106). The BoatsPhaseE tests pin all three cases.
  + Dock production reuses the proven extractor anchor/fencing pattern with full persistence + determinism tests :: DockArmer.ArmIfDormant mirrors Extractor.ArmIfDormant (Seq-anchored, idempotent, slip-occupied stall + re-arm), and BoatsPhaseF pins twin-run hash equality, mid-sail snapshot recovery, and production-anchor round-trip. The boat-faster-than-any-foot-biome invariant (cost 6 < min land 10) is also locked by a test, guarding the core design contract.
FINDINGS (kept=7, refuted/dropped=0):

  [HIGH] (balance | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) Dock produces a free, upkeep-free, uncapped navy forever
    EVIDENCE: StructureCatalog.cs:157-173 â€” a Dock costs 200 Wood + 50 Stone, 200-tick build, 2 builders, then sets ProductionPeriodTicks=300. BoatProductionTickEvent.cs:48-66 spawns a boat on the slip and reschedules at sim.Now+300 with NO material/buffer/worker cost. The boat is added via bare world.AddUnit (line 52), so: it is excluded from PopulationCount/food upkeep (GameWorld.cs:146-151 BumpPopulationCount returns early for UnitRole.Boat), and Population.ScheduleLifespan is never called for it (Population.cs:43-59 is only invoked from the Simulation ctor and BirthEvent), so boats never age or die of old age. There is no fleet cap anywhere. At 1 tickâ‰ˆ1 min (FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:9,21) and TicksPerYear=250, 300 ticks â‰ˆ 5 sim-hours â†’ one free boat every 5 hours, forever, per dock.
    IMPACT:   Every other production loop carries ongoing cost: births cost 20 food (BirthFoodCost) plus permanent 1 food/citizen/period upkeep, extractors need staffed workers. Boats cost nothing after the one-time dock. Over the game's intended multi-day 'geological time', the fleet is unbounded. Concretely exploitable: each boat is a radius-3 water vision source (Sight.RadiusFor default=3) â†’ permanent free water scouting with zero upkeep; and up to 50 free 40-HP hulls (MovementConstants.cs:13 MaxUnitsPerTile=50) can be parked on a 1-wide strait tile to wall off all passage at no cost.
    FIX:      core-touching: add a per-boat material draw at production (e.g. consume Wood from the dock owner's nearest stockpile/castle in BoatProductionTickEvent before spawning, stalling like the slip-occupied path when materials are absent), and/or a per-player fleet cap, and/or count boats toward a (cheaper) upkeep sink. The doc's 'expensive to build, pays off permanently' should mean the dock is the cost â€” but an unbounded free fleet is not 'pays off', it's runaway.
    VERIFY:   Every cited mechanic verified. StructureCatalog.cs:157-173 Dock = 200 Wood + 50 Stone, BuildDurationTicks=200, RequiredBuilderCount=2, ProductionPeriodTicks=300. BoatProductionTickEvent.cs:48-65 spawns a boat via bare world.AddUnit with zero material/worker/buffer cost and reschedules at sim.Now+300 indefinitely. GameWorld.cs:146-151 BumpPopulationCount returns early for UnitRole.Boat, so boats never enter Player.PopulationCount; FoodConsumption.cs:60-61,180-181 computes the food rate strictly from PopulationCount, so boats incur zero food upkeep. Population.cs:43-59 ScheduleLifespan is the only DeathTick writer and is called only from the Simulation ctor and BirthEvent, so boats get no DeathByAgeEvent and are immortal. I grep-confirmed there is NO fleet cap anywhere. Sight.RadiusFor(UnitRole) returns 3 for any non-Scout role including Boat, and MovementConstants.MaxUnitsPerTile=50 with BaseHealth=40, so the free-vision and strait-wall exploits are real. PopulationConfig default TicksPerYear=250 corroborates the 300-tick~5-hour cadence. Mitigations worth noting (don't change the verdict): the Dock is by far the most expensive buildable (next is School at 80 Wood) and production is throttled to one hull per 5 sim-hours; but the unbounded, upkeep-free, never-dying, free-vision nature over geological time genuinely breaks the 'presence as investment' / 'everything has upkeep' invariants. High stands.

  [MEDIUM] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) A unit dying on a dock's slip permanently stalls boat production
    EVIDENCE: Boat production stalls when the slip is occupied (BoatProductionTickEvent.cs:40-46 sets ProductionArmed=false, NextProductionTickSeq=null). The only re-arm trigger is DockArmer.OnUnitLeftTile, which is called from exactly one place: MoveArrivalEvent.cs:65 (on a move arrival, for the tile just left). CombatRules.OnUnitDeath (CombatRules.cs:70-149) removes the unit from world.Units but never calls OnUnitLeftTile; neither do the age/starvation death paths.
    IMPACT:   Reachable in normal play: the first auto-produced boat spawns on the slip (BoatProductionTickEvent.cs:52, Position=dock.Slip) and, if the player doesn't move it, stalls the next production tick. If that boat is then destroyed by a coastal raid while still on the slip, the slip clears but no re-arm fires, so the dock is dormant forever. (Also triggers if any foot unit standing on the slip â€” water is foot-passable â€” dies there of combat/age/starvation.)
    FIX:      core-touching: call DockArmer.OnUnitLeftTile(sim, unit.Position) from CombatRules.OnUnitDeath (and DeathByAge/Starvation paths) after removal, mirroring the MoveArrivalEvent hook. Cheap and localized.
    VERIFY:   Verified. BoatProductionTickEvent.cs:40-46 stalls (ProductionArmed=false, NextProductionTickSeq=null) when the slip is occupied at fire time. I grep-confirmed DockArmer.OnUnitLeftTile has exactly ONE production caller: MoveArrivalEvent.cs:65 (the only re-arm trigger). CombatRules.OnUnitDeath (CombatRules.cs:70-149) removes the unit from world.Units and never calls OnUnitLeftTile/ArmIfDormant; neither do the age/starvation death paths. Reachable in normal play: the first auto-produced boat spawns on the slip (line 52, Position=dock.Slip); if not moved, the tick at +300 stalls; if that boat is then killed by a coastal raid while on the slip, the slip clears but no re-arm fires and the dock is dormant forever. Note boats can't die of age/starvation (immortal per finding 1), so the boat-on-slip death path is specifically combat (a power-1 foot unit takes ~400 ticks to chew 40 HP â€” feasible); the same stall also applies to any foot unit that dies on the slip (water is foot-passable). Also worth flagging: even GroupArrivalEvent doesn't call OnUnitLeftTile, so the normal re-arm path is itself incomplete. Medium confirmed.

  [MEDIUM] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) Foot units wade across water at 250/tile, contradicting boats.md 'un-invadable by sea'
    EVIDENCE: boats.md:51-54 asserts 'an isolated coast with no allies is un-invadable by sea in the MVP'. But Biome.cs:33 keeps Water=250 as a passable (non-Impassable) foot cost; Road.EffectiveCost (Road.cs:38-46) returns that biome cost for water; Pathfinding.cs:48 only skips tiles whose cost >= Impassable. So a Traversal.Foot army can path straight across any water at 250/tile with no dock and no boat. BoatMovementCost.cs:22-27 makes water Impassable only for boats, not the reverse.
    IMPACT:   The dock-gated-landing pillar (presence-as-investment; sea invasion requires allies or a captured dock) is bypassable: infantry can simply walk onto an enemy coast across narrow water. For a 10-tile strait that's ~2500 ticks (~42h) â€” slow but viable in geological time, and the wading army faces zero naval opposition (see naval-combat-cannot-sink). It also lets enemy foot units stand on a dock's water slip. The deferral is acknowledged in Biome.cs's own comment, but boats.md ships the strategic claim as if water were a real barrier.
    FIX:      Either reconcile the doc (drop/qualify the 'un-invadable by sea' claim) or make deep/most water Impassable to Foot (a per-tile 'deep water' flag set at worldgen, Impassable for Foot, cost-6 for Water) so the dock genuinely gates coastal access. This is the cheapest way to make boats strategically necessary rather than a convenience.
    VERIFY:   Verified end to end. boats.md:51-54 does assert an isolated coast is 'un-invadable by sea in the MVP'. Biome.cs:33 keeps Water=250 (a finite cost, not Biomes.Impassable=int.MaxValue at Biome.cs:20). TileGrid.TerrainCost (TileGrid.cs:30) returns Biomes.MoveCost, and Road.EffectiveCost (Road.cs:38-46) falls through to that biome cost on water. Pathfinding.cs:48 only skips tiles with cost >= Impassable, so 250-cost water is enterable by a Traversal.Foot unit â€” confirmed by BoatsTests.cs:80 ('a foot unit can also find it (water is cost 250)'). So foot armies can wade onto an enemy coast with no dock/boat, contradicting the doc. Two fair caveats that keep it at medium (not higher): the cost is brutal (a 10-tile strait ~ 2500 ticks ~ 42 sim-hours; only narrow 1-2 tile straits are practical), and Biome.cs:28-32 explicitly documents water-as-passable-250 as a deliberate placeholder pending 'real water mechanics' â€” an acknowledged deferral, not a hidden bug. Still a real doc/code contradiction that bypasses the dock-gated-landing pillar on narrow water. Medium holds.

  [MEDIUM] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) Boats can't sink each other and lock into a non-terminating combat loop
    EVIDENCE: UnitCombatCatalog.cs:36 â€” Boat BasePower=0 (BaseHealth=40). CombatRules.ForcePower/GatherForcesOnTile (CombatRules.cs:32,52) exclude embarked passengers, so a loaded transport's force is the boat's power = 0. CombatTrigger.cs:27-49 starts combat whenever two hostile owners share a tile (boats qualify). In CombatRoundEvent.cs:65-97, each owner's damage is the sum of hostile counterparts' start-power = 0, so line 74 `if (damage <= 0) continue` applies â€” no deaths; the post-damage re-gather (lines 81-92) still finds both boats present and hostile, so it reschedules another CombatRoundEvent at now+RoundIntervalTicks (CombatConfig.cs:13 default=10) indefinitely.
    IMPACT:   Two hostile boats meeting on a water tile generate a perpetual 0-damage combat that never resolves â€” a scheduled-event leak that, on a server running for days, churns endlessly (escapable only by a player manually sailing a boat away). More importantly there is no naval interdiction at all: you cannot sink an enemy boat with your own boats, so an attacker's transport fleet is completely uninterceptable at sea. The only way to damage a boat is to wade a foot unit (power 1) onto its water tile.
    FIX:      core-touching: either give boats nonzero combat power (or a ram/PowerModifier) so sea battles resolve, or make combat ignore force pairs whose max EffectivePower is 0 (don't start in CombatTrigger / end immediately in CombatRoundEvent) so two inert boats don't spin forever. The design already lists 'sea combat from adjacent water' as future work â€” at minimum stop the infinite loop now.
    VERIFY:   Verified. UnitCombatCatalog.cs:36 Boat BasePower=0, BaseHealth=40. CombatRules.cs:32,52 (ForcePower, GatherForcesOnTile) skip IsEmbarked, so a loaded transport's force = the boat's own power = 0. CombatTrigger.cs:27-29 adds every on-tile unit's owner (boats included, no power filter), so two hostile boats on a water tile start combat. In CombatRoundEvent.cs:59-75 startPower for a boat-only owner is 0, damage = sum of hostile counterparts' startPower = 0, and line 74 'if (damage <= 0) continue' means no Health is removed; the post-damage re-gather (lines 81-92) still finds both boats present + hostile and reschedules at now+RoundIntervalTicks (CombatConfig.cs:13 default=10) forever. The non-terminating 0-damage loop is a real, unintended scheduled-event leak. Caveat: the loop is bounded (one self-rescheduling event per 10 ticks per contested tile, not exponential), and the broader 'no naval interdiction' claim is partly intended â€” boats.md:253-256,279-281 explicitly defers sea-combat-from-adjacent and 'embarked passengers contribute force' to future milestones. The genuine defect is the perpetual loop, not the design choice; medium is appropriate.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=low) EmbarkIntent doesn't bump AssignmentEpoch as the design requires
    EVIDENCE: boats.md:168-173 specifies embark must 'Bump each passenger's AssignmentEpoch (any in-flight solo events fence-out)'. EmbarkIntent.cs:85-97 instead relies on p.TrySetActivity(Activity.Idle) (line 94), and Unit.TrySetActivity only bumps the epoch when Activity actually changes (Unit.cs:145-153). For the normal case â€” a passenger standing Idle on the dock â€” no bump occurs, and the TrySetActivity return value is unchecked. DisembarkIntent.cs:67 by contrast calls p.BumpEpoch() explicitly.
    IMPACT:   Currently harmless because an Idle unit has no live per-unit movement/haul events (embark also nulls PathRemaining/NextArrival* on lines 89-92), and grouped/breeding units are rejected. But it's a latent fence gap and an asymmetry with disembark; if a future Activity ever leaves a pending fence-able event while a unit is Idle on a dock, the stale event would not be invalidated.
    FIX:      Call p.BumpEpoch() unconditionally per passenger in EmbarkIntent (matching DisembarkIntent), and check the TrySetActivity result. Trivial, defensive.
    VERIFY:   Verified. boats.md:172-173 specifies embark must 'Bump each passenger's AssignmentEpoch (any in-flight solo events fence-out).' EmbarkIntent.cs:94 instead calls p.TrySetActivity(Activity.Idle) with the return value unchecked, and Unit.TrySetActivity (Unit.cs:145-153) only bumps AssignmentEpoch when Activity actually changes (line 151 'if (changed)'). For a passenger already Idle on the dock, Idle->Idle is no change, so no bump â€” confirmed asymmetry with DisembarkIntent.cs:66 which calls p.BumpEpoch() unconditionally. Confirmed harmless today: EmbarkIntent.cs:89-93 explicitly nulls PathRemaining/PathFinalDest/NextArrivalTick/NextArrivalSeq/HaulPlan, and any non-Idle passenger (e.g. Hauling/Moving) WOULD trip the activity-change bump anyway, so the only un-bumped case is an Idle unit that by definition has no live fence-able per-unit event. A latent fence gap + spec deviation, not an active bug. Low confirmed.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=low) CombatTrigger counts embarked passengers' frozen Position, unlike every other combat read
    EVIDENCE: Embark leaves a passenger's Position at the dock tile (EmbarkIntent.cs:74,85-97 never clears Position; off-tile-ness is expressed only via IsEmbarked). CombatTrigger.MaybeBeginCombatOnTile (CombatTrigger.cs:27-31) builds the owner set with `if (u.Position == tile) owners.Add(u.OwnerId)` and does NOT skip IsEmbarked â€” whereas ForcePower (CombatRules.cs:32), GatherForcesOnTile (CombatRules.cs:52), CountUnitsOnTile (MovementCost.cs:41) and View (View.cs:75,148) all skip embarked.
    IMPACT:   After a boat sails away, its passengers stay frozen at the original (land) dock tile. An enemy arriving on that dock tile makes CombatTrigger see two owners and start a combat; the first CombatRoundEvent re-gathers via GatherForcesOnTile (which excludes embarked), finds only one real force, and ends it. So it self-corrects to a one-shot no-op â€” no damage to the off-tile passengers (no dupe/loss) â€” but it's an inconsistency that creates spurious combat state.
    FIX:      Add `if (u.IsEmbarked) continue;` to the CombatTrigger owner scan for consistency with the rest of the combat/vision/crowding reads.
    VERIFY:   Verified. EmbarkIntent.cs:85-97 sets EmbarkedOn and clears path/haul anchors but never clears Position, so a passenger stays frozen at the dock tile. CombatTrigger.cs:27-29 builds the owner set with 'if (u.Position == tile) owners.Add(u.OwnerId)' and does NOT skip IsEmbarked â€” whereas ForcePower (CombatRules.cs:32), GatherForcesOnTile (CombatRules.cs:52), CountUnitsOnTile (MovementCost.cs:41) and View (View.cs:77,148; cited as 75 but present) all skip embarked. So after a boat sails off, an enemy arriving on the old dock tile makes the trigger see two owners and schedule round 1; the first CombatRoundEvent.GatherForcesOnTile excludes the embarked passenger, finds a single real owner, and ends combat (CombatRoundEvent.cs:51-55). Self-corrects to a one-shot no-op: no damage to off-tile passengers, no dupe/loss. The spurious CombatState lasts at most one RoundIntervalTicks and a re-gather still picks up any real defender, so no functional harm beyond the transient inconsistency. Low is correct.

  [LOW] (missing-feature | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=medium) Boat 100-unit cargo hold is unreachable dead config
    EVIDENCE: BoatConstants.cs:13 sets DefaultCargoCapacity=100 and the boat is spawned with it (BoatProductionTickEvent.cs:58). But the only writers of a unit's CargoResource/CargoAmount are HaulPickupEvent (HaulPickupEvent.cs:120-121) and snapshot restore. HaulIntent requires the hauler to walk to a structure/ground-pile source and a structure dest (HaulIntent.cs:53-60); a Traversal.Water boat cannot path onto any land structure tile (land is Impassable for it), and no intent targets a boat as a cargo source/sink. So no code path ever loads or unloads a boat's hold.
    IMPACT:   boats.md:274-279 promises 'a boat with passengers can still hold cargo ... move bulk over water'. In practice the only cargo that crosses water is the 1-unit load each embarked passenger already carries (CargoCapacity default 1, untouched by embark). The boat's 100-capacity hold is serialized (Snapshot.cs:202) butæ°¸è¿œ unusable â€” pure dead weight that misleads readers into thinking bulk sea freight exists.
    FIX:      Either implement a LoadBoat/UnloadBoat intent at a dock (boat on slip + structure on dock tile transfer goods to/from the hull) to deliver the promised bulk-freight loop, or remove DefaultCargoCapacity/the boat cargo claim until that milestone. As-is it's a missing feature dressed as a present one.
    VERIFY:   The dead-config fact is real: BoatConstants.cs:13 DefaultCargoCapacity=100, set on every boat (BoatProductionTickEvent.cs:58) and serialized (Snapshot.cs:363-364). I grep-confirmed the ONLY production write that LOADS cargo is HaulPickupEvent.cs:120-121 (other writes â€” CombatRules.cs:119, HaulDepositEvent.cs:91 â€” only zero it). HaulIntent.cs:53-60 requires a structure/ground source and a structure dest; a Traversal.Water boat cannot path onto any land structure tile, so the hold is effectively unloadable (a narrow theoretical exception: a boat already standing on a water-tile ground-pile could pick up, but could never deposit since the dest must be a land structure â€” circular/unreachable). However, severity medium is overstated and the 'broken promise / misleads readers' framing is wrong: boats.md's relevant text (lines 268-279) is the OUT OF SCOPE / intentionally-deferred section, which explicitly says 'Mixed-good Holdings on a single boat is a separate refactor ... not here.' So the 100-capacity is deliberate forward-scaffolding for a deferred feature (like the empty Unit.Buffs list or the append-ready Traversal enum), not dead weight contradicting a shipped contract. The 'move bulk over water' wording is a code comment, not a design promise. Downgraded to low/partial.

---------------------------------------------------------------------

##### Groups & Caravans  [key=groups-caravans]
SUMMARY: The Group layer is a clean, deterministic movement-grouping primitive â€” atomic multi-member arrival, epoch-fenced retask/disband, snapshot/restore coverage, and presence-based combat so a stationary escort genuinely auto-fights with no special-case code. But measured against design Â§7.2, it is a stub of the caravan vision: carts (capacity), horses (speed), per-member pace, and load/weight are entirely unmodeled, and â€” most damningly â€” grouped units cannot haul, so a "caravan" physically carries nothing. Several edge cases (member death during Forming, group-id reuse, boats in groups) are unguarded logic holes. The Â§7 logistics/caravan/capture loop is therefore largely unrealized at the group level even though its lower-level primitives (cargo-drop-on-death, ground-pile haul source) exist.
STRENGTHS:
  + Atomic group arrival with correct per-member side effects :: GroupArrivalEvent updates every member's position in one event and fires road-credit and vision-reveal once per member (GroupArrivalEvent.cs:57-64), so a 3-member caravan credits the road 3x and diminishing returns stack naturally inside the burst (verified by GroupMovementTests.GroupMove_CreditsRoad_PerMember). This is exactly the 'group moves as one' semantic done cleanly.
  + Epoch-fenced retask/disband mirrors the proven Unit pattern :: Group.MovementEpoch is bumped on every MoveGroupIntent and Disband (Group.cs:53-57, MoveGroupIntent.cs:68, DisbandGroupIntent.cs:31); in-flight GroupArrivalEvents fence on mismatch (GroupArrivalEvent.cs:32-36). Retask and disband-mid-flight are covered by tests (MoveRetask_BumpsEpoch_OldChainFences, Disband_MovingGroup_FencesArrival). Consistent with Unit.AssignmentEpoch â€” low cognitive overhead.
  + Presence-based combat makes escort auto-fight with zero special-case code (when stationary) :: ForcePower pools by owner on a tile and explicitly ignores group membership (CombatRules.cs:27-38); CombatTrigger only checks co-located hostile owners (CombatTrigger.cs:26-49). A stationary caravan's escort soldiers fight automatically because they're present â€” delivering Â§7.2's 'no separate caravan-combat system' for the arrived case.
  + Full snapshot/restore + queue regeneration for Forming and Moving groups :: Group anchors mirror Unit anchors and RegenerateQueue rebuilds the in-flight GroupArrivalEvent from pure state (RegenerateQueue.cs:159-169); Forming and Moving groups both round-trip to identical hashes (GroupFormationTests.Form_ThenSnapshotRoundTrips, GroupMovementTests.MovingGroup_SnapshotMidFlight_RestoreReachesSameHash). Determinism-across-crash is genuinely preserved.
  + Clean atomic-formation and solo-intent-lockout invariants :: FormGroupIntent re-validates every member at resolve time and rejects the whole intent on any failure â€” no partial formation (FormGroupIntent.cs:39-69, tested NonexistentMember_Rejected_NoMembershipChanges). Grouped units are uniformly locked out of MoveIntent/HaulIntent/Assign* (MoveIntent.cs:19-20, HaulIntent.cs:37-38), preventing a member being driven by two controllers at once.
  + Capture-economy primitives are actually wired at the unit level :: OnUnitDeath drops a laden unit's cargo to a per-tile GroundResources pile (CombatRules.cs:108-120) and HaulIntent can source from that ground pile, not just structures (HaulIntent.cs:52-58). The Â§7.3 'capture not destruction' loop's lower half exists â€” once caravans can actually carry goods (see caravan-cannot-haul), the raiding pickup path is ready.
FINDINGS (kept=9, refuted/dropped=0):

  [HIGH] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) A Forming group is permanently stuck if any rendezvous-walker dies, fails to path, or cap-yields before arriving
    EVIDENCE: PendingArrivals is set once in FormGroupIntent (FormGroupIntent.cs:85) and decremented ONLY in MoveArrivalEvent.DispatchOnFinalArrival when a member reaches the rendezvous (MoveArrivalEvent.cs:135-147). OnUnitDeath removes a dead member from Members and disbands only if Members hits zero, but never touches PendingArrivals (CombatRules.cs:122-128). MoveArrivalEvent's cap-yield path returns Idle before the dispatch (MoveArrivalEvent.cs:48-59), and BeginMove silently clears anchors if no path is found (MoveIntent.cs:121-128) â€” neither decrements PendingArrivals. The only Formingâ†’Idle transition in the codebase is that single decrement (grep GroupState.Forming). Forming groups reject MoveGroupIntent (MoveGroupIntent.cs:36-37), so the only escape is Disband.
    IMPACT:   Forming members walk to the rendezvous as individual units (FormGroupIntent.cs:94-102), fully exposed to piecemeal ambush, the per-tile cap, and pathfinding failure. If a walker dies en route (very plausible â€” that's exactly the ambush the game is about), PendingArrivals can never reach 0, so the group is frozen in Forming forever: unmovable, with its surviving members locked out of solo intents (GroupId still set). The player's only recourse is to Disband and start over. Reachability is also checked with Road.EffectiveCost (FormGroupIntent.cs:61-65) while the actual walk uses fog-aware PlanCost (MoveIntent.cs:114-120), so a member can pass the check yet fail to path, stranding the group from the start.
    FIX:      core-touching: decrement PendingArrivals (or recompute it from members present at the rendezvous) whenever a Forming member is removed (OnUnitDeath), cap-yields, or fails to path; transition to Idle when the count reaches zero with at least one member present. Add a Forming timeout/abort, and use the same cost function for the reachability check and the actual walk.
    VERIFY:   Verified and serious. PendingArrivals is set once (FormGroupIntent.cs:85) and the ONLY Forming->Idle transition is the decrement in MoveArrivalEvent.cs:140-146 (confirmed by grep: GroupArrivalEvent's Idle-sets at 49/83 are for Moving groups only; MoveGroupIntent.cs:47 is already-at-dest). OnUnitDeath (CombatRules.cs:122-128) removes the dead member and disbands only at zero members, never decrementing PendingArrivals. The cap-yield path (MoveArrivalEvent.cs:48-59) and BeginMove no-path (MoveIntent.cs:121-128) both return without decrementing. Forming members walk solo (FormGroupIntent.cs:101) fully exposed to ambush. So a rendezvous-walker dying / cap-yielding / failing to path freezes the group in Forming forever (MoveGroupIntent.cs:36-37 rejects moves while Forming); survivors keep GroupId set so solo intents reject them â€” only escape is Disband. No test covers a Forming-member death. The reachability/walk cost mismatch (FormGroupIntent.cs:61-65 uses Road.EffectiveCost; MoveIntent uses PlanCost) is a real but narrow extra trigger (only cap-saturated tiles introduce an Impassable the reachability check missed). Core bug is high.

  [HIGH] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=high) Group ids are reused after disband (max+1), enabling a stale GroupArrivalEvent to drive a reformed group
    EVIDENCE: NextGroupId returns max(existing keys)+1 (FormGroupIntent.cs:107-114), so disbanding group 1 frees id 1 for the next Form. This directly contradicts two explicit invariants: Group.cs:56-57 ('Group ids never reuse â€” that would break stale GroupArrivalEvents from a defunct group firing on a new one') and GameWorld.cs:26-29 ('ids ... increment monotonically across the world's lifetime'). DisbandGroupIntent removes the group and bumps its epoch but does NOT cancel the queued GroupArrivalEvent (DisbandGroupIntent.cs:30-52); the engine relies on epoch fencing (GroupArrivalEvent.cs:32-36). A reformed group starts at MovementEpoch 0 (Group.cs:53) and reaches epoch 1 after one MoveGroupIntent â€” the same ExpectedEpoch the old chain's first hop carried, with the same reused id.
    IMPACT:   Disband a moving group with a hop event still queued, then quickly Form+Move a new group that takes the freed id: the stale event's (GroupId=1, ExpectedEpoch=1) can match the new group's (id=1, epoch=1), so GroupArrivalEvent.Apply fires on the NEW group â€” teleporting all its members to the old chain's destination tile, crediting road, triggering combat, and corrupting its path. It is exactly the failure the code comments claim is prevented. Unlike units (which use a monotonic GameWorld.NextUnitId, GameWorld.cs:76), groups have no such counter.
    FIX:      core-touching: add a monotonic GameWorld.NextGroupId counter (mirroring NextUnitId), allocate from it, persist it in the snapshot, and never reuse ids â€” or have DisbandGroupIntent explicitly cancel the queued GroupArrivalEvent. Add a twin-run regression for disband-then-immediate-reform with an in-flight hop.
    VERIFY:   Verified. NextGroupId (FormGroupIntent.cs:107-114) returns max(keys)+1, so disbanding the sole/highest group frees its id for reuse â€” directly contradicting Group.cs:56-57 and GameWorld.cs:26-29 ('never reuse'/'monotonic across lifetime'); units by contrast use the monotonic GameWorld.NextUnitId (GameWorld.cs:76). DisbandGroupIntent.cs:30-52 bumps epoch and removes the group but does not cancel the queued GroupArrivalEvent, relying purely on epoch fencing. Traced the epoch math: old group form->epoch0, one MoveGroupIntent->epoch1 (queued event ExpectedEpoch=1); disband->epoch2 then removed. New group reusing id 1 starts epoch0 (Group.cs:53) and reaches epoch1 after one MoveGroupIntent. GroupArrivalEvent.Apply (32-36) then matches (id=1, ExpectedEpoch=1) against the new group (id=1, epoch=1) and executes â€” teleporting members to the old destination, popping the new group's PathRemaining, crediting road, triggering combat. This is exactly the failure the comments claim is prevented. No test covers id reuse. Window is specific but fully reachable in async play (events fire over hours); fix is a monotonic group-id counter like NextUnitId. High stands.

  [HIGH] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) A group/caravan cannot carry any goods â€” grouped units reject all haul/load intents
    EVIDENCE: HaulIntent.Resolve rejects any unit with a GroupId (HaulIntent.cs:37-38: 'hauler {HaulerId} is in group'); AssignWorkers/AssignBuilders skip grouped units (GroupDisbandTests.cs:169-207). FormGroupIntent requires every member to be Activity.Idle (FormGroupIntent.cs:46-47), and the haul pipeline always ends by depositing and zeroing cargo (HaulDepositEvent / HaulIntent.cs:62-80) â€” there is no 'pick up and hold' intent. The Group class stores only Members/Position/State (Group.cs:22-62); there is no group cargo field. So there is no code path by which a formed group ever holds CargoAmount > 0.
    IMPACT:   Design Â§7.1/Â§7.2 makes a caravan a group of porters that physically carry resources. In the actual sim a caravan is a pure movement-grouping that transports zero goods: you cannot load it, and its members cannot haul while grouped. The only way to move resources remains a SOLO HaulIntent (one unit, one trip), which has no escort, no group, and no capacity pooling. The entire reason caravans exist â€” hauling under protection â€” is unreachable.
    FIX:      core-touching: add a group-haul flow. Options: (a) allow a member's CargoResource/CargoAmount to be set by a LoadGroupIntent at the group's tile (drawing from a co-located stockpile/ground pile), and let GroupArrivalEvent carry that cargo; or (b) introduce a GroupHaulIntent that assigns porter members a HaulPlan executed collectively. Either way the deposit-on-arrival must write to the destination structure. Without this, Â§7 logistics is non-functional.
    VERIFY:   Verified: HaulIntent.cs:37-38 rejects any hauler with GroupId; FormGroupIntent.cs:46 requires Activity.Idle; Group.cs has no cargo field; grep of Groups/ for cargo/load/deposit returns nothing; AssignWorkers/AssignBuilders skip grouped units (GroupDisbandTests 191-207). There is genuinely no group-level load or deposit path, so the designed caravan-hauling workflow (Â§7.2: porters carry resources under escort) is unreachable â€” high severity stands. One sub-claim is overstated: 'no code path by which a formed group holds CargoAmount>0' is technically false. MoveIntent.cs:41-42 keeps cargo on a Hauling unit when retasked, so a laden unit can become Idle and then be Formed (the Idle check passes), and GroupArrivalEvent.cs:57-64 moves that member's position each hop â€” its pre-held cargo physically rides along. But this convoluted path still cannot deposit-as-a-group, so the finding's conclusion (caravans can't function as coordinated haulers) holds.

  [HIGH] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) Carts (capacity), horses (speed), and load/weight are not modeled â€” the speed/capacity/protection tradeoff does not exist
    EVIDENCE: Â§7.2 promises 'porters, carts (capacity), horses (speed), and escort soldiers ... biome cost hits carts harder than foot â€” so speed vs. capacity vs. protection falls out naturally.' Grep for horse|cart|weight|SpeedMultiplier|slowest|heaviest across Sim.Core returns only aspirational COMMENTS in Group.cs:3 and MoveGroupIntent.cs:13-14 â€” no entities, no fields. Unit has only CargoCapacity (init=1, Unit.cs:28) and Traversal (Foot/Water, Unit.cs:33); UnitRole has no Cart/Horse (Unit.cs:4-15). There is no per-unit movement multiplier and no per-biome-per-traversal cost beyond Foot vs Water.
    IMPACT:   The central caravan decision the design is built around (haul more slowly with carts, faster with horses, protected by escort) has no representation in the simulation. Every unit pays identical Foot cost, so assembling a 'caravan' confers no capacity, no speed change, and no terrain tradeoff â€” there is nothing to optimize. The composite-entity vision is absent; only the bag-of-unit-ids exists.
    FIX:      core-touching: introduce cart/horse as either roles or per-unit modifiers (e.g. SpeedFactor + per-biome multiplier table) and make MoveGroupIntent's cost the true max over members. Even a minimal 'cart = +capacity, âˆ’speed on rough biomes; horse = +speed' would make caravans a real decision instead of a label.
    VERIFY:   Verified against code: UnitRole enum (Unit.cs:4-15) has no Cart/Horse; Unit has only CargoCapacity (init=1, Unit.cs:28) and Traversal Foot/Water (Unit.cs:33); MovementCost.TerrainCostFor (74-79) branches only Water vs Road.EffectiveCost(Foot) â€” no per-unit speed multiplier, no per-biome-per-traversal table beyond Foot/Water. Design Â§7.2 (persistent-rts-design.md:259-262) explicitly promises carts/horses/escort with a speed-vs-capacity-vs-protection tradeoff. That tradeoff has no representation. Caveat noted: MoveGroupIntent.cs:11-15 frames it as acknowledged future work, but the central caravan decision is absent, so high severity for the design-promise gap is defensible.

  [MEDIUM] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=medium) Non-Foot units (boats) can be added to a group and are then moved with Foot pathing/cost
    EVIDENCE: FormGroupIntent eligibility checks owner/Idle/not-grouped/not-embarked but NOT Traversal (FormGroupIntent.cs:40-52). A Boat (Role=Boat, Traversal=Water, Unit.cs:14,33) sitting Idle on a water tile is therefore form-eligible. MoveGroupIntent computes the path and hop cost with the default Traversal.Foot (MoveGroupIntent.cs:58-60, 121), so the group routes over land using Road/biome Foot costs â€” whereas a solo boat's BoatMovementCost makes land Impassable (MovementCost.cs:74-79). GroupArrivalEvent moves every member to the land tile unconditionally (GroupArrivalEvent.cs:57-64).
    IMPACT:   A boat dragged into a foot group walks onto land, violating the water-only traversal contract that solo boat movement enforces. Even setting aside boats, the group cost ignoring per-member Traversal is the same root gap as the pace-of-slowest hole â€” the engine never consults member traversal when pricing or pathing a group.
    FIX:      core-touching: reject mixed-traversal groups in FormGroupIntent (or forbid Boat membership), and make MoveGroupIntent derive the group's traversal/cost from its members (Impassable if members disagree). Add a test forming a boat+foot group and asserting rejection.
    VERIFY:   Verified. FormGroupIntent.cs:40-52 checks owner/Idle/not-grouped/not-embarked but never Traversal or Role, so an Idle ungrouped Boat (Traversal.Water, Unit.cs:14,33) is form-eligible. MoveGroupIntent.cs:60,121 price/path with the default Foot, and GroupArrivalEvent.cs:57-64 moves every member onto the land tile unconditionally â€” whereas a solo boat is blocked because BoatMovementCost.cs makes all land Impassable. Net effect: a boat dragged into a foot group walks onto land, and once disembarked there it is stranded (solo MoveIntent finds no water path off land). Real contract violation and the same per-member-traversal-ignored root as the pace-of-slowest hole. Somewhat contrived to trigger (player must mix a boat into a land group), but a genuine validation gap with a real consequence; medium is acceptable.

  [MEDIUM] (balance | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=medium) An in-transit caravan is not pinned by combat and the first round is delayed, so the escort barely fights an ambush
    EVIDENCE: GroupArrivalEvent.Apply triggers combat then immediately schedules the next hop (GroupArrivalEvent.cs:73-88) â€” movement is not stopped. CombatTrigger always schedules round 1 at now+RoundIntervalTicks (CombatTrigger.cs:46-48); RoundIntervalTicks defaults to 10 (CombatConfig.cs:13). A Grassland hop costs 10 (Biomes.MoveCost Grassland=10) with no crowding penalty for â‰¤3 units (MovementConstants.cs:24). Units are health 10 / power 1 (UnitCombatCatalog.cs:24-31). Design Â§9.2 specifies 'instant melee on contact resolves in the engagement event,' but no code path resolves a round at trigger time â€” combat is always the delayed self-rescheduling loop.
    IMPACT:   Because the caravan keeps walking on its pre-committed chain and the first combat round is delayed a full interval, a Moving caravan typically eats at most one round of chip damage (a few HP across many 10-HP units) before sliding off the contested tile and ending the fight by absence. Â§7.2's 'escort automatically fights when the caravan is ambushed' is true only for a STATIONARY/arrived group; a transiting caravan can largely walk through ambushes, and a raider can almost never kill laden units to trigger the Â§7.3 capture drop. The raiding economy is effectively unreachable in transit.
    FIX:      Either implement Â§9.2 instant-melee at trigger time, or pin units that arrive on a hostile tile (suspend their movement chain until combat ends), or schedule round 1 at the trigger tick. Re-tune combat numbers so a meaningful ambush can actually attrit an unescorted caravan within the time it spends on a tile.
    VERIFY:   Verified. GroupArrivalEvent.cs:73 triggers combat then :88 immediately schedules the next hop â€” movement is never halted. CombatTrigger.cs:44-49 only schedules round 1 at now+RoundIntervalTicks (=10, CombatConfig.cs:13); there is no instant resolution, contradicting design Â§9.2 'melee on contact resolves in the engagement event' (line 364). Traced event ordering: combat round is scheduled (lower Seq) before ScheduleNextHop; on Grassland (cost 10 = interval 10) both fire at T+10, combat first, then the group walks off â€” exactly one chip round (a few HP across 10-HP/1-power units), and on improved roads (cost<10) the group can leave before ANY round. Killing a 10-HP laden unit in one round needs ~10 power, so small raiders cannot trigger the Â§7.3 capture drop in transit. Nuance worth flagging: on slow terrain the escort fights more (Forest cost 30 = ~2 rounds, Mountain 45 = ~4), and a large raider stack can still kill in a single round, so 'raiding economy effectively unreachable' is strongest on the grassland/road routes caravans actually use. Medium is fair.

  [MEDIUM] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) Group move cost is not 'pace of the slowest member'; the class comment misrepresents the code, and small groups have zero size penalty
    EVIDENCE: MoveGroupIntent's header claims 'Path is computed using a GROUP cost delegate: max(memberCost(tile)) across members' (MoveGroupIntent.cs:8-15). The code never iterates members: Resolve uses a single PlanCost(world, tile, group.OwnerId, ...) with default Traversal.Foot (MoveGroupIntent.cs:54-60), and ScheduleNextHop uses ExecutionCost(world, group.Position, next, now) with default Foot (MoveGroupIntent.cs:121). The only size effect is source-crowding banding via CountUnitsOnTile (MovementCost.cs:131-133), and BandedCrowdingCost is +0 for 1-3 units (MovementConstants.cs:24-28). So a 2- or 3-member caravan moves at exactly solo speed; the first slowdown (+10 on Grassland base 10, i.e. 2x) only appears at 4 members and is a flat band, not pace-of-slowest.
    IMPACT:   The documented 'moves at the pace of the slowest/heaviest member' mechanic is not what runs. Today all members are Foot so the difference is latent, but the framework claim ('the framework handles it without engine refactor') is false â€” adding a slow unit type would NOT slow the group, because no per-member cost is ever evaluated. And the crowding-band proxy gives small caravans no size cost at all, so there is no incentive to keep caravans small/fast.
    FIX:      Implement the advertised max-over-members cost delegate in MoveGroupIntent (iterate Members, take max of each member's terrain+traversal cost), or delete the misleading comments and document the crowding-band model as the real one. Re-tune bands so a meaningful caravan size (e.g. 5-10 porters) carries a graded speed cost.
    VERIFY:   Verified: MoveGroupIntent.cs:60 and :121 both call PlanCost/ExecutionCost with the default Traversal.Foot and group.Position â€” members are never iterated, so the header comment's 'max(memberCost(tile)) across members' (lines 11-15) misrepresents the code. The only size effect is source-crowding via ExecutionCost->CountUnitsOnTile, and BandedCrowdingCost is +0 for 1-3 units (MovementConstants.cs:24-28), so 2-3 member caravans move at exactly solo speed; first band (+10) only at 4 members. The 'framework handles it without engine refactor' claim is indeed false: a slow unit type would not slow the group because no per-member cost is evaluated. Medium is correct â€” latent today (all Foot) but the documented mechanic does not run.

  [LOW] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=low) No Split/Merge/Add/Remove-member intents â€” a caravan cannot be reconfigured without full disband+reform
    EVIDENCE: Only FormGroupIntent, MoveGroupIntent, and DisbandGroupIntent exist (Groups/*). Several comments reference future operations that were never built: Unit.cs:101 ('cleared on DisbandGroupIntent (or future Split/Merge)'), MoveGroupIntent.cs:80 ('Split eventually might').
    IMPACT:   To drop an escort, peel off scouts, or add a porter, the player must Disband (losing the group and its id) and re-Form, which re-exposes scattered members to the solo-walk rendezvous (and the stuck-Forming hole above). A composite caravan that you can only create-or-destroy is far less useful than one you can adjust in place, especially in an async game where conditions change mid-haul.
    FIX:      Add AddMember/RemoveMember (and optionally SplitGroup) intents that mutate Members and clear/set GroupId without tearing down the group, reusing the existing epoch-fencing for any in-flight chain. Lower priority than the haul and stuck-Forming fixes.
    VERIFY:   Verified: only FormGroupIntent, MoveGroupIntent, DisbandGroupIntent exist under Groups/. Comments reference unbuilt operations (Unit.cs:98-101 'future Split/Merge'; MoveGroupIntent.cs:80 'Split eventually might'). Reconfiguring a caravan requires Disband+reform, which re-scatters members through the solo-walk rendezvous and re-exposes them to the stuck-Forming hole (finding 4). Legitimate low-severity missing-feature observation, especially compounding in an async game.

  [LOW] (unnecessary | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=low) MoveGroupIntent.BeginGroupMove is dead code with a thinking-out-loud comment left in source
    EVIDENCE: BeginGroupMove (MoveGroupIntent.cs:81-104) is never called anywhere (grep BeginGroupMove across the whole repo returns only its definition). Its doc comment is a literal self-correcting train of thought: 'Used by FormGroupIntent for off-rendezvous members â€” wait, no: members walk solo via MoveIntent.BeginMove. This is the group analogue ... Exposed for re-arm paths in future (e.g. Disband doesn't need it; Split eventually might).' (MoveGroupIntent.cs:77-80).
    IMPACT:   Dead, untested code that duplicates ScheduleNextHop/path-setup logic. It is a maintenance hazard (a second, divergent group-move entry point) and the comment signals the method was added speculatively for a Split feature that does not exist.
    FIX:      Delete BeginGroupMove (and the stray comment) until a Split/Merge feature actually needs it, or wire it in and test it. Keep the single move entry point (MoveGroupIntent.Resolve) authoritative.
    VERIFY:   Verified: grep for BeginGroupMove across the whole repo returns only its definition at MoveGroupIntent.cs:81 â€” never called. The doc comment (lines 77-80) is literal thinking-out-loud ('wait, no: members walk solo...', 'Split eventually might'). It duplicates the ScheduleNextHop/path-setup logic, so it is an untested divergent second group-move entry point. Low severity dead code, accurate.
