##### Engine, Event Queue & Scheduling  [key=engine-eventqueue]
SUMMARY: The discrete-event core is genuinely discrete-event, not a disguised global tick: Simulation.Run only pops scheduled events and sets Now=e.At, GameHost drives it with Run(until: virtualTick), and there is no time-driven or grid-driven world sweep anywhere in Sim.Core â€” the Â§2.2/Â§2.3 promises are honored and grep-verified by an explicit determinism audit. Ordering is deterministic and fair because the queue key (At, Seq) is a total order (Seq is unique+monotonic), sidestepping .NET PriorityQueue heap instability, and same-tick = submission order is pinned as a gameplay fairness property by tests. The main risks are operational rather than logical: two in-memory logs grow without bound in a server designed to run forever, one self-rescheduling event lacks the Seq fence its four siblings have, and the single shared RNG stream is a latent replay/patch-compat hazard. None of these break determinism today, but several are footguns the design's own long-horizon goals will eventually trip.
STRENGTHS:
  + Genuinely discrete-event, not a disguised global tick :: Simulation.Run (Simulation.cs:105-116) only pops scheduled events and sets Now=e.At; GameHost advances it with Run(until: virtualTick) (GameHost.cs:66) so idle time costs nothing. A grep over Sim.Core finds no time-loop or per-tile/per-unit world sweep, and the maintained determinism-audit.md Â§1 verifies the only Units/Structures.Values iterations are bounded, event-driven, or serialization. The Â§2.2/Â§2.3 promises (scale with decisions, one global queue, no per-player catch-up) are actually kept.
  + Total-order priority key defeats heap instability and encodes fairness :: EventQueue keys on (At, Seq) with Seq unique and monotonic (EventQueue.cs:7,11; Simulation.cs:67), so .NET PriorityQueue's lack of stability is irrelevant â€” there are never true ties. Same-tick = submission order is pinned not just as reproducibility but as a gameplay fairness property (who pulls the last unit of a buffer) by SameTickFairnessTests, including the swap-order-swaps-winner counter-test.
  + Owned xorshift64 RNG for runtime-stable replay :: Rng.cs deliberately reimplements xorshift64 instead of System.Random precisely because System.Random's algorithm changed across .NET versions; this lets the intent-log replay survive runtime upgrades, and the seed-0 normalization avoids the xorshift all-zero fixed point. Correct determinism hygiene for a game that bets on long-horizon replay.
  + Consistent fencing-token cancellation instead of queue mutation :: Rather than supporting expensive/error-prone removal from the priority queue, retasked/cancelled work is invalidated by anchor+Seq mismatch checked at fire time (CombatRoundEvent.cs:31, FamineCheckEvent.cs:29, BoatProductionTickEvent.cs:30, DeathByAgeEvent). Stale events fire and cleanly no-op. This is elegant, snapshot-friendly (RegenerateQueue rebuilds with original Seq), and bounded by retask rate.
  + Validate-at-resolution is cleanly structured :: IntentEvent wraps each intent so resolution is just another queued event (IntentEvent.cs:10), and IntentOutcome.Reject mutates nothing (IntentOutcome.cs, ScheduledEvent.Outcome default Applied). This makes the intent-validation.md contract ('re-verify all preconditions at resolution, mutate nothing on failure, fail clean') uniform across intents and consequence-events, and is what makes multiplayer same-tick contention fall out for free.
  + A real, maintained determinism audit accompanies the engine :: docs/determinism-audit.md enumerates the structural invariants with literal grep commands, per-milestone addenda, and an explicit 'what would break this, re-run the audit' trigger list. Few codebases keep their determinism contract this legible; it materially lowers the risk of a future change silently introducing a global sweep or unfenced event.
FINDINGS (kept=5, refuted/dropped=0):

  [HIGH] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) _resolvedLog and _intentLog grow forever in a server designed to never stop
    EVIDENCE: Simulation.cs:15-19 declares `_resolvedLog` (List<ScheduledEvent>) and `_intentLog` (List<(long,Intent)>). Simulation.cs:114 appends to `_resolvedLog` for EVERY event in Run; Simulation.cs:91 appends to `_intentLog` for every SubmitIntent. Nothing ever trims either list. The whole design (Â§2.3) is that the sim runs continuously regardless of logins, and self-rescheduling events fire forever: ProductionTickEvent every 10/15 ticks (StructureCatalog.cs:31,52), CombatRoundEvent every 10 (CombatConfig.cs:13), FamineCheckEvent every meal=60 (FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:21), BoatProductionTickEvent every 300 (StructureCatalog.cs:172). Each fire adds one permanent entry to `_resolvedLog`. The only production consumer, GameHost.HarvestRejections (GameHost.cs:114-131), reads via an absolute `_resolvedCursor` index and never trims. `_intentLog` is not read by GameHost or persistence at all â€” only by the Sim.Host debug CLI (Program.cs:144) and tests; the durable replay source is the SQLite intent store, not this list.
    IMPACT:   A persistent 'geological-time' world that runs for weeks will accumulate millions-to-billions of ScheduledEvent objects in `_resolvedLog` (one per production/combat/famine/boat tick across every structure) plus an Intent per command in `_intentLog`, until the host OOMs and the world dies. This directly defeats the headline property that the sim advances on its own schedule indefinitely. `_intentLog` is also pure dead weight in production â€” duplicating the durable store with no reader.
    FIX:      core-touching. Stop unconditionally retaining full history in the live Simulation: (a) replace `_resolvedLog` with either a bounded ring buffer or, better, an observer/callback the host subscribes to for rejection harvesting (and switch GameHost off the absolute `_resolvedCursor`, which silently breaks if the list is ever trimmed); (b) gate `_intentLog` behind a debug flag or remove it, since the SQLite store is the real replay source. Keep full-history retention only in explicit replay/test modes.
    VERIFY:   Code facts hold. Simulation.cs:15-19 declares both lists; :114 appends EVERY resolved event, :91 appends EVERY intent; nothing trims either. GameHost reads _resolvedLog via an ever-advancing absolute index _resolvedCursor (GameHost.cs:28,115) and never trims. _intentLog is read only by the Sim.Host debug CLI (Program.cs:144) and tests (DurableSubmitTests.cs:48, DeterminismTests.cs:39) â€” the server never touches it and DurableSubmit/SqliteIntentStore do not read it, so in production it is pure dead weight. Crucially, Sim.Server/Program.cs wires NO persistence/snapshot/Recovery â€” GameHost runs the Simulation purely in-memory, so there is no restart/restore cycle that ever resets these lists. With default tps=20 (ServerOptions.cs:8), production reschedules every 10/15 ticks (StructureCatalog.cs:31,52,69,90) and combat every 10 (CombatConfig.cs:13), so an active world accumulates events without bound until OOM, defeating the run-forever design. Two minor inaccuracies in the evidence, not the conclusion: (a) FamineCheckEvent is scheduled at the predicted dry-out tick (FoodConsumption.cs:147-159), NOT 'every meal=60'; (b) growth is proportional to actual resolved activity rather than raw wall-clock (a fully-idle world with all buffers full and no combat lets the queue drain and the log stop growing). Neither softens the core defect: zero reclamation in a server designed never to stop. High stands.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=partial | conf=medium | sev0=medium) Schedule's hard throw on past-time has no host-level containment â€” a single scheduling bug bricks the world silently
    EVIDENCE: Simulation.Schedule throws InvalidOperationException when at < Now (Simulation.cs:64-65), as does ScheduleWithSeq (Simulation.cs:82-83). This throw propagates out of event Apply / intent Resolve through Simulation.Run. GameHost.ClockLoop (GameHost.cs:63-68) calls `_sim.Run(until: _virtualTick)` inside `lock(_gate)` with NO try/catch. If any future code computes a past `at`, the background sim-clock thread dies, `_running` stays true, `_virtualTick` freezes, and the world silently stops advancing while the HTTP layer keeps serving stale views. The producers that could regress here defensively floor their times (Population.cs:55 `if (deathTick <= sim.Now) deathTick = sim.Now+1`; FoodConsumption.cs:156; FamineCheckEvent path), which is exactly the kind of guard whose absence in a new event would be fatal.
    IMPACT:   The engine's documented philosophy (intent-validation.md) is 'fail forward â€” the world stays valid, the queue still drains, no operator intervention.' Schedule's throw is a legitimate invariant tripwire, but the host does not contain its blast radius, so the failure mode is the opposite of fail-forward: a frozen world with no error surfaced to operator or players. For an async game where bugs surface hours later, a silently dead clock thread is the worst possible failure shape.
    FIX:      Non-core host fix (preferred): wrap the `_sim.Run` call in ClockLoop with a guarded catch that logs the offending event, stops the clock cleanly, and flags the world as halted so the operator is alerted instead of the thread vanishing. Optionally (core-touching) keep the throw but have Run surface a structured fault rather than an unhandled exception. Either way, no scheduling bug should be able to kill the clock thread invisibly.
    VERIFY:   The code facts hold: Schedule/ScheduleWithSeq throw InvalidOperationException on at<Now (Simulation.cs:64-65,82-83), and ClockLoop calls _sim.Run inside lock(_gate) with NO try/catch (GameHost.cs:63-68); the try/catch that exists is in the HTTP path (HttpApi.cs:41-71) and SubmitEnvelopeJson (GameHost.cs:78-92), not the clock. BUT the finding's central characterization â€” 'bricks the world SILENTLY,' 'clock thread dies, _running stays true, world silently stops while HTTP serves stale views,' 'worst possible silent failure shape' â€” is wrong. An unhandled exception escaping the entry method of a background Thread terminates the entire .NET process (IsBackground only affects shutdown, not exception handling), and there is no AppDomain.UnhandledException handler anywhere in Sim.Server (Program.cs and a grep confirm none). So the real failure is a LOUD whole-process crash (stack trace to stderr, clients get connection-refused), not a silent stale-serving freeze. The fail-forward 'add a defensive guard' kernel is fair, but the failure mode and 'medium' severity are overstated/refuted. (Separately â€” and not what the finding claims â€” a crash means total world loss because the live server wires no persistence; that is a different finding.) Downgraded to low.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=low) Run() with no bound assumes the queue eventually drains â€” undocumented and fragile
    EVIDENCE: Simulation.Run (Simulation.cs:105-116) loops `while (_queue.Count > 0)` when `until` is null. This terminates only because every self-rescheduling chain currently self-retires: production fills its finite buffer and goes dormant (ProductionTickEvent.cs:101-117), combat ends when one side dies and removes CombatStates (CombatRoundEvent.cs:88-92), boat production stalls when its slip is occupied by the boat it just spawned (BoatProductionTickEvent.cs:40-46), famine/death are one-shot or re-anchored. Many tests rely on this (e.g. EndToEndLoopTests.cs:78,97 call bare `sim.Run()`).
    IMPACT:   The drain-to-empty behavior is an implicit, undocumented invariant of every event type rather than a property of Run itself. The first perpetual self-rescheduler that never stalls (e.g. a future continuous auto-haul, a regenerating resource node, or a passive structure tick) would make `sim.Run()` spin forever, hanging tests and any tool that calls it unbounded. The production server is safe because GameHost always uses Run(until:), but the bare overload is a latent footgun.
    FIX:      Document Run()'s precondition ('only safe when all live event chains are guaranteed to terminate or stall'), and consider a defensive max-iterations / max-advance guard on the unbounded overload, or restrict the no-arg overload to test/replay code. Low priority â€” no active bug today.
    VERIFY:   Accurate and correctly scoped. Run(null) loops while (_queue.Count > 0) and only breaks early when until is set (Simulation.cs:107-115), so the unbounded overload relies entirely on every self-rescheduling chain self-retiring (production fills its finite buffer then clears TickArmed â€” ProductionTickEvent.cs:101-117; combat ends and removes CombatStates â€” CombatRoundEvent.cs:88-92; boat production stalls on occupied slip â€” BoatProductionTickEvent.cs:40-46; famine/death one-shot or re-anchored). Tests depend on this drain-to-empty behavior pervasively, with explicit comments confirming the implicit contract (e.g. BiomeDegradationTests.cs:213 'drains the queue â€” last event is the buffer-fill stop'; bare sim.Run() across CombatCaptureTests, BuildIntentTests, BreedingMoveLockTests, etc.). The production server is safe (GameHost.ClockLoop always uses Run(until:) â€” GameHost.cs:66). The first perpetual self-rescheduler would hang the bare overload. Genuine latent footgun, appropriately rated low; the auditor did not overstate it.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=partial | conf=medium | sev0=medium) ProductionTickEvent is the only self-rescheduling event without an explicit Seq fence
    EVIDENCE: ProductionTickEvent.Apply (ProductionTickEvent.cs:26-33) fences only on 'structure exists and is an Extractor' â€” it never checks `extractor.NextProductionTickSeq == Seq`. Every other self-rescheduling event DOES carry that fence: CombatRoundEvent.cs:31 (`state.NextRoundSeq != Seq`), BoatProductionTickEvent.cs:30 (`dock.NextProductionTickSeq != Seq`), FamineCheckEvent.cs:29 (`castle.NextFamineCheckSeq != Seq`), DeathByAgeEvent (`unit.DeathSeq != Seq`). The invariant that keeps exactly one live tick per extractor is the TickArmed boolean: ArmIfDormant returns early if `TickArmed` (Structure.cs:155) and UnassignWorkersIntent deliberately does NOT clear TickArmed (UnassignWorkersIntent.cs:4), relying on the queued tick to fire and self-retire. So it is safe today, but only by discipline, not by the fencing-token mechanism the rest of the engine uses.
    IMPACT:   TickArmed is only ever set false from inside ProductionTickEvent itself. The first future feature that needs to stop/pause/relocate an extractor and clears TickArmed (or rearms) without dequeuing the in-flight tick will produce TWO live production chains for one extractor: the stale tick fires, sees workers present and buffer not full, produces, and reschedules â€” silently doubling output rate and corrupting the back-pressure model the determinism audit relies on. It is the asymmetric weak link among the five self-reschedulers.
    FIX:      core-touching. Add the symmetric guard at the top of ProductionTickEvent.Apply: after the structure/type check, `if (!extractor.TickArmed || extractor.NextProductionTickSeq != Seq) { Outcome = Reject('stale production tick'); return; }`. This is always true for a legitimately-live tick (a live tick has TickArmed=true and NextProductionTickSeq==Seq) and closes the future double-arm hole. Also add 'self-rescheduling events must carry a (state, Seq) fence' to the determinism-audit re-run triggers.
    VERIFY:   The factual asymmetry is exactly as claimed: ProductionTickEvent.Apply (ProductionTickEvent.cs:29-33) fences only on 'structure exists and is Extractor' with no Seq check, while the other four self-reschedulers all carry an explicit (At/Seq) fence (CombatRoundEvent.cs:31, BoatProductionTickEvent.cs:30, FamineCheckEvent.cs:29, DeathByAgeEvent.cs:32). I confirmed TickArmed is set false ONLY inside ProductionTickEvent (lines 55,69,79,115; plus Snapshot restore at Snapshot.cs:503) and true only in Extractor.ArmIfDormant (Structure.cs:165) and ProductionTickEvent.cs:106; AssignWorkersIntent guards re-arm with !extractor.TickArmed (AssignWorkersIntent.cs:56) and ArmIfDormant early-returns when TickArmed (Structure.cs:155); UnassignWorkersIntent intentionally leaves TickArmed (UnassignWorkersIntent.cs:4-6). So there is no code path today that produces two live ticks per extractor â€” it is genuinely safe, and the finding itself admits 'safe today, but only by discipline.' This is a latent maintainability/robustness asymmetry, not a present logic hole; 'medium' overstates a non-bug. Downgraded to low.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=partial | conf=medium | sev0=medium) One shared RNG stream couples every subsystem's randomness â€” a replay/patch-compat hazard
    EVIDENCE: Rng.cs holds a single mutable `_state` (xorshift64) exposed as `sim.Rng`. The ONLY production consumer today is population lifespan: Population.cs:49 `cfg.LifespanMinYears + sim.Rng.NextInt(span)` (span = 80-50+1 = 31, PopulationConfig.cs:41-42), drawn at genesis in canonical order (Simulation.cs:41-44) and in BirthEvent. Combat draws nothing â€” a grep of src/Sim.Core/Combat for Rng/Random/NextInt returns zero matches, so CombatRoundEvent is fully deterministic. Determinism is therefore intact today because there is exactly one draw site inside deterministically-ordered events.
    IMPACT:   The design (Â§2.4 'seed all RNG') and intent-validation.md's patch-survivability goal both bet on long-term replay of the intent log across code versions. With a single shared stream, the moment any second subsystem draws from sim.Rng â€” the design's hinted 'low-variance combat', mob spawns, weather, raid rolls â€” every subsequent lifespan roll shifts, because the interleaving of draws now depends on event timing. Worse, replaying an OLD intent log under a NEW build that adds or removes a single RNG draw anywhere desyncs the entire population's lifespans and births â†’ replay divergence. You can currently never add a randomness source without breaking replay of existing worlds. (Side note: combat being zero-variance rather than the design's 'low-variance' is a separate combat-scope question, but it is why the shared stream hasn't bitten yet.) `NextInt`'s modulo (`NextUInt64() % bound`) bias is negligible at span=31 and not a concern.
    FIX:      core-touching. Derive independent per-domain sub-streams from the master seed (e.g. `new Rng(SplitMix64(seed ^ DomainConstant))` for Population, Combat, Worldgen, â€¦) so each subsystem's draw sequence is independent of others' draw counts and ordering. This localizes the replay blast radius of any future RNG addition to its own domain and is the standard fix for shared-stream fragility. Document the per-domain seeding in the determinism audit.
    VERIFY:   Code claims verified. Rng holds a single mutable xorshift state (Rng.cs:8). A grep of all of Sim.Core for Rng/NextInt/Random returns exactly one production draw site: Population.cs:49 (ScheduleLifespan), invoked from the genesis ctor (Simulation.cs:41-44) and BirthEvent; combat has zero RNG matches, so CombatRoundEvent is fully deterministic. span = LifespanMaxYears(80) - LifespanMinYears(50) + 1 = 31 (PopulationConfig.cs:41-42), and NextInt's modulo bias at bound 31 is negligible. Determinism is therefore intact today â€” which the finding explicitly concedes ('Determinism is therefore intact today'). The replay/patch-compat concern (adding any second draw to an existing event path shifts all subsequent lifespan rolls and desyncs old-log replay) is a real forward-compatibility/architecture concern and the per-subsystem-stream recommendation is sound, but it is NOT a present bug or logic hole. 'medium' overstates a latent concern; downgraded to low.

##### Persistence & Replay  [key=persistence-replay]
SUMMARY: The snapshot+anchor recovery core is genuinely well-built: RegenerateQueue reconstructs in-flight events from per-entity anchors with original Seqs preserved, canonical serialization is disciplined, and crash-safety leans correctly on SQLite WAL. But the subsystem has two showstoppers and several real holes. The actual player-facing server (Sim.Server) does not use any of it â€” it acks intents with no durable write, no snapshots, no recovery â€” so production has zero durability despite the whole milestone. And the design's mandated anti-silent-rewrite guard (per-intent code_version) is entirely absent from code. On top of that, the "load-bearing" intent-tail-replay path has no test/demo with a non-empty tail, the up-front batch replay can reorder same-tick events vs live, and the strict tick-boundary can drop committed-but-unapplied intents (demonstrated by the reference host's own cold start).
STRENGTHS:
  + RegenerateQueue + per-entity anchors with Seq preservation :: In-flight events are reconstructed from pure state (Unit.NextArrival*, Extractor/Construction/Dock/Castle Seqs, diplomacy/combat/population anchors) and re-scheduled via ScheduleWithSeq, which deliberately does NOT bump _nextSeq (Simulation.cs:80-87). Because all live in-flight events had Seq < the snapshot's _nextSeq, regenerated Seqs can never collide with post-restore Seqs â€” a clean, well-reasoned invariant. RegenerateQueueTests and MidFlightSnapshotTests pin queue identity (same type/At/Seq), genuinely closing the in-flight gap for anchor-able events.
  + Disciplined canonical serialization :: Every collection is iterated in a documented deterministic order (SortedDictionary/SortedSet for players/units/holdings/workers, explicit OrderBy(y).ThenBy(x) for structures/roads/combat/ground/remembered-biome). The road-condition pure-read filter (Snapshot.cs:677-697) correctly excludes lazily-decayed-to-zero road tiles so a live serialize and a restored serialize hash identically â€” a subtle canonicalization handled correctly.
  + Fail-loud catalog-drift guards :: ReadStorage (Snapshot.cs:472-475) and ReadConstruction (548-552) throw InvalidDataException if a structure's capacity or build spec drifts from the live catalog, turning a balance-patch-induced silent corruption into a loud failure. This is the right instinct and partially compensates for the missing code_version guard (though only for these specific fields).
  + Correct log-then-apply crash discipline :: DurableSubmit (DurableSubmit.cs:26-47) writes and commits the durable intent row BEFORE mutating the sim, so a crash between commit and apply replays the intent and a crash before commit leaves it as if never sent. CrashSafetyTests pin SQLite WAL rollback/reopen as a property of our usage, and the (tick,seq) PRIMARY KEY gives idempotent dedupe. The boundary is correctly placed on the low-volume intent side per the A-vs-B analysis.
FINDINGS (kept=10, refuted/dropped=0):

  [CRITICAL] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=critical) The real game server (Sim.Server) never uses the persistence subsystem â€” zero durability in production
    EVIDENCE: GameHost.SubmitEnvelopeJson (src/Sim.Server/GameHost.cs:84-92) calls `_sim.SubmitIntent(at, intent)` directly and returns `Ack(true, "")` with NO durable write. GameHost has no IIntentStore, no ISnapshotStore, no SnapshotCadence, no Recovery, and never calls SaveSnapshot. A grep over src/Sim.Server for DurableSubmit|IIntentStore|ISnapshotStore|SaveSnapshot|Recovery|SqliteIntentStore returns no matches (GameHost.cs only `using Sim.Persistence;` for IntentJson). ServerOptions.cs (lines 14-37) has no --data-dir flag. Program.cs (Sim.Server) builds GameHost with no stores. The only consumers of Sim.Persistence are tests and the Sim.Host CLI smoke demo (PersistentDemo). This directly breaks persistence-model.md:168-170: "the intent row ... is written and fsynced before the server acknowledges the player's command."
    IMPACT:   For an async 'fair while asleep' RTS whose server is expected to run across players' multi-hour absences, any crash or restart of Sim.Server loses ALL state since process launch â€” not even an initial snapshot is written. Every in-flight caravan, build, war timer, and breeding lock vanishes; on restart the world is regenerated from genesis. The entire M4 milestone's purpose (survive restarts/deploys without rewriting the world) is unrealized at the only place it matters. The doc's claim that 'host --data-dir mode' shipped is true only of the Sim.Host demo binary, not the networked server.
    FIX:      Wire DurableSubmit + SnapshotCadence + Recovery into GameHost: open Sqlite stores from a --data-dir, log-then-apply in SubmitEnvelopeJson (write durable BEFORE Ack), drive SaveSnapshot from the ClockLoop on cadence, and Recover-or-cold-start at construction. Not core-touching (Sim.Server only). This should be the top priority; the rest of the subsystem is academic until it runs.
    VERIFY:   Verified. GameHost.SubmitEnvelopeJson (src/Sim.Server/GameHost.cs:84-92) calls _sim.SubmitIntent then returns Ack(true,"") with no durable write; the only `using Sim.Persistence;` (line 5) is for IntentJson.Deserialize (line 84). A grep for DurableSubmit|IIntentStore|ISnapshotStore|SaveSnapshot|Recovery|SqliteIntentStore|SnapshotCadence|data-dir over all of src/Sim.Server returns zero matches. Program.cs:14-16 constructs `new GameHost(build, options.Seed, options.TicksPerSecond)` with no stores; ServerOptions.cs:5-37 has no --data-dir. The only runtime persistence consumer is Sim.Host/Program.cs PersistentDemo. This directly breaks persistence-model.md:168-170 ('the intent row is written and fsynced before the server acknowledges the player's command'). For a server expected to run across multi-hour player absences, any restart of Sim.Server regenerates the world from genesis. Critical is correct.

  [HIGH] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) Per-intent code_version stamp and version-skew refusal (mandated guard 1) are completely unimplemented
    EVIDENCE: persistence-model.md:130-138 mandates guard 1 ('Every intent is stamped with code_version when written. Recovery refuses to start if any tail intent's code_version differs'), line 160 lists the 'Version-skew refusal test' as a REQUIRED acceptance test, and lines 169/172/180 require code_version on intent rows, on snapshots, and a baked-in CodeVersion constant. In code: SqliteIntentStore schema (SqliteIntentStore.cs:48-56) is (tick, seq, player_id, type, payload) with no version column; AppendIntent (line 60) and IIntentStore.AppendIntent (IIntentStore.cs:14) take no version; Recovery.Recover (Recovery.cs:25-67) performs no version check on intents. A repo-wide grep for code_version|CodeVersion matches only docs/persistence-model.md â€” zero hits in code. No version-skew test exists.
    IMPACT:   Approach A (persist intents, re-derive events) is admitted to risk silent history rewrite after a balance patch (persistence-model.md:113-116); the named mitigation is this guard. A balance change to e.g. movement-cost or combat numbers does NOT bump Snapshot.FormatVersion, so a recovery that replays a non-empty intent tail under new rules re-derives past outcomes silently. In an async game where battles resolve while players sleep, a silent rewrite of a past battle is exactly the catastrophic-can't-react outcome the design forbids. The snapshot FormatVersion check is the only surviving guard and it does not cover behavioral (non-layout) code changes. Snapshot-on-deploy (the other guard) is also unimplemented, so the skew window is wide open.
    FIX:      Add a code_version column to the intents table, thread a CodeVersion constant through DurableSubmit/AppendIntent, and have Recovery.Recover refuse (RecoveryException) if any replayed tail row's version != the running binary's. Add the version-skew refusal test the doc lists as required. Lives in Sim.Persistence â€” not core-touching.
    VERIFY:   Verified. grep code_version|CodeVersion over src = zero matches. SqliteIntentStore schema is (tick,seq,player_id,type,payload) PK(tick,seq) with no version column (SqliteIntentStore.cs:48-56); AppendIntent (line 60) and IIntentStore.AppendIntent (IIntentStore.cs:14) take no version; Recovery.Recover (Recovery.cs:57-61) does no per-intent version check. No CodeVersion constant exists, contradicting persistence-model.md:130-138 (mandated guard 1), :160 (required version-skew test), :180 (CodeVersion constant). The surviving FormatVersion check is verified to be layout-only: Snapshot.cs:40-56 documents every bump as a milestone/layout change, and a movement-cost/combat balance tweak does not bump it (FormatVersion=8). Guard 2 (snapshot-on-deploy quiesce) is also absent in code, so the skew window is open. high is appropriate.

  [MEDIUM] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) Strict tick>snapshot boundary loses intents committed at the snapshot tick but not yet applied
    EVIDENCE: Recovery.cs:57 calls LoadIntentsAfter(snap.Tick); SqliteIntentStore.LoadIntentsAfter (line 84) filters `WHERE tick > $tick`, so any intent with tick == snap.Tick is never replayed. The snapshot tick is sim.Now at serialize time, but an intent can be durably logged at tick T (== Now) with its IntentEvent still queued/unapplied when the snapshot is taken. Concrete: PersistentDemo.ColdStart (Sim.Host/Program.cs:525) takes the initial snapshot at tick 0, THEN logs MoveIntent+HaulIntent at tick 0 (lines 529-532) without running. The cadence's first real snapshot is not until ~tick 5000 (DefaultTargetTick, 5000-tick cadence). A SIGKILL before then â€” which the demo explicitly invites (Program.cs:430-432) â€” leaves only the tick-0 snapshot; recovery does LoadIntentsAfter(0), excludes the tick-0 intents, and resumes a fresh genesis world with the Move/Haul lost. The ColdStart comment (Program.cs:523-524) wrongly claims 'intent log replay handles the seed-time submissions.' MidGestation's tick-0 snapshot is the same pattern, saved only because a later snapshot supersedes it.
    IMPACT:   Recovery can silently lose committed, already-acknowledged player intents at the snapshot boundary. The design conflates 'snapshot tick' with an 'intents-applied-through' watermark; they diverge whenever an intent is logged-but-unapplied at snapshot time, which is the normal state right after a player submits. The reference host demonstrates the bug in its own cold-start path.
    FIX:      Record an explicit applied-through watermark in the snapshot (distinct from sim.Now) and have Recovery replay from it; or guarantee the host drains all logged intents (Run past their ticks) before snapshotting; or take the cold-start snapshot stamped before any intent is logged. Snapshot/Recovery change â€” Snapshot is in Sim.Core (core-touching if the watermark goes in the blob).
    VERIFY:   Verified. LoadIntentsAfter filters WHERE tick > $tick (SqliteIntentStore.cs:84), and Recovery calls LoadIntentsAfter(snap.Tick) (Recovery.cs:57). ColdStart (Sim.Host/Program.cs:525) saves the initial snapshot at tick 0 BEFORE logging the MoveIntent+HaulIntent at tick 0 (lines 529-532), so the snapshot's anchors/next_seq predate them; a crash before the first cadence snapshot (DefaultTargetTick 5000) leaves only the tick-0 snapshot, recovery does LoadIntentsAfter(0) excluding both tick-0 intents, and they are silently lost. The ColdStart comment (lines 523-524) claiming 'intent log replay handles the seed-time submissions' is provably false. The general flaw is real: snapshot.Tick conflates 'sim clock' with an 'intents-applied-through' watermark and the two diverge whenever an intent is logged-but-unapplied at snapshot time (a wired GameHost that snapshots concurrently with intake would hit it). I adjust high->medium: demonstrated and the comment is wrong, but the concrete manifestation is confined to the demo cold-start and the production server does not snapshot at all yet.

  [MEDIUM] (missing-feature | verdict=partial | conf=medium | sev0=medium) No fencing token / single-writer enforcement on the intent store â€” two hosts can split-brain the log
    EVIDENCE: IIntentStore.cs:6-7 and persistence-model.md:168 specify 'SQLite, single writer,' but nothing enforces it. SqliteIntentStore.Open (SqliteIntentStore.cs:27-33) just opens a ReadWriteCreate connection; there is no lease row, PID lock, advisory file lock, or fencing/epoch token. AppendIntent (line 60-76) and Recovery (Recovery.cs) never validate a writer identity. The deploy playbook (persistence-model.md:216-236) is quiesce-based with no mechanism to block a second writer.
    IMPACT:   Restart/deploy races (a zombie old host plus a new host on the same data dir) let both processes AppendIntent. PRIMARY KEY (tick, seq) collisions either throw â€” DurableSubmit propagates, silently dropping that player's command â€” or, if Seqs diverge, interleave intents from two different sim states into one log, producing an unrecoverable split-brain on replay. The prompt explicitly calls out fencing tokens; there is none.
    FIX:      Add a fencing/epoch token: on host start, atomically bump a 'writer epoch' row (or take an OS advisory lock on the data dir); stamp it on every AppendIntent and validate it; Recovery and AppendIntent reject a stale epoch. Sim.Persistence only â€” not core-touching.
    VERIFY:   Verified there is no application-level single-writer enforcement: SqliteIntentStore.Open just opens Mode=ReadWriteCreate (SqliteIntentStore.cs:27-33); no lease row, PID/file lock, or fencing/epoch token; AppendIntent and Recovery never validate writer identity; the deploy playbook (persistence-model.md:216-236) is quiesce-only with no second-writer block, despite IIntentStore.cs and :168 asserting 'single writer'. The missing-fencing core is real. Partial, because the worst case is overstated: SQLite WAL serializes writers (a second writer gets SQLITE_BUSY) and PRIMARY KEY(tick,seq) makes colliding same-tick writes throw rather than silently interleave â€” DurableSubmit propagates that as a failed ack (log-then-apply leaves the sim unmutated), so the truly 'unrecoverable silent split-brain' requires two sims whose seqs happen never to collide. Medium severity for the missing operational guard is fair.

  [MEDIUM] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) Intent-tail replay (the milestone's load-bearing mechanism) is never exercised with a non-empty tail
    EVIDENCE: Recovery.cs:57-61 loops over LoadIntentsAfter(snap.Tick) to replay the tail. In every RecoveryTests case the tail is empty: CrashRecoveryMatchesUninterrupted submits intents at ticks 0,0,0,10 (RecoveryTests.cs:65-71) but snapshots at ~50/100/150, so all intents are pre-snapshot; DeclareWar (intent tick 10, snapshot at 60); MidGestation (BeginBreeding tick 0, snapshot at Gestation/2=25); MidFight and DeathByAge have no intents. The reference host (Sim.Host/Program.cs:529-532) also logs its only intents at tick 0 with the initial snapshot at tick 0. So the foreach replay loop runs zero iterations in every test and demo. persistence-model.md:144-156 calls the in-flight crash-recovery test 'the gating one' and frames intent-tail replay as 'the load-bearing line item' (:176-179), yet the gating tests only ever cover snapshot + RegenerateQueue (anchors).
    IMPACT:   The headline correctness claim 'intent-tail replay closes the in-flight gap' is unverified by any test. Whatever divergence exists in the replay path (see the seq-reordering and boundary findings) cannot be caught, because no test feeds a post-snapshot intent through Recovery. The reassurance from the green test suite is real for the anchor path but narrow exactly where the doc says the risk lives.
    FIX:      Add a recovery test where a player intent is submitted AFTER the last snapshot and BEFORE the crash, so LoadIntentsAfter returns a non-empty tail, and assert hash-equality against a live run that submits the same intent at the same tick interleaved with execution (not batched up front). Not core-touching.
    VERIFY:   Verified that the Recovery.cs:57-61 foreach over LoadIntentsAfter(snap.Tick) runs zero iterations in every test. CrashRecoveryMatchesUninterrupted: intents at ticks 0,0,0,10, snapshots at ~50/100/150, latest snap ~150 > all intent ticks. DeclareWar: intent@10, snap@60. MidGestation: BeginBreeding@0, snap@25. MidFight/DeathByAge: no intents. DurableSubmitTests/IntentStoreTests/CrashSafetyTests never invoke Recovery. So the milestone's load-bearing intent-tail replay path is genuinely never exercised with a non-empty tail. I adjust to medium: in isolation this is a coverage gap (the SubmitIntent path itself is the same one used live, so it likely works), but its practical weight is real because it is exactly where the divergences in batch-replay-reorders-same-tick-events and snapshot-tick-boundary-drops-intents would hide uncaught.

  [MEDIUM] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=high) Recovery submits the whole tail up-front, reordering same-tick contention vs live operation
    EVIDENCE: Recovery.cs:57-64 submits ALL tail intents (sim.SubmitIntent) before any sim.Run. SubmitIntentâ†’Schedule (Simulation.cs:62-70, 89-93) assigns each IntentEvent a fresh monotonic Seq at submission time. EventQueue keys on (At, Seq) with Seq as the same-tick tiebreak (EventQueue.cs:7,11). In live operation a tail intent at tick T gets a Seq AFTER all post-snapshot domain events scheduled before T consumed Seqs; on replay every tail IntentEvent gets the lowest post-restore Seqs (N, N+1, â€¦) before any regenerated in-flight event fires and schedules its follow-ups (which then get higher Seqs). So for a tail IntentEvent and a post-snapshot domain event sharing tick T, the (At,Seq) order flips between live and replay. This is the exact 'who wins contention by submission order' fairness contract RegenerateQueue.cs:5-7 says must survive crash+restart. Tests can't catch it: RunUninterrupted (RecoveryTests.cs:75-84) also batch-submits, so the baseline reproduces the recovery pattern â€” and the tail is empty anyway.
    IMPACT:   Replay is deterministic but can deterministically produce a DIFFERENT final state than the live run it is meant to reproduce â€” undermining 'determinism + replay from day one' (design Â§2.4) and the doc's premise that replay is the only sane way to debug async bugs. It bites whenever a player command and an in-flight consequence land on the same tile/structure on the same tick after a snapshot (tile-cap contention, stockpile withdraw, construction-site completion races).
    FIX:      Replay faithfully by interleaving: `foreach (row) { sim.Run(until: row.Tick); sim.SubmitIntent(row.Tick, intent); } sim.Run(until: target);` so IntentEvent Seqs are assigned at the same relative point as live. Add the interleaved-baseline test from the previous finding to lock it. Not core-touching (Recovery is in Sim.Persistence).
    VERIFY:   Mechanism verified. ScheduleWithSeq (Simulation.cs:80-87) does NOT bump _nextSeq and RegenerateQueue restores in-flight events with their original (pre-snapshot, <S0) seqs; Recovery (Recovery.cs:57-61) then batch-submits the ENTIRE tail via SubmitIntent before any Run, so every tail IntentEvent gets the lowest post-restore seqs (S0,S0+1,...), while re-derived in-flight follow-ups scheduled during Run get higher seqs. In live GameHost operation SubmitIntent and Run interleave under _gate, so a tail intent at tick T can receive a seq AFTER a same-tick consequence whose parent fired earlier â€” i.e. (At,Seq) order flips between live and replay. EventQueue keys on (At,Seq) (EventQueue.cs:7,11). The test cannot catch it: RunUninterrupted (RecoveryTests.cs:80-82) also batch-submits all intents up front, so the baseline mirrors the recovery pattern rather than live interleaving, and the tail is empty anyway. This partially violates the fairness-survives-restart contract RegenerateQueue.cs:5-7 states. I adjust high->medium: the divergence is real but only bites on exact same-tick, same-resource contention between a post-snapshot intent and a re-derived consequence, and is currently latent (Recovery is only wired into the Sim.Host demo).

  [LOW] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=low | sev0=low) Snapshot blob has no integrity check beyond magic+version
    EVIDENCE: SqliteSnapshotStore stores (tick, version, blob, created_at) with no checksum (SqliteSnapshotStore.cs:38-43). Snapshot.Restore validates only the 4-byte magic and the version int (Snapshot.cs:94-101); any corruption deeper in the blob is consumed as real field data, yielding a wrong-but-self-consistent state (whose hash matches the corrupted bytes) or an opaque BinaryReader throw. The doc only contemplates per-region hashes 'at scale' (persistence-model.md:201-203).
    IMPACT:   The snapshot is the sole recovery anchor (Recovery refuses to start without one). A silently bad restore reseeds the authoritative world with corrupted state and would be hard to attribute. Low likelihood given SQLite page integrity, but high blast radius if it happens.
    FIX:      Store a SHA-256 of the blob alongside it (Snapshot.Hash already exists) and verify on LoadLatest/Restore, failing loud (RecoveryException) on mismatch so recovery falls back to an older retained snapshot. Not core-touching.
    VERIFY:   Verified. SqliteSnapshotStore schema is (tick,version,blob,created_at) with no checksum/hash column (SqliteSnapshotStore.cs:38-43). Snapshot.Restore validates only the 4-byte magic and the int version (Snapshot.cs:94-101) and then consumes the rest as field data via BinaryReader; deeper corruption yields a wrong-but-self-consistent state or an opaque reader throw. The doc only contemplates per-region hashes at scale (persistence-model.md:201-203). Low blast-probability given SQLite page integrity, high impact if it occurs (the snapshot is the sole recovery anchor). low is correct.

  [LOW] (unnecessary | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=low) SnapshotCadence intent-counter half is unused by every real caller; PruneToLast(0) can wipe all snapshots
    EVIDENCE: SnapshotCadence exposes both a ticks threshold and an intents threshold (SnapshotCadence.cs:42-43, AccumulateIntent line 40), but the only runtime caller (PersistentDemo, Sim.Host/Program.cs:473) calls AccumulateTicks only and never AccumulateIntent; Sim.Server uses neither. So the bursty-intent half of the policy is dead in practice. Separately, SqliteSnapshotStore.PruneToLast rejects only n<0 (line 120), so PruneToLast(0) deletes every snapshot and makes recovery impossible â€” whereas the constructor enforces retention>=1 (lines 18-20), an inconsistency.
    IMPACT:   Minor over-engineering and a latent footgun: the intent-cadence is built and tested (SnapshotCadenceTests) but unwired, and PruneToLast(0) is a manual-op landmine that defeats the retention floor the constructor carefully guarantees.
    FIX:      Either wire AccumulateIntent into the host loop (call it on each durable submit) or drop the intent half; and make PruneToLast reject n<1 to match the retention floor. Not core-touching.
    VERIFY:   Both parts verified. grep AccumulateIntent shows it is called only in SnapshotCadenceTests; the sole runtime caller PersistentDemo (Sim.Host/Program.cs:473) calls AccumulateTicks only, and Sim.Server uses neither â€” so the intent-counter half of SnapshotCadence (SnapshotCadence.cs:40-43) is built and unit-tested but unwired in practice. Separately, PruneToLast guards only n<0 (SqliteSnapshotStore.cs:120), so PruneToLast(0) executes DELETE ... LIMIT 0 and wipes every snapshot, defeating the constructor's retention>=1 floor (lines 18-20) and making recovery impossible (Recovery throws on no snapshot). Minor over-engineering plus a manual-op footgun. low is correct.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=medium) HaulPickup/HaulDeposit events are not regenerated; round-trip relies on an unpinned same-tick invariant
    EVIDENCE: RegenerateQueue.From (RegenerateQueue.cs:18-130) regenerates MoveArrival, Group, Extractor, Construction, War, Combat, Death, Birth, BoatProduction, Famine, Starvation â€” but NOT HaulPickupEvent or HaulDepositEvent. Those are scheduled at sim.Now (same tick) in MoveArrivalEvent.DispatchOnFinalArrival (MoveArrivalEvent.cs:117,121) and HaulPickupEvent.Apply (HaulPickupEvent.cs:134-135). Because Run drains all events with At<=until before returning (Simulation.cs:107-115), a same-tick pickup/deposit can never be observed queued-but-unfired at a snapshot boundary, so it is safe today. The Snapshot does serialize HaulPlan (Snapshot.cs:305-323) so the unit's phase survives, but the queued event itself is not anchored.
    IMPACT:   Correctness currently depends on the invisible invariant 'pickup/deposit are always scheduled for the current tick.' Nothing tests or asserts this. A plausible future change (loading/unloading takes time, scheduling pickup/deposit at a future tick) would make them survive a Run boundary and then be silently dropped on restore â€” re-opening the exact in-flight-loss class the milestone closed, but only for hauls and only after the change.
    FIX:      Either add a guard/comment-backed test pinning that pickup/deposit are always sim.Now-scheduled, or give them on-unit anchors (e.g., a HaulPlan.PendingEventTick/Seq) and regenerate them like the others. RegenerateQueue is in Sim.Core â€” core-touching if anchors are added.
    VERIFY:   All facts verified. RegenerateQueue.From (RegenerateQueue.cs:18-130) regenerates MoveArrival/Group/Extractor/Construction/War/Combat/Death/Birth/BoatProduction/Famine/Starvation but not HaulPickupEvent/HaulDepositEvent. Both are scheduled at sim.Now (MoveArrivalEvent.cs:117,121; HaulPickupEvent.cs:134), and Run drains all events with At<=until before returning (Simulation.cs:107-115), so a same-tick pickup/deposit can never be queued-but-unfired at a snapshot boundary â€” safe today. HaulPlan is serialized (Snapshot.cs:305-323), so the unit's phase survives and the event re-chains from MoveArrival. I adjust medium->low: the finding itself concedes it is safe today; it is a latent fragility (an unpinned same-tick invariant with no test/assert) that only becomes a bug if loading/unloading is ever given a non-zero duration, not a current defect.

  [LOW] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=low) 4 of 16 registered intent types are never round-tripped or deserialized in any test
    EVIDENCE: IntentJson registers 16 intent types (IntentJson.cs:34-52).     IMPACT:   If any of these (or a future intent) ships without a working [JsonConstructor] or with a non-round-tripping field, recovery throws at deserialize and the server cannot restart â€” a fail-to-boot rather than a silent corruption, but still a durability outage discovered only in a real crash.
