---------------------------------------------------------------------

##### World Data Model & Genesis  [key=world-model]
SUMMARY: The world data model is coherent and well-disciplined: a single coordinate space (TileGrid biome array + sparse per-tile/per-player overlay dicts on GameWorld) with documented single-mutation-point "pure-read walls" that serve determinism well, plus clean append-only enums and solid genesis validation. The starting loadout (2x of each of 7 roles, Wood70/Stone50/Food40) is playable and bootstrappable. The real issues are at the seams: (1) the Activity state machine declares a Moving state the sim never enters and the wire never tells the client a unit is in motion or where it is headed, undermining the design's central smooth-movement promise; (2) biome degradation changes build-eligibility, production and the displayed biome but NOT movement cost, so a desertified grassland still moves at grassland speed; (3) "the opening" is only complete through the spec-aware Simulation ctor, so Genesis.Build alone yields immortal, famine-free worlds. Food pressure is also very weak and the server has no fair symmetric PvP opening.
STRENGTHS:
  + Single coordinate space with sparse per-layer overlays and enforced pure-read/single-write walls :: Design Â§2.5's 'one grid holds biome/fog/road' is realized as a dense biome array (TileGrid) plus sparse TileCoord-keyed dicts on GameWorld for roads, fertility, ground resources, combat, and per-player explored/remembered biome. Each layer documents a single mutation site and an 'INVERTED PURE-READ WALL' (GameWorld.cs:14-89), so views/pathfinding can read freely without corrupting snapshot state â€” a clean, determinism-friendly substrate that is memory-efficient and matches the design intent.
  + Disciplined append-only enums for everything serialized :: Resource, Biome, UnitRole, Activity, Traversal, HaulPhase, GroupState and StructureKind are all explicitly marked append-only with stable byte values (e.g. Resource.cs:3, StructureKind.cs:4, Traversal.cs:14-19). This is exactly the discipline a long-lived snapshot+replay format needs and is followed consistently.
  + Centralized Activity transition table fenced by AssignmentEpoch tokens :: ActivityTransitions (Activity.cs:27-36) makes the legal state machine a single explicit table rather than scattered inline checks, and Unit.AssignmentEpoch (Unit.cs:61-71, bumped in TrySetActivity) is a clean fencing-token that lets stale future-scheduled per-unit events no-op deterministically (MoveArrivalEvent.cs:33-37). This is a robust pattern for an async, replayable sim where events fire long after they were scheduled.
  + StructureCatalog as a single tunable spec table :: All Phase-A consumers read costs/rates/biomes from one hand-authored StructureSpec table (StructureCatalog.cs) instead of hard-coding constants, and every scheduled-event-owning structure threads an M4 recovery Seq anchor (Extractor.NextProductionTickSeq, ConstructionSite.BuildCompleteSeq, Dock.NextProductionTickSeq). This keeps balance tuning in one place and makes the world state reconstructable from a snapshot.
  + Genesis validates its inputs and places deterministically :: Genesis.Build rejects empty FactionStarts and duplicate OwnerIds, iterates factions in OwnerId order for deterministic placement matching the snapshot canonical order, and capacity-checks starting holdings against the castle (Genesis.cs:70-98). The starting loadout itself is thoughtfully composed (haulers get real cargo capacity; starting Stone lets a Mine be built before a Quarry exists), giving a genuinely bootstrappable opening.
FINDINGS (kept=7, refuted/dropped=0):

  [MEDIUM] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) Server genesis builds only one rich faction plus a defenseless neutral dummy; no fair symmetric multiplayer opening exists
    EVIDENCE: WorldFactory hardcodes faction 0 with 14 units (2x of each role) + Wood70/Stone50/Food40 (WorldFactory.cs:51-86), then adds at most ONE neutral faction ~12 tiles away with a single Scout and Wood=20 (WorldFactory.cs:88-98). The win condition is 'conquer every enemy castle or force surrender' (design Â§1), but the only opponent is a lone-scout neutral castle with no defenders. Genesis itself fully supports symmetric N-faction starts (MultiFactionGenesisTests.cs:15-43), so the gap is purely in the server build path; StartPicker also explicitly defers fair multi-player placement (StartPicker.cs:12-15).
    IMPACT:   The core data model is ready for fair PvP, but the only production genesis path is single-player-plus-dummy with grossly asymmetric loadouts and minimal spacing (12 tiles vs castle vision radius 5 each). There is no implementation of the balanced, well-separated, equal-loadout opening the conquer-every-castle win condition requires.
    FIX:      Add a multi-player WorldFactory path that gives each real player the same rich loadout and uses a fair, well-spaced StartPicker (multiple starts with minimum separation), rather than hardcoding OwnerId 0 as the only stocked faction.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed and accurately characterized. WorldFactory hardcodes faction 0 with 14 units (2x of 7 roles) + Wood70/Stone50/Food40 (WorldFactory.cs:51-86), then adds at most ONE neutral faction via FindGrasslandNear(...,12) with a single Scout (Id 99) and Wood=20, no defenders/economy (WorldFactory.cs:88-98) â€” explicitly 'so fog/combat have an other.' The win condition is conquest (design Â§1 line 12: 'conquer every other player's castle or force them to surrender'). The core fully supports symmetric N-faction starts (Genesis.Build + MultiFactionGenesisTests, e.g. Genesis_WithNFactions [2,3,4]) and StartPicker explicitly defers fair multi-player placement (StartPicker.cs:14-15). So the only production genesis path is single-player-plus-dummy with grossly asymmetric loadouts and ~12-tile spacing (castle vision radius 5 each, Sight.cs:28) â€” no balanced, equal-loadout, well-separated PvP opening exists despite the conquest win condition. Genuine missing feature; medium stands.

  [MEDIUM] (logic-hole | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=high) Activity.Moving is never entered; the wire exposes no destination/next-tile, so the client cannot render in-motion units
    EVIDENCE: Activity.cs:4-11 defines Moving=1, but a repo-wide search of src/ finds NO call to TrySetActivity(Activity.Moving) anywhere â€” only the enum definition and the Unity Hud's label map. MoveIntent.Resolve explicitly idles the unit before moving (MoveIntent.cs:61 unit.TrySetActivity(Activity.Idle)) and movement is then driven purely by Unit.PathRemaining/NextArrivalTick (MoveIntent.cs:94-153). Group members likewise stay Idle (GroupArrivalEvent/MoveGroupIntent only call BumpEpoch). So a solo unit walking across the map reports Activity.Idle the entire time. The projection only ships current tile + activity: UnitDto has X,Y,Role,Age,Activity,PassengerCap,Passengers (WireDtos.cs:67-78) and ViewProjector sets Activity=(int)u.Activity (ViewProjector.cs:158) with NO destination, next-tile, or arrival-tick field. Hauling units do set Activity.Hauling (HaulIntent.cs:62), so the one moving state that exists is Hauling â€” Moving is dead and cannot even represent a moving hauler.
    IMPACT:   Design Â§2.5/Â§6.1 make smooth, interpolated tile-to-tile movement the headline rendering promise. But the client receives only the unit's CURRENT tile and 'Idle', with no target tile or ETA to interpolate toward â€” so units must visibly teleport one tile per arrival event, and the HUD mislabels every walking unit as 'Idle'. The data model has no field that answers 'is this unit in motion and where is it going,' because the only truth (PathRemaining/NextArrivalTick) is never surfaced and Activity.Moving is never set.
    FIX:      Surface the movement anchor in the projection: add NextTile (PathRemaining[0]) + NextArrivalTick (and optionally PathFinalDest) to UnitDto so the client can spline between tile centers and show ETA. Either set Activity.Moving for plain moves (core-touching, and note it cannot represent a moving hauler â€” Hauling/Moving are not orthogonal, so prefer the projection fix) or delete the dead Moving enum value. The projection-side fix is non-core and unblocks the smooth-movement design promise.
    VERIFY:   Mechanics confirmed: a repo-wide grep finds NO TrySetActivity(Activity.Moving) call (only the enum def at Activity.cs:7, GroupState/Group comments, and the HUD label map). MoveIntent.Resolve idles the unit (MoveIntent.cs:61 via CleanUpAssignment, or BumpEpoch at :47) and movement runs off Unit.PathRemaining/NextArrivalTick (Unit.cs:85-88). UnitDto (WireDtos.cs:67-78) carries X/Y/Activity but NO destination/next-tile/arrival-tick; ViewProjector sets Activity=(int)u.Activity (:158 reveal, :173 fogged), so own moving units report Idle and Activity.Moving is dead. These two defects (dead Moving enum, walking units mislabeled Idle, no ETA field) are real. BUT the headline 'the client cannot render in-motion units / units must teleport' is overstated: design Â§2.5/Â§6.1 only ask the client to 'interpolate between tile centers,' which standard reactive entity-interpolation between consecutive polled positions satisfies without an on-wire ETA (fine for an async game with hour-long moves). The missing-destination field limits faithful multi-tile path reconstruction at coarse poll rates, but smooth rendering is achievable. Severity high -> medium.

  [LOW] (balance | verdict=partial | conf=medium | sev0=medium) Food is a near non-constraint: one farmer sustains ~24 citizens, so starvation only threatens players who build zero farms
    EVIDENCE: Consumption is FoodPerCitizenPerPeriod=1 over a 60-tick period (FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:21-22): the 14 starting citizens (2x of each of 7 roles, WorldFactory.cs:51-66) eat 14/60 = 0.233 food/tick. A Farm has BaseRatePerWorker=2 over a 10-tick period with a 2x Farmer bonus (StructureCatalog.cs:83-95): one farmer = 4 food/10t = 0.4/tick, feeding ~24 citizens; WorkerCap=3 makes one farm feed ~72. Starting larder is Food=40 (WorldFactory.cs:78-83), covering only ~2 meals for 14 mouths (famine flag at tick 180), but the first starvation death is StarvationStartDelay=1440 ticks later (FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:28), i.e. tick ~1620 â€” ample time to stand up a single farm (BuildDuration 30 ticks).
    IMPACT:   The design frames the game as an 'economy of scarcity and distance' where food is ongoing pressure. With these numbers food is solved permanently the moment a player builds one farm with one farmer, leaving spare farm capacity for ~10x the starting population. Starvation becomes a binary 'did you forget to build any farm' check rather than a logistics tension that scales with army/population growth.
    FIX:      Treat as tuning (the catalog calls its numbers placeholders): raise FoodPerCitizenPerPeriod (or per-soldier), lower farm output, or add per-period upkeep that scales with army size, so feeding a growing population stays an active logistics burden rather than a one-time bootstrap step.
    VERIFY:   Rate arithmetic confirmed: consumption FoodPerCitizenPerPeriod=1 over 60 ticks (FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:21-22); Farm BaseRatePerWorker=2, period 10, Farmer bonus 2x (StructureCatalog.cs:89-95) -> 1 farmer = 4 food/10t = 0.4/tick = ~24 citizens; WorkerCap=3 -> ~72. Larder Food=40 (WorldFactory.cs:82), first death at ~tick 1620 (StarvationStartDelay=1440 after famine), farm build 30t (StructureCatalog.cs:97) â€” all correct, so food rate is genuinely generous. BUT 'solved permanently the moment a player builds one farm' is refuted by M9: a Farm drives its own Grassland to PERMANENT Desert in ~260 active-production ticks (StructureCatalog.cs:99-108), after which ProductionTickEvent's biome-mismatch guard shuts it down (ProductionTickEvent.cs:46-61, 'the closure of extract forever from one tile') â€” forcing continual relocation. Production also lands in the farm's own Buffer (cap 40; dormant when full, :75-83), so food must be HAULED to the castle (the consumption sink), and population grows via breeding. So food is over-rated per-worker (a real, mild tuning note) but NOT a permanent non-constraint; the relocation+haul loop is the intended ongoing pressure. Medium -> low.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=low) Tower is fully buildable and functional, but StructureSpec/PlaceSiteIntent comments still call it reserved/non-buildable
    EVIDENCE: StructureCatalog marks Tower IsPlayerBuildable=true (StructureCatalog.cs:115-128) with a real cost (Wood20+Stone10, 60 ticks, 1 builder), and a built Tower provides radius-7 live vision: Sight.RadiusFor(Tower)=7 (Sight.cs:29) and View.VisibleTiles unions owned structures' discs (View.cs:85-90). Yet StructureSpec.cs:17 comments 'Tower = false (reserved)', PlaceSiteIntent.cs:10-11 lists Tower among non-buildable kinds, and Structure.cs:311-318 calls Tower 'Reserved for the fog milestone... no impl yet.' PlaceSiteIntent actually gates on spec.IsPlayerBuildable (PlaceSiteIntent.cs:35), which is true â€” so players CAN place and build functional watchtowers.
    IMPACT:   The watchtower of design Â§4.4 is actually implemented (a genuine win), but three contract comments assert the opposite. Stale/contradictory documentation on the buildable surface is a real maintenance hazard: a future change trusting 'Tower is reserved' could wrongly remove validation or skip handling for an in-use structure.
    FIX:      Update the stale comments in StructureSpec.cs:17, PlaceSiteIntent.cs:10-11 and Structure.cs:311-318 to reflect that Tower is buildable and provides pinned vision. If towers are intentionally not meant to ship yet, instead flip IsPlayerBuildable=false in the catalog.
    VERIFY:   Fully confirmed. Tower IsPlayerBuildable=true with real cost Wood20+Stone10 / 60 ticks / 1 builder (StructureCatalog.cs:115-128); built Tower gives radius-7 live vision (Sight.RadiusFor Tower=7 at Sight.cs:29) unioned via View.cs:85-90; PlaceSiteIntent gates only on spec.IsPlayerBuildable (PlaceSiteIntent.cs:35), which is true, so players can build it. A test actively builds one (LiveVisibilityTests.Tower_HoldsItsArea_AfterBeingBuilt, lines 115-142) and BuildIntentTests.cs:82 notes 'M3 graduated it to buildable.' Yet four stale contract comments still call it reserved/non-impl: StructureSpec.cs:16 ('Tower = false (reserved)'), PlaceSiteIntent.cs:9 (lists Tower as non-buildable), Structure.cs:311 ('Reserved for the fog milestone'), and StructureKind.cs:8 ('reserved for fog milestone â€” no impl yet'). Stale-documentation hazard, no functional defect. Low is correct.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=low) StructureKind, HaulPhase and GroupState have no 0 value, so default(T) is an invalid enum that throws on lookup
    EVIDENCE: StructureKind starts at Stockpile=1 with no 0 (StructureKind.cs:4-17); StructureCatalog.Spec throws KeyNotFoundException for an unknown kind (StructureCatalog.cs:176-179), so default(StructureKind)=0 throws. HaulPhase starts at ToSource=1 (HaulPlan.cs:4-8) and GroupState at Forming=1 (GroupState.cs:8-13). By contrast Resource(None=0), Biome(None=0), UnitRole(None=0), Activity(Idle=0) and Traversal(Foot=0) all reserve an explicit 0 sentinel.
    IMPACT:   Append-only discipline is otherwise clean and well-documented, but the missing 0 means a default-constructed or zero-deserialized value of these three enums is a landmine rather than a benign 'None'. It is currently unreachable in practice (no code constructs these from default), but it is an asymmetry with the rest of the model and removes the cheap safety net the other enums have.
    FIX:      Add an explicit None=0 to StructureKind, HaulPhase and GroupState (append-only-safe since it only fills the unused 0 slot), or document that 0 is intentionally invalid for these. This makes default/zero values fail loudly-or-safely rather than via a KeyNotFoundException deep in catalog lookup.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed. StructureKind starts at Stockpile=1 (StructureKind.cs:6, no 0); HaulPhase at ToSource=1 (HaulPlan.cs in World/, line 6, no 0); GroupState at Forming=1 (GroupState.cs:10, no 0). StructureCatalog.Spec throws KeyNotFoundException for an unknown kind (StructureCatalog.cs:176-179), so default(StructureKind)=0 throws on lookup. By contrast Resource(None=0, Resource.cs:6), Biome(None=0), UnitRole(None=0), Activity(Idle=0), and Traversal(Foot=0, Traversal.cs:17) all reserve an explicit 0. Real asymmetry, low impact. One nuance making the finding's 'unreachable' caveat slightly optimistic: PlaceSiteIntent.Resolve calls Spec(Kind) directly (PlaceSiteIntent.cs:34) with no TryGetSpec guard, and intents resolve during Run inside IntentEvent.Apply (IntentEvent.cs:10) OUTSIDE GameHost.SubmitIntent's try/catch (GameHost.cs:78-92) â€” so a malformed wire PlaceSiteIntent with kind=0 could throw an unhandled KeyNotFoundException at resolution time. That is really an input-validation gap, but it confirms (does not refute) the enum-sentinel concern. Low stands.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=medium) Genesis.Build alone produces an incomplete starting state (immortal units, no famine pipeline); completeness depends on which Simulation ctor is used
    EVIDENCE: Genesis.Build sets BornTick but never DeathTick (Genesis.cs:108-115). DeathTick (lifespan) and the initial FamineCheckEvent are seeded ONLY in the spec-aware ctor Simulation(GenesisSpec,seed) (Simulation.cs:41-54: ScheduleLifespan per unit + OnRateOrFoodChanged per castle). The plain ctor Simulation(GameWorld,seed) (Simulation.cs:21-25) does neither. MultiFactionGenesisTests builds worlds via the plain ctor (MultiFactionGenesisTests.cs:72-73, 85) â€” those genesis units are immortal and never run the proactive starvation pipeline. WorldFactory.cs:6-10 explicitly warns the plain ctor 'would leave them immortal.'
    IMPACT:   'The starting state' is not owned by one place. Genesis.Build returns a world that is missing aging and the proactive dry-out check; only wrapping it in the spec ctor makes it complete. Any code path (or test author, or future tooling) that builds a genesis world and wraps it in the plain ctor gets a subtly wrong opening where citizens never age and the castle never proactively starves. The build-order doc (Â§14) treats genesis seeding as part of world construction, but here it leaks into the ctor.
    FIX:      Make a single entry point own the complete genesis (e.g., have the spec ctor be the only sanctioned genesis path and have the plain ctor assert/reject a never-run genesis world, or fold lifespan+famine seeding into a Genesis.Build overload that takes an Rng+scheduler). At minimum document this as a required-pairing footgun.
    VERIFY:   Facts accurate: Genesis.Build sets BornTick but not DeathTick (Genesis.cs:114); the spec-aware ctor adds ScheduleLifespan + famine seeding (Simulation.cs:41-54); the plain (GameWorld,seed) ctor (Simulation.cs:21-25) does neither; MultiFactionGenesisTests uses the plain ctor (lines 72-73,85). BUT this is intentional, documented in 3 places (Simulation.cs:33-35, WorldFactory.cs:9-10), and STRUCTURALLY NECESSARY: lifespan rolling consumes the sim's Rng, which only exists on Simulation, so it cannot live in Genesis.Build (which returns a bare GameWorld). The production server path correctly uses the spec ctor (GameHost.cs:37 new Simulation(build.Spec, seed)); the plain ctor is REQUIRED for Snapshot.Restore (Snapshot.cs:121 â€” lifespans restored from state, not re-rolled); the one other plain-ctor use (Program.cs:246 GroupDemo) hand-builds units, not a Genesis world. So there is no production bug â€” only a latent footgun for future tooling. Medium -> low.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=medium) Biome degradation changes build/view/production but not movement cost (raw worldgen biome used for traversal)
    EVIDENCE: Movement terrain cost for foot units flows Road.EffectiveCost -> world.Grid.TerrainCost (Road.cs:40) -> Biomes.MoveCost(_biome[Idx]) reading the RAW worldgen array (TileGrid.cs:30); boat cost also reads world.Grid.BiomeAt (MovementCost.cs:77). SetBiome is only ever called in Genesis.Build and Snapshot.Restore (grep) â€” degradation NEVER writes back to the grid. Meanwhile build-eligibility (PlaceSiteIntent.cs:50), the production biome-mismatch guard (ProductionTickEvent.cs:48) and fog memory (Sight.cs:84) all use the DERIVED BiomeDegradation.BiomeAt (BiomeDegradation.cs:89-94). Move costs differ across the M9 ladder: Forest=30, Grassland=10, Desert=40 (Biome.cs:22-41), and the ladder is Forest->Grassland (LumberCamp) and Grassland->Desert (Farm, permanent).
    IMPACT:   After a tile degrades, what the player SEES and what they can BUILD change, but how fast they can WALK it does not. A forest depleted to grassland still costs 30 to cross (should be 10); a grassland desertified by a farm still costs 10 (should be 40). This contradicts design Â§3 ('biomes set movement cost') and the Â§4.2 'world changes behind the fog' theme, and makes route planning lie â€” a permanently-dead desert offers no movement penalty and an exhausted forest never speeds up.
    FIX:      Core-touching: route terrain cost through BiomeDegradation.BiomeAt (make TerrainCost time-aware the way roads already are) so traversal reflects the derived biome, OR explicitly document that degradation deliberately does not affect movement. Today the divergence is silent and inconsistent with every other consumer of biome.
    VERIFY:   Mechanism fully confirmed. Foot cost flows Road.EffectiveCost (Road.cs:40) -> TileGrid.TerrainCost reading the RAW _biome array (TileGrid.cs:30); boat cost reads world.Grid.BiomeAt (MovementCost.cs:77, also raw). SetBiome is only called in Genesis.cs:81 and Snapshot.cs:165 (restore) â€” degradation (BiomeDegradation) never writes the grid. SEE/BUILD/PRODUCE all use the DERIVED BiomeAt (PlaceSiteIntent.cs:50, ProductionTickEvent.cs:48, Sight.cs:84). Derived BiomeAt bands Forest/Grassland/Desert (BiomeDegradation.cs:62-94) and costs differ (Forest=30, Grassland=10, Desert=40; Biome.cs:24-36), so route cost genuinely diverges from the visible/buildable biome â€” even contradicting Biome.cs:3-4's own invariant that 'movement cost and production both derive from' the biome. However medium overstates it: impact is bounded to ladder tiles inside an active extractor's degrade radius, the M9 engineering doc (biome-degradation.md) explicitly enumerates the derived-biome consumers and deliberately omits movement (evidence of scope, not a hard bug), and no test pins the behavior either way. Real inconsistency, but low severity.

---------------------------------------------------------------------

##### X: Whole Loop, Win Condition & Missing Pillars  [key=whole-loop-pillars]
SUMMARY: The sim is an impressively rigorous economy/logistics/combat engine â€” explore â†’ gather â†’ build â†’ grow â†’ fight all exist and are tested end-to-end â€” but the loop has no terminal: there is NO victory, defeat, or surrender condition anywhere in the code, and a castle cannot be captured or destroyed (combat only ever damages Units; structures are inert). So the game's stated win condition (Â§1/Â§13.7: conquer every castle or force surrender) is literally unreachable. Two more design-declared "core" pillars are entirely absent: Trade/barter (Â§11, called "core, not a nicety") has zero code, and action-queuing (Â§12/Â§13.4, "the genre lives or dies on it") is not exposed â€” the host stamps every intent at "now" and there are no standing/repeating orders, so an offline player's supply lines and castle food simply stop. Combat is degenerate civilian-headcount attrition (every role is BaseHealth 10 / BasePower 1; no military units exist), which voids the design's own anti-doomstack argument and makes turtle-and-outgrow the dominant non-strategy. Ranked, the biggest missing pillars are: (1) win/surrender + castle capture, (2) trade posts, (3) military units / meaningful combat, (4) action-queuing + repeating supply orders, (5) ally benefits + real push notifications.
STRENGTHS:
  + Determinism, persistence, and crash-recovery are rigorously engineered :: Twin-run hash equality is enforced per system (EndToEndLoopTests.FullLoop_TwinRunHashesMatch; architecture.md:19-23 acceptance criteria), every in-flight obligation carries a fencing anchor (Unit.AssignmentEpoch, NextArrivalSeq, combat NextRoundTick/Seq, breeding BirthSeq), and mid-flight snapshot/recovery is tested across movement, combat, gestation, and food. This is the genuinely hard foundation for an async server, and it is solid.
  + Biome degradation is a real anti-snowball brake tied to space :: Farms drive Grassland to PERMANENT Desert after ~260 ticks of continuous output and LumberCamps revert Forest after ~1000 ticks (StructureCatalog.cs:99-108, 40-43). Extraction is therefore spatial and exhaustible, forcing expansion and movement rather than infinite single-tile economies â€” exactly the 'presence/distance' pillar, and a rare economy that can't be parked-and-forgotten.
  + Telegraphed war correctly implements the async-fairness contract :: DeclareWarIntent schedules a WarBecomesEffectiveEvent at now+Delay and the pending war is immediately public in every player's view (DeclareWarIntent.cs, GameWorld.cs:57-59), so the target sees aggression coming and can react before it bites (Â§10.1). Consensual peace flips instantly and cancels an in-flight war via fence (RespondToProposalIntent.cs:62-70). This is the clearest example of design intent landing cleanly in code.
  + Capture-on-death economy keeps faith with 'everything physical' :: A laden unit that dies drops its cargo to a tile pile (CombatRules.OnUnitDeath:108-120) that any hauler can later pick up (HaulIntent.cs:51-58, CombatCaptureTests), and boat sinkings drown passengers and spill cargo to the wreck tile. Raiding a caravan yields physical, recoverable loot rather than vanished goods â€” the Â§7.3 'capture not destruction' principle, correctly applied at the unit/cargo layer.
  + Event-driven combat with no global tick :: Combat triggers only on arrival onto a contested tile (CombatTrigger) and self-reschedules rounds only while that one tile is still contested (CombatRoundEvent.cs:94-97), with simultaneous start-of-round damage resolution. The rest of the world stays dormant â€” this is the scalable, Â§9.1/Â§9.2-faithful model and avoids the global-scan trap entirely.
FINDINGS (kept=11, refuted/dropped=0):

  [CRITICAL] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=critical) Combat damages only Units; a castle/structure can never be captured or destroyed
    EVIDENCE: CombatRoundEvent.cs:39-126 and CombatRules.cs:27-62 (ForcePower/GatherForcesOnTile) iterate ONLY world.Units; structures are never gathered, never take damage, never change OwnerId. Structure ownership is set only at Genesis (Genesis.cs:91) and BuildCompleteEvent â€” there is no runtime owner-flip path. The capture intent is explicitly future work: FoodConsumption.cs:184 'a future capture mechanic', Population.cs:116 'lost-castle case post-capture'. Marching an army onto an enemy castle tile and killing every defender leaves the castle (StructureCatalog: Castle, IsPlayerBuildable=false, StorageCapacity=5000) fully owned and operational.
    IMPACT:   This is the mechanism by which the missing win condition manifests in play: there is no physical act of conquest. Â§7.3 ('Capture, not destruction') is implemented for caravans/cargo (capture-on-death drops to GroundResources) but NOT for the one structure the whole game is about. The design's anti-doomstack reasoning (Â§9.3: 'go around and hit their undefended castle and structures') depends on hitting the castle meaning something â€” here it means nothing.
    FIX:      Core-touching: add structure contest/capture in the combat round (when only one hostile owner holds a tile with an enemy Castle and no defenders, transfer ownership of the Castle and its holdings, or start a siege timer). This unlocks the win condition and makes offensive maneuver rational.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed, and stronger than stated: Structure.OwnerId is declared `public int OwnerId { get; init; }` (Structure.cs:11) â€” init-only, so it physically cannot be reassigned after construction. Every OwnerId write site (grep) is a constructor/object-initializer at genesis (Genesis.cs:91,113), BuildCompleteEvent (built structures), PlaceSiteIntent (the site), BirthEvent/BoatProductionTickEvent (new units), or Snapshot restore. CombatRoundEvent.cs and CombatRules.GatherForcesOnTile/ForcePower iterate only world.Units; the sole Structures.Remove is BuildCompleteEvent.cs:57 replacing a construction site with its finished building. There is no runtime structure-capture or structure-destruction path. CombatCaptureTests.cs only exercises cargo-drop-to-ground, never structure ownership. Critical stands.

  [CRITICAL] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=critical) No win/defeat/surrender condition exists â€” the game cannot be won or lost
    EVIDENCE: Design Â§1 (persistent-rts-design.md:12) and Â§13.7 (line 520-521): win = 'conquer every other player's castle or force them to surrender'. Code: GameWorld.cs:22 comment 'no factions / economies / win conditions yet'. Player.cs has only Id + PopulationCount â€” no 'defeated'/'alive' flag. There is no IntentJson entry for any surrender intent (IntentJson.cs:34-52 lists 16 intents; none is surrender/yield) and no Â§13.7 surrender mechanic anywhere. No code path detects elimination: a player whose units all starve to death (StarvationDeathEvent) keeps an empty realm and the sim just continues. Grep for surrender/victory/defeat/win/conquer/gameover across src returned only unrelated 'capture'/'win'-substring hits.
    IMPACT:   Every other system feeds a loop that has no exit. You can fight wars indefinitely but nothing ever resolves them and nobody can ever win. For a 1-vs-N conquest game this is the single most load-bearing missing mechanic â€” without it the entire combat/diplomacy stack is theater. It is the #1 missing pillar.
    FIX:      Implement a victory/elimination check (core-touching, in Sim.Core): on castle-capture (see no-castle-capture finding) and on last-unit-death, evaluate per-player defeat; declare game-over when one faction holds all surviving castles. Add a SurrenderIntent (yields castle/land to a chosen enemy) to satisfy Â§13.7. Emit a notify-tagged event so the async layer can push the result.
    VERIFY:   Verified. GameWorld.cs:22 comment 'no factions / economies / win conditions yet'; Player.cs has exactly Id + PopulationCount, no defeated/alive flag. IntentJson.cs TypeNames lists exactly 16 intents, none surrender/yield. StarvationDeathEvent.cs:59-79 is decisive: when the last citizen dies (PopulationCount==0) it merely clears FamineStartTick and returns â€” the empty realm persists and the global queue keeps running; no elimination is ever detected. Grep across src for surrender|victory|defeat|conquer|eliminate returned zero. Design Â§13.7 lists 'Surrender mechanic' as an explicit OPEN question, so this is acknowledged-deferred, but it is genuinely absent and is the single load-bearing missing pillar for a conquest game. Critical stands.

  [HIGH] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) Action-queuing (Â§12/Â§13.4 'essential for fairness') is not exposed; every intent fires 'now'
    EVIDENCE: Simulation.SubmitIntent(at, intent) (Simulation.cs:89-93) accepts an arbitrary future tick â€” the seam exists. But GameHost.SubmitEnvelopeJson:87 stamps 'var at = Math.Max(_sim.Now, _virtualTick)', forcing immediate submission, and IntentEnvelopeDto (WireDtos.cs:9-13) carries only {TypeName, Payload} â€” no scheduled-tick field. So a client cannot queue an order for later or chain orders. Design Â§12 (line 488): 'Action queuing is essential for fairness'; Â§13.4 (line 512-514): 'The genre lives or dies on whether being logged in 24/7 beats playing smartâ€¦ Needs an explicit action-queuing design.'
    IMPACT:   In an async, offline-first game this is a core fairness mechanism: a player who logs off should be able to plan ahead. With only fire-now intents, presence beats planning â€” exactly the failure mode Â§13.4 warns about. The engine is ready; only the wire/host expose nothing.
    FIX:      Add an optional scheduledTick to IntentEnvelopeDto and pass it through GameHost to SubmitIntent(at,â€¦) with validation (not in the past, sane horizon). Pair with repeating/standing orders (see no-standing-supply).
    VERIFY:   Confirmed. Simulation.SubmitIntent(at,intent) (Simulation.cs:89-93) genuinely accepts an arbitrary future tick (it Schedules an IntentEvent at `at`), so the engine seam exists. GameHost.SubmitEnvelopeJson:87 stamps `var at = Math.Max(_sim.Now, _virtualTick)`, forcing ~immediate submission, and IntentEnvelopeDto (WireDtos.cs:9-13) carries only {TypeName, Payload} â€” no scheduled-tick field and no order-chaining. So the client cannot queue or chain. Design Â§12/Â§13.4 call queuing essential for offline fairness. Context: the full client/networking layer is the pre-M10 roadmap item (architecture.md:370), so this is partly intended-incomplete, but the specific, accurate observation â€” engine ready, wire/host expose nothing â€” holds. High stands.

  [HIGH] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) Hauls are one-shot single trips â€” no standing/repeating supply lines for the offline player
    EVIDENCE: HaulIntent.cs:3 'One submission = one trip.' There is no repeat/loop and no auto-refill order. Castle food is the live consumption sink (FoodConsumption drains the Castle only; ViewDto.CastleFood/FoodRunwayTicks, WireDtos.cs:39-42), but Farm output accumulates in the Farm's own buffer (StructureCatalog Farm BufferCap=40) and must be hand-hauled to the Castle.     IMPACT:   The game bills itself as 'a game about logistics and supply lines' (Â§1), yet a supply line must be re-issued trip-by-trip by an online player. An offline player's castle inexorably drains because nothing keeps food flowing from farm to castle while they sleep. This directly undercuts the 'fair while asleep' pillar and compounds the missing action-queue.
    FIX:      Add a standing/repeating haul order (or a 'supply route' bound to a hauler that re-fires on deposit) so logistics persist offline. Low risk: it reschedules an existing HaulIntent shape rather than touching core economy math.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed (one immaterial number nit). HaulIntent.cs:1-3,16 'One submission = one trip.' â€” no repeat/loop, and no auto-refill intent exists in the 16-intent registry. Food consumption (FoodConsumption.cs) drains ONLY the Castle; Farm output accumulates in the Farm's own Buffer (StructureCatalog Farm BufferCap=40) and must be hand-hauled. Math: owner-0 spawns 14 units (WorldFactory roster: 7 roles Ã— 2), 40 starting Food, rate = popÃ—FoodPerCitizenPerPeriod = 14 per 60-tick period â†’ integer-floor 2 full meals then famine at ~tick 180 (the finding's 171 = 40/14Ã—60 ignores integer-meal flooring; immaterial), then StarvationStartDelay=1440 (60Ã—24) to first death. The offline castle inexorably drains with no standing supply line. High stands.

  [HIGH] (balance | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) All units have identical combat stats; no military roles exist; training is combat-inert
    EVIDENCE: UnitCombatCatalog.cs:24-36 gives every non-boat role BaseHealth=10, BasePower=1 â€” a Builder fights exactly as well as anyone.     IMPACT:   Combat collapses to 'whoever stacks more identical bodies on the tile wins, predictably'. There is no army composition, no equipment, no ranged, no reason to build a School for war. Worse, since outcomes are deterministic by headcount, the design's own Â§9.3 'residual concern' (players avoid all uncertain fights and stalemate into maneuvering) is fully realized â€” fights are never worth risking unless already overwhelming.
    FIX:      Core-touching: add military UnitRole rows with higher BaseHealth/BasePower (and a Buff-backed equipment/training bonus so School pays off), and implement the Â§9.4 ranged-from-adjacent gather. Until then the School structure is dead weight (see school-dead-weight).
    VERIFY:   Confirmed. UnitCombatCatalog.cs:24-31 gives every non-boat role BaseHealth=10/BasePower=1 (boat is 40/0). UnitRole enum (Unit.cs:4-15) ends at Boat=8 â€” no Soldier/Archer/Knight. GatherForcesOnTile (CombatRules.cs:47-62) reads only the one tile, comment confirms ranged-from-adjacent is 'later'. One nuance worth noting: deterministic-by-headcount is design-INTENDED (Â§9.3 'low variance / lean deterministic'), so determinism is not the bug â€” the genuine gap is the total absence of any military differentiation (roles, equipment, ranged). High stands.

  [HIGH] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) Trade/barter â€” declared a 'core' pillar â€” has no code at all
    EVIDENCE: Design Â§11 (line 429): 'Trade is core, not a nicety'; Â§11.2 specifies trade-post structure + deposit + list barter terms + async accept. StructureKind.cs enumerates Stockpileâ€¦School (1-11) with NO TradePost. IntentJson.cs:34-52 registers 16 intents â€” none for list/deposit-offer/accept-barter/withdraw. Grep for trade|barter|listing|swap across src found only unrelated 'swap in'/'swap site' comments. architecture.md:362-364 confirms trade is 'Next big system â€” open', unbuilt.
    IMPACT:   An economy of 'scarcity and distance' (Â§11) with no exchange release valve means a player who is poor in one resource (e.g. lands with no Mountain for Stone) has no way to acquire it except conquest â€” which itself doesn't work (no capture). Cooperation has no mechanical expression. This is the #2 missing pillar and the natural composition partner for roads, raids, and diplomacy that the design leans on.
    FIX:      Add a TradePost StructureKind + the Â§11.2 intent set (deposit goods via caravan, list terms, async accept that swaps holdings, withdraw). The physical caravan layer already exists (HaulIntent + capture-on-death), so trade is mostly menu-state on top of existing sim primitives.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed. Grep for trade|barter|TradePost|listing across src returned zero matches. StructureKind.cs enumerates Stockpile=1..School=11 with no TradePost. IntentJson.cs registers 16 intents, none for list/deposit-offer/accept-barter/withdraw. architecture.md:362-364 explicitly lists trade as 'Next big system â€” open' / 'M7 â€” Trade ... async trade posts (Â§11)', unbuilt. Design Â§11 line 429 calls trade 'core, not a nicety'. This is design-acknowledged deferral rather than a contradiction, but the pillar is genuinely absent and, with capture also non-functional, leaves a resource-poor start with no acquisition path. High stands.

  [MEDIUM] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=medium) Push notifications cover only rejected intents, not the meaningful async events
    EVIDENCE: Design Â§12 (lines 481-483): 'a push notification is just a side-effect hooked onto event resolution â€” tag events with notify player X' (arrival, battle started, under attack, build complete, war declared).   [MEDIUM] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) A victim cannot end a war they didn't start; with no conquest, wars can be permanently unresolvable
    EVIDENCE: DeclareWarIntent.cs:23-26: 'once declared, the war cannot be cancelled unilaterally. The only way out is a bilateral peace proposal that the declarer accepts.' Peace flows through ProposeRelationshipIntent + RespondToProposalIntent (RespondToProposalIntent.cs:42-45: only the proposal's TargetId may accept). So a victim may PROPOSE peace, but the aggressor must accept; the victim has no unilateral exit. Combined with no-castle-capture, two factions can be locked at war forever with no resolution path.
    IMPACT:   For a 'fair while asleep' game this is a one-sided trap: an aggressor can keep a weaker neighbor permanently attackable and the neighbor can do nothing but keep asking. Without surrender or conquest, the war state has no natural terminus.
    FIX:      Either (a) implement surrender (Â§13.7) as the victim's unilateral exit (yield assets to end hostilities), or (b) allow a unilateral cease-fire-after-cooldown. Both are core-touching diplomacy changes.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed. DeclareWarIntent.cs:23-26 documents 'once declared, the war cannot be cancelled unilaterally.' There is no auto-peace, war-weariness, or timeout anywhere (WarBecomesEffectiveEvent only flips to Enemy). Combined with no-castle-capture, a stronger aggressor can hold a weaker neighbor permanently attackable with no terminus. Medium stands.

  [MEDIUM] (balance | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=high) Turtle-and-outgrow is dominant; offense is strictly negative-EV (the Â§9.3 self-balance is void)
    EVIDENCE: Composition of the above: castles can't be taken (no-castle-capture), combat is predictable headcount (combat-no-military-units), and there is no win condition. Â§9.3 (lines 377-391) argues doomstacking self-punishes because an opponent 'simply goes around and hits your undefended castle' â€” but hitting a castle does nothing here, so the geographic counterplay the design relies on does not exist. Attacking can at best kill enemy units and loot dropped cargo (CombatCaptureTests.cs) while exposing your own structures, with no territorial or victory payoff.
    IMPACT:   The rational play is: never fight a fight you might lose, breed up, and harvest until biome degradation forces expansion. Wars devolve into the predictable-winner stalemate Â§9.3 explicitly flags. There is no incentive gradient toward the game's own objective because the objective is unreachable.
    FIX:      Fixing no-castle-capture + a win condition is the primary lever (gives offense a payoff). Secondarily, add the low-variance military layer so contested fights have meaningful, telegraphed stakes rather than pure headcount determinism.
    VERIFY:   Premises confirmed (no capture, no win, deterministic headcount combat), so the structural conclusions â€” 'hitting a castle does nothing' and 'wars never resolve' â€” are correct, and Â§9.3's geographic self-balance is indeed void. The finding is also speculative (no playtest data) and largely re-derives findings 1-3. Real concern, overstated framing â€” downgrade to medium.

  [LOW] (unnecessary | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=low) School + TrainUnitIntent are built but currently buy nothing meaningful

---------------------------------------------------------------------

##### X: Balance Ledger (all constants)  [key=balance-ledger]
SUMMARY: Most per-system math is internally clean and the lazy-catch-up determinism is excellent, but the constants do NOT share one coherent tick->time scale. Food/movement comments assume 1 tick ~= 1 game-minute (60t/hour, 1440t/day, grassland hop=10t), yet PopulationConfig sets a YEAR at 250 ticks â€” i.e. a "year" (250t) is shorter than a "day" (1440t), so aging runs ~2100x too fast and lifespans elapse in minutes at the default 20 ticks/sec. Combat collapses to pure civilian headcount (no Soldier role, all units 10HP/1POW, empty Buffs), Ore has no sink, and there is no castle-capture/win-condition, so the macro loop never closes. The logistics backbone is also throttled by a CargoCapacity that is hardcoded to 1 and decoupled from the Hauler role. LEDGER (per-tick, common units): Farm 3xFarmer=1.2 food/t (buf40); LumberCamp 0.6 wood/t (buf30); Quarry/Mine 0.4/t (buf20); citizen eats 0.0167 food/t; war delay 100t; proposal expiry 200t; dock=1 free boat/300t carrying 100 cargo vs ground hauler's 1.
STRENGTHS:
  + Observation-independent lazy catch-up math is genuinely well-engineered across road decay, biome fertility, and food consumption :: Road.cs, BiomeDegradation.cs, and FoodConsumption.cs all use the same integer-exact 'periods = elapsed/period; carry the remainder' pattern with rate-change anchoring, so state at tick T is identical regardless of how often it was observed. This is the load-bearing requirement for a deterministic, async, snapshot-replayable sim and it is implemented consistently and correctly â€” including the asymmetric band-snap step penalty (degrade snaps down, recovery is smooth) that keeps biome flips durable.
  + Combat is low-variance and deterministic, and doomstacking is self-punishing by construction :: CombatRoundEvent uses simultaneous start-of-round power with lowest-HP-first distribution (no dice), so losses are proportional to the power ratio exactly as design Â§9.3 demands for 'fair while asleep'. Banded crowding cost (MovementConstants: +0/+10/+25/+50) pays max(source,dest) crowd, so a big stack pays its own source-crowd every hop and moves sluggishly â€” the map-and-clock solution to deathballs the design chose, realized cleanly in integer math with no coupled-interval trap.
  + Genesis starting loadout is thoughtfully bootstrapped :: WorldFactory seeds 70 wood / 50 stone / 40 food plus two of every role and gives the 2 Haulers cargo=5, which is exactly enough to avoid the soft-lock where you can't afford the first LumberCamp and to bridge the M13 food drain until a Farm is up â€” a coherent opening that respects the consumption and build-cost numbers.
FINDINGS (kept=9, refuted/dropped=0):

  [MEDIUM] (logic-hole | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=high) CargoCapacity is a fixed spawn-time field (default 1), not tied to the Hauler role and not upgradeable in-game
    EVIDENCE: Unit.cs:28 CargoCapacity { get; init; } = 1 â€” init-only. Only runtime writer is boat spawn at 100 (BoatProductionTickEvent.cs:58).     IMPACT:   The Hauler role gives no cargo bonus, so 'capacity matters' is unfulfilled â€” a Hauler hauls exactly as much (1) as a Farmer.     VERIFY:   Core facts verified: Unit.cs:28 CargoCapacity is init-only default 1; only runtime writer is boat spawn at 100 (BoatProductionTickEvent.cs:58 via BoatConstants.cs:13); BirthEvent.cs:45-50 creates children with no CargoCapacity -> default 1; TrainUnitIntent flips only Role; WorldFactory.cs:53 hardcodes 2 starting Haulers to cargo 5; HaulPickupEvent.cs:88 pickup=min(CargoCapacity,available).
