BUT the food break-even framing is imprecise: the castle food sink (FoodConsumption.cs) charges pop*1/60t whether a unit hauls or idles, so a haul itself adds zero marginal food cost. The valid version is a marginal-citizen/Malthusian point (a citizen that spends its life hauling food over distance D delivers cargo but eats D/3 per round trip, so food-haul-to-castle is only net-positive at D<=3 roadless cargo-1). And 'throughput never scales with population / hard cap' is overstated â€” throughput scales with the NUMBER of haulers (parallelism), and mitigations exist: roads cut grassland cost 80% (push break-even to D<15), host 5-cargo haulers, farms near the castle. Real gap, but doom framing inflates it from medium.

  [MEDIUM] (balance | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=high) Incoherent calendar: a population 'year' (250 ticks) is shorter than a food 'day' (1440 ticks); aging is ~2100x too fast
    EVIDENCE: PopulationConfig.cs:35 TicksPerYear=250. FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:28 StarvationStartDelay=60*24=1440 ('~= 1 sim-day') and line 21 FoodConsumptionPeriod=60 ('~= 1 sim-hour'). So the food subsystem's day=1440 ticks but a whole population year=250 ticks â€” a year is 0.17 of a day. A coherent year at 1440t/day*365 would be ~525,600 ticks; TicksPerYear is ~2100x too small. Lifespan 50-80yr (PopulationConfig.cs:41-42) = 12,500-20,000 ticks; a genesis unit spawned at age 30 (Genesis.cs:54) dies in 5,000-12,500 ticks. Movement cross-map (256 tiles * grassland 10t, Biome.cs:24) = 2,560 ticks, so a citizen lives only ~2-5 map-crossings and can age 10 'years' (2,500t) during one long march. Gestation 300t (PopulationConfig.cs:39) = 1.2 'years' but only 5 food-'hours'.
    IMPACT:   The same global event queue runs food (meal/hour, famine-death/day) and aging (year/250t) on clocks that differ by 3 orders of magnitude, so no single narrative time exists. In play, citizens churn through full lifespans in a handful of food-days while a farm has barely produced a few meals; breeding/lifespan pacing is unrelatable to supply-line pacing, defeating the 'plan hours ahead in your head' legibility goal.
    FIX:      Pick ONE tick=minute convention and set TicksPerYear consistently (~525,600 for realistic years, or deliberately compress to e.g. 40,000-100,000 and document that a 'year' is an abstract aging unit). core-touching (PopulationConfig default). At minimum make all four anchors â€” meal period, famine day, war delay, year â€” derive from a single documented TicksPerGameHour constant.
    VERIFY:   All cited numbers verified: PopulationConfig.cs:35 TicksPerYear=250; FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:21 period=60, :28 StarvationStartDelay=60*24=1440; lifespan 50-80yr (PopulationConfig.cs:41-42) = 12,500-20,000 ticks; Genesis.cs:54 StartingAgeYears=30; gestation 300t (line 39). Math checks (genesis unit dies at tick 5,000-12,500; cross-map 256*10=2,560t = ~10 'years'). EXTRA corroboration: PopulationConfig.cs comment (lines 9-11) says default should be 100 / '60-yr lifespan = 6000 ticks' but code is 250 â€” a real internal comment/value drift. BUT 'high / aging is ~2100x too fast' is overstated: the food 'hour/day' are explicitly flagged approximations ('â‰ˆ 1 sim-hour (60 ticks if 1 tick â‰ˆ 1 min)'), so treating 1440 as the canonical clock is a framing choice; gameplay is driven by raw ticks where the loop is internally workable (a citizen eats ~200-330 food over a 12.5-20k-tick life vs a fertility window of 4,500-11,250t). The genuine consequence is narrative incoherence + units aging out in ~2-5 map crossings, which is a legibility/tuning concern, not mechanical breakage â€” hence medium not high.

  [LOW] (balance | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=low) MAX_REDUCTION=8 makes roads matter only on cheap grassland; they barely help the terrain that needs them most
    EVIDENCE: RoadConstants.cs:20 MAX_REDUCTION=8 (flat, subtracted). A maxed road: Grassland 10->2 (-80%), Forest 30->22 (-27%), Hills 25->17 (-32%), Mountain 45->37 (-18%) (Road.cs:43-45, Biome.cs:24). BASE_GAIN=50 over CONDITION_MAX=1000 -> ~20+ traversals to a meaningful road (RoadConstants.cs:26); decay 1/100t so a maxed road lasts 100,000 ticks.
    IMPACT:   Roads are pitched as the 'strongest emergent system' (design Â§8) â€” exploration becoming permanent capital that pins speed through hard country. But a flat -8 cap means a mountain pass road is only 18% faster even when fully built, while grasslands you didn't need help on get 80% off. The incentive curve is backwards: you build roads where movement is already cheap and can't meaningfully tunnel through chokepoint terrain.
    FIX:      Make reduction proportional to biome cost (e.g. up to ~50-70% off) or scale MAX_REDUCTION with terrain, so a maxed mountain road approaches grassland speed â€” that is what turns a pass into the 'permanent capital' the design wants. Lives in RoadConstants/Road.cs (core-touching).
    VERIFY:   Numbers exact. RoadConstants.cs:20 MAX_REDUCTION=8, applied as a flat subtraction: Road.cs:43 reduction = condition*8/1000, cost = biomeCost - reduction (line 44), floored at MIN_COST=1. Maxed (condition 1000): Grassland 10->2 (-80%), Forest 30->22 (-27%), Hills 25->17 (-32%), Mountain 45->37 (-18%) â€” all verified against Biome.cs:24-27. BASE_GAIN=50/CONDITION_MAX=1000 (lines 26,10) -> ~20 traversals to a meaningful road; decay 1/100t (lines 38-39) -> maxed road lasts 100,000 ticks. The percentage critique is valid: a flat cap means roads can never make chokepoint terrain competitive (a maxed mountain road is still 37 vs bare grassland 10). Two softening notes keep it at low (matching the stated severity): roads are traffic-EMERGENT (Road.CreditTraffic from MoveArrivalEvent), not deliberately placed with resources, so 'you build roads where movement is already cheap' is imprecise â€” they form wherever you repeatedly travel; and the behavior is explicitly intended/documented (RoadConstants.cs:16-20 lists these exact outcomes). A fair low-severity balance observation.

  [LOW] (balance | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=medium) Default TicksPerSecond=20 turns 'moves last hours' into 'moves last seconds' and lifespans into minutes
    EVIDENCE: ServerOptions.cs:8 TicksPerSecond=20.0; GameHost.cs:61-66 maps wall-clock to ticks at that rate. A grassland hop=10 ticks (Biome.cs:24) = 0.5 real seconds; crossing the default 256-wide map (WorldFactory uses opts.MapWidth=256) = 2,560 ticks = 128 real seconds (~2 min) for the WHOLE continent. A lifespan of 12,500-20,000 ticks = 10.4-16.7 real minutes; reaching end-of-fertility (45yr=11,250t) ~9 real min. War delay 100t (DiplomacyConfig.cs:21) = 5 real seconds of warning.
    IMPACT:   The design's whole premise is async 'geological time' where players are offline for hours/days and combat must be 'fair while asleep'. At 20 tps the entire economy, population turnover, and war telegraph play out faster than a coffee break, so an offline player misses everything. The constants are denominated in ticks but the tick is wired ~2-3 orders of magnitude too fast for the stated vision.
    FIX:      Drop the default tps by ~100-1000x (e.g. 0.05-0.2 ticks/sec) so a grassland hop is minutes and a map crossing is hours of real time, then re-validate that war delay and starvation grace land in the intended real-hours band. This is a host config, not core, but it must be chosen jointly with TicksPerYear (see year-shorter-than-day).
    VERIFY:   Facts verified: ServerOptions.cs:8 TicksPerSecond=20.0; GameHost.cs:60-66 maps wall-clock to ticks at that rate; MapWidth=256. The derived real-times (map crossing ~2 min, lifespan ~10-17 min, war delay 100t=5s) follow from the verified constants. HOWEVER this is a single host-side default in Sim.Server (not a Sim.Core balance constant), it is overridable at launch (ServerOptions.cs:23 '--tps'), and is almost certainly a dev/testing placeholder â€” you cannot iterate on a sim where a lifespan is 16 hours of wall-clock. The simulation's tick-denominated logic is correct; only the deployment knob contradicts the async vision. That's a real 'set a production tps' note but a trivially-fixed config choice, not a balance flaw â€” severity overstated at medium.

---------------------------------------------------------------------

##### X: Determinism & Async Fairness  [key=determinism-async-fairness]
SUMMARY: The deterministic-replay core is genuinely excellent: a single (At, Seq) priority queue makes ties impossible, RNG is a hand-rolled xorshift64 (owned bits for cross-runtime stability) consumed in exactly one canonical-ordered site, combat is fully RNG-free and proportional, and the "views are pure reads" wall is pinned by runtime hash-equality tests. The replay/snapshot machinery (mid-flight restore == uninterrupted hash) is solid. The problems are almost entirely on the ASYNC-FAIRNESS axis, not the determinism axis: there is no action-queuing/catch-up/anti-whale design (the Â§13.4 "essential" feature), the telegraphed-war delay collapses to ~5 wall-seconds at the default tick rate, intents carry no ownership authorization (an online player can puppet a sleeping one), and the entire durable-persistence layer that backs "replay from day one" is built, tested, and then never wired into the running server. One latent determinism hazard remains in worldgen (third-party double-precision noise vs. the stated cross-machine reproducibility promise).
STRENGTHS:
  + Single (At, Seq) priority queue makes ordering ties impossible :: EventQueue keys on (At, Seq) with a monotonic _nextSeq (Simulation.cs:62-70); every same-tick event has a unique Seq, so the .NET PriorityQueue's instability is irrelevant. DeterminismTests.SameTickEvents_ResolveInSubmissionOrder pins it. This is the load-bearing determinism guarantee and it is clean.
  + RNG is owned, minimal, and canonically consumed :: Rng.cs is a hand-rolled xorshift64 chosen specifically so replay survives runtime upgrades, and it is drawn in exactly ONE place (Population.ScheduleLifespan, Population.cs:49) iterated in canonical (faction-id, unit-id) order from the sim ctor (Simulation.cs:41-44). No wall-clock, Guid, System.Random, Dictionary-order, or float draw leaks into hashed state (grep-confirmed).
  + Combat is fully deterministic and proportional â€” the async low-variance model done right :: CombatRoundEvent uses start-of-round snapshot power (simultaneous resolution), sorts owners and damage targets by (Health, Id), and draws zero RNG (CombatRoundEvent.cs:39-126). Losses are proportional to power ratio with no dice â€” exactly the Â§9.3 'no coin-flip that wipes an army while you sleep' requirement.
  + The inverted pure-read wall is enforced by runtime hash-equality tests :: Views never mutate sim state, proven not by convention but by tests: FogDeterminism.ViewsOff_HashEquals_ViewsOn, CombatDeterminism.Views_DoNotAffectCombatState, and the 100x-no-mutation pins for visibility/roads/crowding/fertility. Any future view that leaked into state fails immediately.
  + Mid-flight snapshot/restore reproduces the uninterrupted hash; serialization is rigorously canonical :: MidFlightSnapshotTests proves run-to-T â†’ snapshot â†’ restore â†’ run-to-END equals the uninterrupted hash, closing the in-flight gap via per-entity anchors + RegenerateQueue with preserved Seqs. Snapshot.cs iterates every collection in an explicit sorted order and the determinism-audit.md catalogs every mutation/iteration site â€” unusually disciplined determinism engineering.
  + Telegraphed war is correctly modeled and fenced (mechanism, not magnitude) :: DeclareWarIntent schedules a delayed WarBecomesEffectiveEvent that flips state only after the delay, with epoch/anchor fencing so a peace deal cleanly no-ops the pending flip (WarBecomesEffectiveEvent.cs:28-41). DiplomacyDeterminismTests twin-runs the full declareâ†’effectiveâ†’peace cycle to identical hashes. The design is right; only the delay tuning (separate finding) undercuts it.
FINDINGS (kept=8, refuted/dropped=0):

  [HIGH] (logic-hole | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) Intents carry no ownership check â€” any client can command another player's units, including a sleeping one
    EVIDENCE: MoveIntent.Resolve (MoveIntent.cs:17-18) only checks the unit exists; it never compares unit.OwnerId to the intent's PlayerId. The base Intent.PlayerId is documented as aspirational: Intent.cs:11-12 says it is '(eventually) used by validation when intents become player-scoped.' HttpApi.cs:58-63 (POST /intent) deserializes the envelope and forwards it with no authentication of who is calling; the player id is taken from the JSON payload itself, and GameHost.SubmitEnvelopeJson (GameHost.cs:76-93) performs no owner check. Same gap in HaulIntent, AssignWorkersIntent, DeclareWarIntent, etc.
    IMPACT:   This is the strongest possible violation of 'fair while asleep': an online attacker can submit MoveIntent/HaulIntent for a sleeping victim's unit ids (which leak through any shared view), scatter their haulers, abort their builds, or even declare war in the victim's name. The telegraphed-war protection is irrelevant if you can just puppet the target's own army. It also corrupts same-tick fairness (you can act for two factions at once).
    FIX:      Add an authenticated player id at the transport layer and reject any intent whose target unit/structure OwnerId != authenticated player (with the per-id 'continue' skip pattern already used for grouped units). The owner check belongs in each Intent.Resolve (core-touching) plus host auth.
    VERIFY:   Core vulnerability verified, with one overstatement to flag. MoveIntent.cs:17-18 only checks unit existence (no OwnerId compare); HaulIntent.cs:35-60 and AssignWorkersIntent.cs:34-53 likewise validate existence/idle/position but never ownership; DeclareWarIntent.cs:39-46 validates DeclarerId/TargetId are registered factions but never ties DeclarerId to the submitter â€” so war can be declared in a victim's name. HttpApi.cs:58-62 reads the raw body and GameHost.SubmitEnvelopeJson:76-93 trusts the JSON-supplied PlayerId with zero authentication. So an attacker can move/haul/scatter a victim's units (no spoof even needed for those intents). OVERSTATEMENT: the blanket claim 'Intents carry no ownership check' is wrong â€” TrainUnitIntent.cs:39,64 and MoveGroupIntent.cs:34 DO reject on `OwnerId != PlayerId`. But those checks are defeated anyway because PlayerId itself is attacker-controlled (no transport auth), so the headline holds. Caveat: the listener binds localhost only (HttpApi.cs:19), so today's threat surface is a dev box; for the intended multiplayer game this is a genuine high-severity hole, and Intent.cs:11-12 itself concedes player-scoping is only 'eventually' enforced.

  [HIGH] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) No action-queuing / catch-up / anti-whale mechanism â€” being online-and-fast beats playing-smart-while-asleep
    EVIDENCE: GameHost.cs:87 sets `at = Math.Max(_sim.Now, _virtualTick)` for EVERY submitted intent, so a player can only ever schedule at the current virtual tick â€” there is no API to queue a future-dated, conditional, sequenced, or standing order. SubmitIntent(at,...) does support future `at` (Simulation.cs:62-70), but the host never exposes it. Design Â§12 ('Action queuing is essential for fairness') and Â§13.4 ('the genre lives or dies on whether being logged in 24/7 beats playing smart â€¦ needs an explicit action-queuing design and possibly catch-up mechanics') call this out as essential and unsolved.
    IMPACT:   The only 'queued action' a player gets today is a single long-running intent (move/haul/build-when-materials-arrive) that plays out over time. They cannot pre-program a plan and log off ('when this caravan arrives, send it home', 'declare war at dawn', 'keep hauling wood from A to B'). An online player who can re-task continuously in real time therefore strictly dominates an absent one in every micro-decision â€” exactly the whale advantage Â§13.4 says the genre must not have. There is also no catch-up that rewards the absent-but-smart player.
    FIX:      Expose future-/conditional-intent submission (the engine already accepts a future `at`) and add standing-order primitives (repeat-haul loop, on-arrival chain, scheduled declare-war). Consider an explicit catch-up/grace mechanic. Mostly host + new intent types; the queue already orders future events deterministically.
    VERIFY:   Verified. GameHost.cs:87 forces `at = Math.Max(_sim.Now, _virtualTick)` for every submission, and the only HTTP surface is POST /intent + GET /view (HttpApi.cs:46-64) â€” there is no endpoint to future-date, sequence, condition, or stand-order an intent, even though Simulation.SubmitIntent/Schedule (Simulation.cs:62-70,89-93) accept an arbitrary future `at`. The only 'queued action' is a single long-running move/haul/build. Design Â§12 (line 487 'Action queuing is essential for fairness') and Â§13.4 (lines 512-514, 'the genre lives or dies on whether being logged in 24/7 beats playing smart â€¦ needs an explicit action-queuing design and possibly catch-up mechanics') flag this as essential and explicitly unsolved, which corroborates rather than refutes the finding. High stands.

  [HIGH] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=high) Durable intent log + snapshot recovery exists but is never wired into the running server â€” a restart loses the whole world
    EVIDENCE: Program.cs:13-28 constructs only GameHost(build, seed, tps) + HttpApi; no IIntentStore/ISnapshotStore. GameHost.cs has no store fields and GameHost.cs:88 calls `_sim.SubmitIntent(at, intent)` directly â€” NOT Sim.Persistence/DurableSubmit.cs:26 (SubmitIntentDurable). No SnapshotCadence (SnapshotCadence.cs) tick is ever called and Recovery.Recover (Recovery.cs:25) has no caller in Sim.Server. The full Sim.Persistence project (SqliteIntentStore, SqliteSnapshotStore, Recovery, SnapshotCadence) is production-dead code.
    IMPACT:   Design Â§2.4 makes 'determinism + replay from day one' a founding principle, and the game's whole premise is a PERSISTENT world on geological time with players offline for days. With persistence unwired, the authoritative Simulation lives only in process RAM: any crash, deploy, or restart wipes every castle, road, and in-flight caravan. The determinism contract that the audit doc, MidFlightSnapshotTests, and RecoveryTests all carefully protect is inert in the only binary that actually runs.
    FIX:      Wire GameHost to DurableSubmit.SubmitIntentDurable (log-then-apply) behind the same _gate, drive SnapshotCadence after each Run batch and persist via ISnapshotStore, and add a cold-start path that calls Recovery.Recover (falling back to Genesis + initial snapshot when no snapshot exists). Not core-touching â€” all of this is host + Sim.Persistence which already exist.
    VERIFY:   Verified. Sim.Server/Program.cs:13-19 constructs only GameHost+HttpApi; GameHost.cs:37 builds a bare `new Simulation(build.Spec, seed)` with no store fields, and :88 calls `_sim.SubmitIntent(at, intent)` directly (not DurableSubmit). No SnapshotCadence and no Recovery.Recover caller exist anywhere in Sim.Server. So the production HTTP server the Unity client drives keeps the entire authoritative world in process RAM and loses it on any restart/crash/deploy â€” a direct break of design Â§2.4 'determinism + replay from day one' and the persistent-world premise. One correction to the evidence: the persistence stack is NOT literally dead code â€” Sim.Host/Program.cs PersistentDemo (lines 431-535) wires the full path (Recovery, SnapshotCadence, DurableSubmit, both Sqlite stores) and the Persistence test suites exercise it. But Sim.Host is a demo/smoke harness, not the live server, so the core claim (the running game server has no durability) holds at high.

  [MEDIUM] (unnecessary | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) Simulation keeps every resolved event and every intent in unbounded in-memory lists for the life of the process
    EVIDENCE: Simulation._resolvedLog (Simulation.cs:15-16) is appended on every single event in Run (Simulation.cs:114 `_resolvedLog.Add(e)`) and never trimmed; _intentLog (Simulation.cs:18-19) is appended on every SubmitIntent (Simulation.cs:91) and never trimmed. Both are exposed read-only and grow for the entire run.
    IMPACT:   For a server explicitly meant to run on 'geological time' (days/weeks/months), an in-RAM list that gains an entry per event is an unbounded memory leak; GameHost.HarvestRejections also re-walks _resolvedLog via a cursor, so the list must stay resident. The durable SQLite intent log (the intended system-of-record) would make _intentLog redundant, but it isn't wired (see persistence-not-wired). This is the kind of over-retention the persistent design can't afford.
    FIX:      Once durable logging is wired, drop or window these lists (e.g. ring buffer for recent rejections only). At minimum cap _resolvedLog to the un-harvested tail. Core-touching (Simulation), but mechanical.
    VERIFY:   Verified. Simulation._resolvedLog.Add(e) runs on every dequeued event in Run (Simulation.cs:114) and is never trimmed; _intentLog.Add runs on every SubmitIntent (Simulation.cs:91) and is never trimmed; both are exposed read-only (lines 16,19) and grow for the entire process life. GameHost.HarvestRejections walks _resolvedLog via the forward-only _resolvedCursor (GameHost.cs:115), so the resolved list must stay resident even though already-harvested entries are never re-read â€” i.e. the retention past the cursor is pure waste. For a server explicitly built for 'geological time' this is unbounded RAM growth (one entry per resolved event, which over weeks at any tick rate is unbounded). Correctly a medium retention/over-engineering concern (latent OOM, not a correctness bug); it parallels the audit doc's other acknowledged O(n) scaling notes. Medium stands.

  [MEDIUM] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) Offline players are never pushed war/under-attack notifications â€” the telegraph is pull-only
    EVIDENCE: GameHost.HarvestRejections (GameHost.cs:112-132) builds NoticeDto entries ONLY for IntentEvents whose Outcome.IsRejected and whose Intent.PlayerId matches â€” i.e. only a player's OWN rejected commands. There is no notice for 'war declared against you', 'your caravan is under attack', or 'famine started'. The pending war is surfaced only if the target polls GET /view (DeclareWarIntent.cs:8-13 / the PlayerView), and notices are delivered only inside that same poll response (GameHost.cs:103).
    IMPACT:   Design Â§12 states a push notification is 'just a side-effect hooked onto event resolution â€” tag events with notify player X', and Â§10.1 says the immediate notification 'is exactly what makes [telegraphed war] fair.' Without server-initiated push, an offline target learns of an incoming war or an ambush only if they happen to log in during the (already too-short) window. The reactive half of the fairness model is missing.
    FIX:      Tag resolved events (WarBecomesEffective scheduling, CombatTrigger, famine start) with a notify-player-id and emit notices for them in HarvestRejections-equivalent harvesting, then deliver via a real push channel. Host-side; the resolved-event log already carries the needed metadata.
    VERIFY:   Verified. GameHost.HarvestRejections (GameHost.cs:112-131) creates NoticeDto entries ONLY for resolved IntentEvents that IsRejected, attributed to the intent's own PlayerId (:118) â€” i.e. only a player's own bounced commands. There is no notice generated for 'war declared against you', 'caravan under attack', or 'famine started'. The pending war is surfaced only through PlayerView when the target polls GET /view (DeclareWarIntent.cs:9-13 comment confirms 'the target sees the pending war in their PlayerView'), and even the rejection notices are delivered only inside that same poll response (GameHost.cs:103). So there is no server-initiated push at all â€” the reactive half of Â§10.1's fairness model and the Â§12 promise ('a push notification is just a side-effect hooked onto event resolution â€” tag events with notify player X', lines 481-483) is unbuilt. Mild mitigation: the telegraph isn't invisible â€” a polling target does see the pending war â€” so medium (missing feature) is the right level, not high.

  [MEDIUM] (balance | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=high) Telegraphed-war delay is ~5 wall-clock seconds at the default tick rate â€” the anti-ambush fairness window is effectively zero
    EVIDENCE: DiplomacyConfig default Delay = 100 ticks (DiplomacyConfig.cs:21); WorldFactory never overrides it, so the live world uses 100. ServerOptions.TicksPerSecond default = 20.0 (ServerOptions.cs:8), i.e. 1 tick = 50 ms wall-clock. 100 ticks / 20 tps = 5 wall-seconds of warning. Design Â§10.1 specifies 'effective in 6 hours.' Famine is the same story: FoodConsumptionConstants.StarvationStartDelay = 60*24 = 1440 ticks (FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:28) â†’ 72 wall-seconds before the first starvation death. For Delay to telegraph 6 real hours at tps=20 it would need ~432,000 ticks.
    IMPACT:   The entire Â§10.1 fairness argument is 'the sneak-army must survive the target reacting before the switch flips.' A sleeping (or even just AFK) target cannot react in 5 seconds, so betrayal is once again a free point-blank ambush â€” the exact exploit the delay was designed to close. At tps=20 the sim also runs ~14,000x faster than the design's 'two hours per tile' pace (Grassland = 10 ticks/tile = 0.5 wall-seconds/tile), so every async telegraph window is compressed into seconds.
    FIX:      Define the diplomacy Delay and starvation delays in real-time-anchored terms and pick a production TicksPerSecond that actually maps the sim to geological time; assert that Delay translates to multiple real hours. Config/host-touching, not Sim.Core (the delay is already configurable).
    VERIFY:   Arithmetic and constants all verified: DiplomacyConfig.cs:21 Delay=100; GenesisSpec.Diplomacy defaults to new() (Genesis.cs:29) and WorldFactory never overrides it, so the live world uses 100; ServerOptions.cs:8 tps=20 â†’ 100/20 = 5 wall-seconds; FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:28 StarvationStartDelay=1440 â†’ 72s; Biome.cs:24 Grassland=10 ticks â†’ 0.5s/tile. So as-shipped the windows really are seconds. BUT the 'effectively zero / high' framing overstates a dev-tps artifact: tps is an explicit CLI knob (ServerOptions.cs:23) and both the code (FoodConsumptionConstants.cs:9 'Default â‰ˆ 1 sim-hour (60 ticks if 1 tick â‰ˆ 1 min)') and design intend a far slower production clock; at the intended ~1 tick/min the war delay is ~1.67h, not 5s. The genuine residual balance gap is that Delay=100 â‰ˆ 1.67h still falls short of the Â§10.1 'effective in 6 hours' promise (which needs ~360 ticks at 1 tick/min), and that all fairness windows are tick-denominated with no wall-clock anchor. That is a real medium tuning/structural gap, not a high 'window is zero' hole â€” hence partial/medium.

  [LOW] (balance | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=low) Contested-resource resolution is first-real-time-submit-wins, giving a low-latency online player a presence edge
    EVIDENCE: All live intents are scheduled at the current virtual tick (GameHost.cs:87) and the (At, Seq) queue (EventQueue.cs:7-11) resolves equal-At events in Seq = submission order. SameTickFairnessTests pins this as intended ('who gets the last unit of depleting stock / filling buffer'). At tps=20 a tick is 50 ms, so two players racing for the last unit of a buffer must land in the same 50 ms window to even tie; otherwise the earlier real-time submitter simply resolves at an earlier tick and wins outright.
    IMPACT:   This is deterministic and reproducible (a genuine strength for replay), but as a FAIRNESS property it means faster reaction / lower latency wins every contested pull or last-material deposit. It is narrow (only literal contests), yet it reinforces the broader Â§13.4 concern: there is no queuing or arbitration that lets an absent player compete for contested stock on equal footing.
    FIX:      Acceptable for now given contests are rare, but revisit alongside action-queuing: e.g. reservation/commit semantics for trade-post pulls so outcomes don't hinge on millisecond arrival order. No change needed if action-queuing lands first.
    VERIFY:   Verified and correctly scoped. All live intents schedule at the current virtual tick (GameHost.cs:87) and EventQueue keys on (At, Seq) resolving equal-At events in submission/Seq order (EventQueue.cs:7,11). SameTickFairnessTests.cs:54-93 pins exactly this as intended gameplay ('first-submitted wins' the last buffer unit / last deposit, and swapping submission order swaps the winner). So the earlier real-time submitter gets the lower Seq and wins contested pulls â€” a genuine low-latency presence edge, consistent with the broader Â§13.4 whale concern. The finding itself rates this low and acknowledges it's simultaneously a determinism/replay strength; it's a narrow property (only literal contested pulls/deposits) and the dominant fairness story is hours-long travel, so low is correct. Confirmed at low.

  [LOW] (logic-hole | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=medium) World generation uses third-party double-precision noise, contradicting the stated cross-machine seed-reproducibility promise
    EVIDENCE: NoiseField.Generate (NoiseField.cs:13-39) builds the biome map from SharpNoise.Modules.Perlin using doubles (raw*0.5 etc.). ServerOptions.cs:5-6 promises 'Seed is fixed â€¦ so a given --mapseed always reproduces the same game,' and Rng.cs:3-4 deliberately hand-rolls xorshift64 because 'replay must survive runtime upgrades' â€” establishing cross-runtime determinism as an explicit goal. Floating-point transcendental noise from a third-party lib is not guaranteed bit-identical across CPU/JIT/library versions.
    IMPACT:   Live replay is protected because Recovery anchors on the snapshot, which serializes the frozen integer biome grid (Snapshot WriteGrid, determinism-audit.md), so the Perlin floats never re-run on the recovery path. But the genesis-from-seed path (cold start, pre-first-snapshot recovery, or any 'reproduce this map on another box from --mapseed') can diverge across machines, silently violating the reproducibility the comment advertises. It is a latent hazard, not a live divergence today.
    FIX:      Either restate the reproducibility guarantee as 'same map seed on the same build/runtime' and treat the snapshot grid as the source of truth, or replace SharpNoise with an integer/fixed-point noise generator owned in-repo (matching the Rng rationale). Worldgen is off the live replay path, so this is low-urgency but worth pinning before any 'regenerate from seed' tooling ships.
    VERIFY:   Factually true but the severity/framing is overstated. NoiseField.Generate (NoiseField.cs:13-39) does use SharpNoise.Modules.Perlin in doubles, and Rng.cs:3-5 does hand-roll xorshift64 to survive runtime upgrades, and ServerOptions.cs:4 does promise '--mapseed always reproduces the same game.' BUT: (1) the file header explicitly scopes this â€” 'Floats are fine here â€” generator-only code, off the replay path' (NoiseField.cs:2-3) â€” so it's a considered decision, not an oversight; (2) the live replay/recovery path is protected because the biome grid is frozen to integers and serialized in the snapshot (the finding concedes this), and Sim.Server regenerates from seed only on the same machine each cold start, which IS deterministic; (3) there is only one authoritative generation per world â€” no cross-machine consensus is required by the architecture; (4) 'transcendental noise' is a mischaracterization â€” Perlin is polynomial gradient/interpolation over an integer lattice with no sin/cos/pow, so it's far more likely bit-stable across conforming IEEE-754 platforms than the wording implies. The only real exposure is theoretical cross-machine / cross-SharpNoise-version cold-start divergence, which the finding itself calls 'a latent hazard, not a live divergence today.' That's a low-severity latent note, not a medium logic-hole contradicting the promise.

---------------------------------------------------------------------

##### X: Client Playability & Feel  [key=client-playability]
SUMMARY: The client has a genuinely clean, extensible command-mode architecture and a complete vertical slice of the ECONOMY: select/move, build (incl. 2-click docks), haul, assign workers/builders, breed, train, and boats are all wired end-to-end with toasts, info panels, and a food/famine HUD. But the entire CONFLICT half of the game is invisible and uncommandable: the server's PlayerView already computes per-unit Health, OngoingCombats, Factions, Relationships, PendingWars and IncomingProposals (Sim.Core/Vision/View.cs), yet ViewProjector and the wire DTOs drop every one of them, and no client mode issues the DeclareWar/Propose/Respond or Form/Move/DisbandGroup intents. The result is a polished logistics sandbox where you cannot see a battle, cannot tell a unit died from a unit that walked into fog, cannot see or receive a telegraphed war declaration (the linchpin of the game's "fair while asleep" promise), cannot command groups, and cannot reach the stated win condition. The highest-leverage work is bridging the already-computed combat/diplomacy state across the wire seam and adding the matching command modes.
STRENGTHS:
  + Clean, extensible command-mode architecture :: ICommandMode + CommandController + CommandContext make every intent a self-contained mode; adding one is a single Register call (GameClient.cs:159-165) with no change to the input core (CommandController.cs). This is exactly the seam the 'systematically wire each intent' plan needs, and it's why the economy slice is coherent.
  + Complete economy + boats vertical slice :: Move, Build (incl. the 2-click dock slip flow, BuildMode.cs:80-93), Haul (stateful sourceâ†’destâ†’resource machine), Assign/Unassign workers & builders, Breed, Train at a School, and full boat embark/disembark are all wired end-to-end with payload DTOs and IntentFactory methods (Intents.cs:110-230). Boats are a fully finished slice including passenger-count rendering (WorldRenderer.cs:147-166).
  + Honest fog and 'knowledge from presence' rendering :: Remembered-but-not-visible terrain is dimmed (WorldRenderer.cs:134), enemy units/structures are red-shifted and their activity is hidden (-1) per the design's no-activity-leak rule (ViewProjector.cs:159,169), and roads persist as terrain memory on explored tiles (ViewProjector.cs:120-129). The client faithfully reflects the server's fog contract.
  + Robust resolution-time notice surfacing :: Because validation happens after the submit ack, the client primes on first view to skip backlog and then toasts each new server notice exactly once by monotonic id (GameClient.cs:194-205) â€” a thoughtful solution to the fire-and-forget-rejection problem the async design creates.
  + Food/famine HUD with edge-detected alerts :: The Realm panel shows population, live castle food, per-period drain and runway, turns red in famine, and toasts on the famine rising/falling edge (Hud.cs:217-240; GameClient.cs:208-215) â€” the one economic pressure loop that IS surfaced is surfaced well, including a death countdown.
  + Smooth, legible rendering over a discrete sim :: SmoothDamp carries velocity across discrete tile hops so movement reads continuous (WorldRenderer.cs:259-275), stacked units fan out on a ring so each stays clickable (WorldRenderer.cs:113-119), boats float on the waterline, and own-unit role labels float overhead â€” the Â§2.5/Â§6.1 'smooth rendering is a client concern' promise is delivered cheaply.
FINDINGS (kept=11, refuted/dropped=0):

  [CRITICAL] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=critical) No diplomacy on the wire and no diplomacy UI â€” the telegraphed war declaration (the async-fairness linchpin) cannot be seen or sent
    EVIDENCE: Server registers DeclareWarIntent, ProposeRelationshipIntent, RespondToProposalIntent (Sim.Persistence/IntentJson.cs:45-47,78-80) and PlayerView exposes Factions, Relationships (with PendingEffectiveTick), PendingWars (LoId,HiId,EffectiveTick) and per-viewer IncomingProposals (View.cs:20-29,166-186). diplomacy-model.md:138-140 states 'Pending wars and incoming proposals are surfaced via PlayerView today.' Yet ViewDto/WirePlayerView have zero diplomacy fields (WireDtos.cs:24-50; Wire.cs:117-140), ViewProjector never reads them, the client IntentFactory has no DeclareWar/Propose/Respond methods (Intents.cs:110-230), and GameClient registers no diplomacy mode (GameClient.cs:159-165).
    IMPACT:   The design's entire answer to 'how is betrayal fair while I sleep' is Â§10.1/Â§12: war is unilateral but DELAYED and the target is NOTIFIED immediately ('effective in 6 hours'). With no diplomacy on the wire, the target receives no telegraph, cannot see relationship state, and cannot accept/decline an alliance â€” so combat (which only triggers between hostile factions per combat-model.md) can never be entered or anticipated through the client. The strategic stack the design is built around is entirely unreachable.
    FIX:      Project Factions/Relationships/PendingWars/IncomingProposals onto the wire (data already in PlayerView â€” not core-touching) and add a Diplomacy command mode + a standing 'incoming war / proposals' panel that toasts loudly on a new PendingWar with a live countdown to EffectiveTick. Add IntentFactory.DeclareWar/Propose/Respond.
    VERIFY:   Fully confirmed. PlayerView exposes Factions/Relationships/PendingWars/IncomingProposals (View.cs:42-55,164-186) and IntentJson registers DeclareWar/ProposeRelationship/RespondToProposal (IntentJson.cs:45-47,78-80). But WirePlayerView/ViewDto have ZERO diplomacy fields (Wire.cs:117-140; WireDtos.cs:24-50), ViewProjector never reads them (Sim.Server grep for Relationship|PendingWar|DeclareWar|Proposal = no matches), IntentFactory has no declare-war/propose/respond methods (Intents.cs ends at TrainUnit:225-229), and GameClient registers no diplomacy mode (GameClient.cs:159-165: only Move/Build/Haul/Assign/Breed/Boat/Train). Telegraphed war is the design's core async-fairness mechanism (design Â§10.1/Â§12), and the entire war/win stack is unreachable from the client. Server-readiness doesn't mitigate the player-facing gap. Critical stands.

  [HIGH] (logic-hole | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=critical) Combat is fully computed server-side but never crosses the wire â€” battles and deaths are invisible
    EVIDENCE: Sim.Core/Vision/View.cs:8 UnitView carries Health, and BuildPlayerView populates IReadOnlyList<CombatView> OngoingCombats (View.cs:14, 25, 189-194, 207) with (Tile, RoundNumber, NextRoundTick) for every contested tile in the viewer's vision. But Sim.Server/ViewProjector.cs never reads OngoingCombats, and ToUnitDto (ViewProjector.cs:151-185) drops Health â€” UnitDto/WireUnit have no Health field at all (Wire/WireDtos.cs:67-78; client Wire.cs:42-53). WorldRenderer.Apply culls any unit no longer in the view by Destroy()-ing its GameObject (WorldRenderer.cs:97-99) with no effect or notice. CombatRoundEvent removes dead units server-side (Combat/CombatRoundEvent.cs:107 OrderBy Health).
    IMPACT:   A player whose caravan or workers are being killed sees units silently blink out of existence one by one, indistinguishable from a unit walking into fog. There is no health bar, no 'battle here' marker, no damage feedback, no idea who is attacking or whether you are winning. This directly violates the design's core async-fairness principle (Â§9, combat-model.md: low-variance, observable, 'the wounded soldier crawls home') because the texture the model was built to deliver is never shown.
    FIX:      Add Health to UnitDto/WireUnit and an OngoingCombats array (tile, round, nextRoundTick) to ViewDto/WirePlayerView; map them in ViewProjector (the data is already in PlayerView, so this is NOT core-touching). Client: draw a health bar on units with Health < BaseHealth, a clash marker on combat tiles, and a death puff + optional toast when an own unit is culled while a combat existed on its tile.
    VERIFY:   Facts are airtight. UnitView carries Health (View.cs:8) and BuildPlayerView populates OngoingCombats (View.cs:189-194); but ViewProjector.ToUnitDto drops Health (ViewProjector.cs:151-185), UnitDto/WireUnit have no Health field (WireDtos.cs:67-78; client Wire.cs:42-53), and a Sim.Server grep for Health|CombatView|OngoingCombat returns ZERO matches, so neither ever crosses the wire. WorldRenderer.Apply Destroy()s culled units with no effect (WorldRenderer.cs:97-99). CombatRoundEvent removes dead via OnUnitDeath (CombatRoundEvent.cs:118). So combat is genuinely invisible. HOWEVER 'critical' overstates current player-facing impact: combat only fires between hostile owners (CombatRoundEvent.cs:50,71) and every pair starts Neutral (diplomacy-model.md:130-133) with no client way to declare war (see diplomacy finding), so a player CANNOT currently trigger any battle through the client. The invisible-combat gap is real and latent but downstream of the missing-diplomacy root, so it's high, not critical.

  [MEDIUM] (logic-hole | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=high) No self-contained playable build: the mock implements only Move, and the default transport needs a live server with a stale comment claiming otherwise
    EVIDENCE: MockGameServer.SubmitIntentJson handles only case "MoveIntent"; every other type returns accepted=false reason 'mock does not implement intent X yet' (MockGameServer.cs:81-99), and BuildView emits no holdings/food enrichment (MockGameServer.cs:195-213 â€” no capacity/workers/population). GameClient defaults UseMock=false (GameClient.cs:25) pointing at http://localhost:8080, but HttpGameServer's header comment says 'NOT used yetâ€¦ GameClient defaults to MockGameServer' (HttpGameServer.cs:10-13) and a failed GET only Debug.LogWarnings (HttpGameServer.cs:43-44).
    IMPACT:   If you press Play with defaults and no server is running, you get a blank world and a silent console warning with no on-screen explanation. If you flip to the mock to demo offline, every mode except Move just toasts 'Rejected: mock does not implementâ€¦', and the info/food panels are empty (population 0). There is no configuration in which a newcomer can experience the wired economy without standing up the C# server.
    FIX:      Either teach MockGameServer the economy intents + enrichment so it is a true offline demo, or add a visible 'Connectingâ€¦/Server unreachable' banner when GET fails, and fix the stale HttpGameServer comment so the default behavior is documented correctly.
    VERIFY:   All sub-claims verified: MockGameServer.SubmitIntentJson handles only 'MoveIntent', else returns 'mock does not implement intent X yet' (MockGameServer.cs:89-95); BuildView sets only playerId/visible/remembered/units/structures, leaving population/food/holdings at default 0 (MockGameServer.cs:205-213); GameClient.UseMock defaults false at localhost:8080 (GameClient.cs:25-26); HttpGameServer header comment is genuinely stale/contradictory ('NOT used yet... GameClient defaults to MockGameServer', HttpGameServer.cs:9-13); failed GET only Debug.LogWarning (HttpGameServer.cs:44); OnView early-returns on empty json so the world stays blank (GameClient.cs:132). The stale comment is a real defect. But 'high' overstates it: the client-server split is by design (the server IS the game), the mock self-describes as a minimal 'contract exercise' (MockGameServer.cs:11-14), and the client is built intent-by-intent (Intents.cs:107-109). It's a dev-onboarding/docs problem, not a gameplay logic hole. Medium.

  [MEDIUM] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) No box-select, select-all, or unit roster â€” commanding many citizens is one-click-at-a-time
    EVIDENCE: Selection is built only via single-unit clicks: SelectMoveMode toggles/selects one UnitId per click with Shift-to-add (SelectMoveMode.cs:30-34); Selection exposes only SelectOnly/AddUnit/ToggleUnit/ClearUnits (Selection.cs:26-51). CommandController.Raycast resolves exactly one unit under the cursor (CommandController.cs:96-129). There is no drag-rectangle, no 'select all my units', and no roster/overview panel.
    IMPACT:   This is a logistics game whose population grows via breeding/training, so the steady state is dozens of citizens. Having to shift-click each one individually to move a work crew or assemble an escort is the single biggest 'this doesn't feel like an RTS' friction, and it makes the group/escort plays the design wants impractical even before groups exist.
    FIX:      Add drag-box selection (and a 'select all idle workers' / roster list with click-to-focus). Low risk â€” purely client-side over the existing Selection set.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed. Selection exposes only SelectOnly/AddUnit/ToggleUnit/ClearUnits (Selection.cs:26-51) with no box-select or select-all; SelectMoveMode selects one UnitId per click with Shift-add (SelectMoveMode.cs:30-34); CommandController.Raycast resolves exactly one unit (CommandController.cs:96-129); HandleHotkeys only binds Esc + mode hotkeys, no select-all (CommandController.cs:84-94). No roster panel anywhere. For a population game whose steady state is dozens of citizens (breeding/training are wired), one-click-at-a-time selection is real RTS-feel friction. Medium is fair.

  [MEDIUM] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=high | sev0=medium) A game about time and distance shows no clock, no move/haul ETA, and ticks that can't be converted to real time
    EVIDENCE: ViewDto/WirePlayerView carry no current sim tick or seconds-per-tick â€” only FoodPeriodTicks/FoodRunwayTicks/StarvationInTicks as raw tick counts (WireDtos.cs:38-44; Wire.cs:131-140), surfaced verbatim as e.g. 'Runs dry in ~Nt' / 'Next death in Nt' (Hud.cs:226-231). No mode shows how long a move or haul will take; the HUD has no clock.
    IMPACT:   The design's whole constraint is that 'moves last hours' and players reason about time/distance (Â§5, Â§6). The client never tells the player how long anything takes or what time it is in the sim, and the only time numbers shown are in opaque 'ticks' with no tickâ†’hours conversion, so a returning offline player cannot reason about runway or arrival in human terms.
    FIX:      Add the current tick + a tickâ†’wall-clock scale to ViewDto, render a sim clock, and show a path-cost ETA preview when issuing a move/haul (server can return the committed path cost, which it already computes for A*).
    VERIFY:   Confirmed. WirePlayerView/ViewDto carry no current tick and no seconds-per-tick (Wire.cs:117-140; WireDtos.cs:24-50) â€” only raw tick counts (FoodPeriodTicks/FoodRunwayTicks/StarvationInTicks). GameHost has ticksPerSecond (GameHost.cs:18,32-39) but never sends it. HUD surfaces these verbatim as '~Nt' / 'Next death in Nt' (Hud.cs:226-231). No mode shows move/haul ETA; no clock. Client grep for secondsPerTick|currentTick = no matches. For a game whose central constraint is 'moves last hours' and reasoning about time/distance, showing only opaque ticks with no tick->hours conversion is a genuine gap. Medium confirmed.

  [MEDIUM] (missing-feature | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=high) Group intents exist server-side but movement is per-unit only â€” no caravans, escorts, or formations
    EVIDENCE: FormGroupIntent/MoveGroupIntent/DisbandGroupIntent are registered server-side (IntentJson.cs:42-44,75-77) but absent from the client IntentFactory (Intents.cs) and have no command mode. SelectMoveMode.OnLeftClick loops the selection and submits one separate MoveIntent per unit (SelectMoveMode.cs:40-44).
    IMPACT:   Sending N independent MoveIntents means selected units path independently and arrive at staggered times. Because combat pools all of an owner's units on a tile (combat-model.md force-vs-force), a scattered arrival means your escort trickles into a fight piecemeal instead of as one force â€” the opposite of the design's escorted-caravan intent (Â§7). It also makes commanding more than a couple of citizens tedious and removes 'send this group to P' (Â§2.1) as a first-class action.
    FIX:      Add a Group command mode (form from selection, move-group, disband) wired to the existing intents, and render a group as a labeled banner so the player can see and re-command it as one object.
    VERIFY:   Factually correct: FormGroup/MoveGroup/DisbandGroup are registered server-side (IntentJson.cs:42-44,75-77) but absent from IntentFactory (Intents.cs) with no command mode (GameClient.cs:159-165), and SelectMoveMode loops one MoveIntent per selected unit (SelectMoveMode.cs:40-44). But 'high' is overstated: the finding's strongest argument (escort trickling piecemeal into a fight, combat-model.md force-vs-force) is gated behind combat being reachable, which it isn't yet. For pure civilian logistics on geological time, N independent moves all arrive and the loop works (if tedious). The tedium overlaps heavily with the no-box-select finding. Real missing feature, medium.

  [MEDIUM] (missing-feature | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=high) Only intent REJECTIONS become notices â€” the design's event-tagged pushes (attacked, war declared, build complete) don't exist
    EVIDENCE: GameHost.HarvestRejections only creates a NoticeDto for IntentEvents whose Outcome.IsRejected (GameHost.cs:112-131); the comment confirms 'Only IntentEvents carry a PlayerId; consequence-event rejections aren't attributed.' WireNotice/SurfaceNotices on the client only toast these rejections (Wire.cs:109-115; GameClient.cs:194-205). Design Â§12: 'An event can notify a player (attack, build complete, war declared) â€” a push notification is just a side-effect hooked onto event resolution â€” tag events with notify player X.'
    IMPACT:   The whole point of the game is being played offline on 'geological time,' so the async notification channel is load-bearing. Today a returning player gets no alert that they were attacked, lost units, finished a building, or had war declared â€” only that one of THEIR OWN fire-and-forget intents was rejected. The positive/external-event half of Â§12 is unbuilt, leaving the offline experience blind.
    FIX:      Extend the server notice pipeline to tag consequence events (combat started on your tile, unit died, war now effective, construction finished) with the affected PlayerId, and surface them as a persistent notification log in the HUD (not just transient 4.5s toasts), since an offline player must see them on return.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed: HarvestRejections only emits NoticeDto for IntentEvents where Outcome.IsRejected (GameHost.cs:112-131), the comment confirms consequence/external events aren't attributed, and the client only toasts these rejections (GameClient.cs:194-205). Design Â§12 (line 481-482) does want notify-on-event for attack/build-complete/war-declared. But severity is overstated: diplomacy-model.md:138-144 EXPLICITLY defers notification infrastructure ('richer notification ... is a product-multiplayer concern, deferred') and notes the resolved-event log is sim-global with per-faction filtering as 'future work'. So this is a design-acknowledged staged gap, not an oversight. Real and matters for offline play, but medium given the explicit deferral.

  [MEDIUM] (logic-hole | verdict=partial | conf=high | sev0=high) The stated win condition (conquer every castle or force surrender) is unimplemented and uncommandable
    EVIDENCE: Design line 12: 'conquer every other player's castle or force them to surrender.' No surrender/victory/conquer code exists anywhere in src (grep for surrender|conquer|victory|defeat in src/*.cs returns nothing). combat-model.md:51 states 'Structures are NOT combatants. Combat is therefore civilians at BaseHealth=10/BasePower=1.
    IMPACT:   Through the client a player can never win or lose: castles can't be attacked, there is no surrender intent, and there are no military units distinct from workers. This caps the entire product at a logistics sandbox â€” there is no terminal state and no army to build toward it, so the 'war' framing has no payoff the client can deliver.
    FIX:      Core-touching: add siege/structure-as-combatant + castle capture (or a surrender intent) and at least one trainable combat role, then expose castle ownership/health and a win-progress readout in the client.     VERIFY:   Facts correct: no surrender/victory/conquer/defeat code (grep finds only resource 'capture economy' and a defensive 'lost-castle' comment in Population.cs:116), UnitRole stops at Boat=8 with no military role (Unit.cs:4-15), TrainMode offers only civilian roles (TrainMode.cs:16-20). BUT this is mislabeled as a 'logic-hole': combat-model.md:51-52 explicitly states 'Structures are NOT combatants. Sieges and capturing castles are a later combat extension' and FoodConsumption.cs:184 references 'a future capture mechanic'. It's an openly-staged roadmap milestone, not a contradiction or broken mechanic. The observation (no terminal state yet, civilians-only) is accurate and worth noting, but 'high logic-hole' overstates a planned, doc-acknowledged future feature. Medium.

  [LOW] (unnecessary | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=low) Two parallel environment renderers kept behind a runtime A/B flag
    EVIDENCE: GameClient keeps both the legacy ScatterRenderer and the newer WorldBuilder environment pipeline alive behind UseEnvironmentSystem (GameClient.cs:29,67-76,138-139), instantiating one or the other at runtime.
    IMPACT:   Carrying both rendering paths is maintenance drag: every view-apply site must branch, and the legacy path is effectively dead once the new pipeline is the default. It doesn't hurt feel but it's surface area that has to be kept compiling for no gameplay benefit.
    FIX:      Once the WorldBuilder pipeline is the accepted look, delete ScatterRenderer and the A/B flag (or move the comparison behind an editor-only build) to shrink the client's apply path.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed factually: GameClient keeps both ScatterRenderer and WorldBuilder behind UseEnvironmentSystem, instantiating one in Awake (GameClient.cs:29,67-76) and branching on every view-apply (GameClient.cs:138-139). Both paths must keep compiling. Minor nuance: this is an intentional transition A/B (new pipeline defaults on, legacy retained as fallback/comparison per the env-pipeline roadmap), so 'dead path' slightly overstates â€” it's not yet removed by choice. But it is real, unneeded maintenance surface with no gameplay benefit. Low confirmed.

  [LOW] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=low) Build placement is blind to cost and biome legality until after placing

  [LOW] (missing-feature | verdict=confirmed | conf=medium | sev0=low) Units vanish instantly on cull with no death/loss feedback
    EVIDENCE: WorldRenderer.Apply Destroy()s any unit GameObject not present in the latest view, with no effect or callback (WorldRenderer.cs:97-99). The same culling path fires for a unit that died in combat, starved, or simply walked out of vision â€” they are indistinguishable.
    IMPACT:   Losing a citizen (the costliest thing in a population game) produces zero feedback, and is visually identical to a unit fogging out. Players can't tell attrition from exploration, which compounds the invisible-combat problem.
    FIX:      Distinguish 'fogged out' (fade/leave a last-known ghost) from 'destroyed' (death puff + toast/notice), using a server-provided death event rather than inferring from absence.
    VERIFY:   Confirmed. WorldRenderer.Apply builds a 'seen' set and Destroy()s any unit GameObject not present in the latest view with no effect or callback (WorldRenderer.cs:97-99). The identical path fires for combat death, starvation, or simply fogging out â€” visually indistinguishable. Losing a citizen (the costliest asset in a population game) produces zero feedback. Correctly scoped as low; compounds the invisible-combat finding.
